The Requirement of a Written Receipt for Tasdiq in Zakat Payment to Another Collector
Discussion of whether a written release is required for the owner's claim of prior payment to another 'ashir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations regarding the requirement of a written document (khatt ibra') for the owner's tasdiq and explain the practical difference between them.

Core Idea
For the owner's claim of paying zakat to another collector, one Hanafi narration requires a written receipt; another does not — the difference hinges on the reliability of documents.

In this passage, al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether an owner must produce a written release when claiming he already paid zakat to another appointed collector. Two transmitted positions are examined, each with its own proof. Understanding this dispute clarifies when documentary evidence is needed in zakat collection and reveals how later scholars reconciled seemingly general statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific claim and the two positions
Recognise that the dispute is about the owner's claim of paying zakat to another 'ashir. State the two views: (1) from Imam Muhammad in Jami' al-Saghir: no document required; (2) from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad in al-Mabsut: document required.
Both narrations are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Examine the proof for each narration
For Jami' al-Saghir: documents can be forged, so a writing is not a reliable sign (tashabbuh al-kitaba). For al-Mabsut: the owner makes a claim and a sign exists (the other 'ashir's writing), so presenting it becomes wajib.
The proofs are based on the evidentiary value of written documents.
3
Note the practical problem of applying the requirement generally
If the condition of a document is applied to all forms of tasdiq, it would be impossible in three of the four scenarios (year not passed, debt, direct payment to poor). Only the scenario of payment to another 'ashir allows for a document.
This problem is identified by the commentator.
4
Understand the commentator's resolution
The commentator resolves by stating that the general wording ('in all forms') is used but a specific meaning is intended (amiri bi al-'amm wa al-irada al-khas). The requirement of a document applies only to the scenario where a document is possible: payment to another 'ashir.
This is a typical Hanafi interpretive move to reconcile conflicting texts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In the case of payment to another 'ashir, some Hanafi scholars require a written release for the owner to be believed by the current 'ashir, while others accept his statement without documentary evidence. This affects how a mufti advises a collector.
The text does not give a definitive tarjih, so the mufti must be aware of both positions.

کرنا شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور مبسوط میں اس کو شرط قرار دیا ہے یہی ایک روایت امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اسی تصدیقی تحریر کو اخراج البراۃ کے لفظ کے ساتھ تعبیر فرمایا ہے اور اسی کو خط ابراء کہتے ہیں روایت مبسوط کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صاحب مال نے ایک دعوی کیا ہے یعنی یہ دعوی کیا ہے کہ میں نے دوسرے عاشر کوز کو ۃ ادا کر دی ہے اور اس کے دعوی کی صداقت پر علامت بھی موجود ہے یعنی دوسرے عاشر کی تحریر تو اس پر تحریر کا ظاہر کرنا واجب ہو گا ۔ روایت جامع صغیر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک تحریر دوسری تحریر کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اس لئے تحریر کا علامت ہو نا معتبر نہ ہو گا یعنی جو تحریر صاحب مال نے عاشر آ خر کی طرف منسوب کی ہے معلوم نہیں وہ اسی کی ہے یا کسی اور کی ہم اس لئے کسی تحریر کو علامت کے طور پر پیش کرنا مفید اور کارآمد نہ ہوگا۔ مصنف بدايه كى عبارت ثُمَّ فِيْمَا يصدق فى السَّوَائِم واموال التجارة میں نظر ب نظر کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ سوائم اور اموال التجارت میں صاحب مال کے قول کی چار چار صورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ اس نے عاشر سے کہا کہ میری ملک میں جو مال ہے اس پر حولان حول نہیں ہوا۔ دوم یہ کہ اس نے کہا کہ میرے ذمہ قرضہ ہے سوم یہ کہ اس نے کہا کہ دوسرے عاشر کو جو اس سال میں پر تھا ز کوۃ ادا کر چکا چہارم یہ کہ میں بذات خود فقراء کو زکوۃ ادا کر چکا۔ سابق میں یہ بات بھی گذر چکی ہے کہ اموال التجارت میں چاروں صورتوں کے اندر صاحب مال کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے اور سوائم میں اول کی تین صورتوں میں تصدیق کی جاتی ہے اس تفصیل کے بعد مصنف ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اموال التجارت اور سوائم میں جن جن صورتوں میں صاحب مال کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے ان تمام صوتوں میں جامع صغیر کے مطابق اخراج براءت شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور مبسوط کے مطابق شرط ہے اس عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مبسوط کے بیان کی رو سے تمام صورتوں میں اخراج براوت یعنی تحریک ثبوت کا پیش کرنا ضروری ہے۔ حالانکہ ایک صورت کے علاوہ اخراج براوت ممکن ہی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ جب مالک نے یہ کہا کہ ابھی حولان حول نہیں ہوا یا میرے ذمہ قرضہ ہے یا میں فقراء کو دے چکا ہوں تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں کیا تحریر پیش کی جا سکتی ہے ہاں اگر اس نے یہ کہا کہ میں دوسرے عاشر کوز کو دے چکا ہوں تو اس صورت میں دوسرے عاشر کی دی ہوئی تحریر کا پیش کر ناممکن ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عبارت میں مجاز اعام بول کر خاص مراد لیا ہے یعنی بولا تو ایسا لفظ جو تمام صورتوں کو شامل ہے مگر مراد مذکورہ صورتوں میں سے ایک ہی صورت ہے۔
Then, regarding what is believed in grazing animals and trade goods... the summary of this expression is that if the owner says to the 'ashir (collector), 'I have paid the zakat wealth to another 'ashir who was in this year,' then for his being believed, an oath alone is sufficient, or it is necessary to show a documentary receipt from the other 'ashir. Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir that presenting such a document is not required for the owner to be believed. And in al-Mabsut it is made a condition; this is one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad. The author of al-Hidayah expressed this same documentary receipt with the word 'ikhraj al-bara'ah' and it is called 'khatt ibra'. The proof of the narration of al-Mabsut is that the owner made a claim, i.e., he claimed that he paid zakat to another 'ashir, and there is a sign of the truth of his claim, i.e., the writing of the other 'ashir, so presenting the writing becomes wajib. The proof of the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir is that one writing resembles another writing, so the writing's being a sign is not reliable; i.e., the writing that the owner attributes to the last 'ashir is not known whether it is actually his or someone else's, therefore presenting a writing as a sign is not beneficial or effective. The gist of the author of al-Bidayh's expression 'thumma fima yusaddaqu fi al-sawa'im wa amwal al-tijara' upon reflection is that it has already passed that for grazing animals and trade goods there are four forms of the owner's statement. One: he said to the 'ashir that the wealth in my possession has not had a full year pass. Two: he said that I have a debt upon me. Three: he said that I have paid zakat to another 'ashir who was in this year. Four: he said that I have myself paid zakat to the poor. It has also already passed that in trade goods, the owner's tasdiq is accepted in all four forms, and in grazing animals it is accepted in the first three forms. After this detail, the author of al-Hidayah says: in all the forms where the owner's tasdiq is accepted in trade goods and grazing animals, according to al-Jami' al-Saghir, 'ikhraj al-bara'ah' is not a condition, and according to al-Mabsut it is a condition. The meaning of this expression becomes: according to the statement of al-Mabsut, in all forms presenting 'ikhraj al-bara'ah' i.e., documentary proof is necessary. Yet in all but one form, 'ikhraj al-bara'ah' is not possible, because when the owner says that a year has not passed, or I have a debt, or I have given to the poor, what document can be presented in these three forms? Yes, if he said that I have given to another 'ashir, then in that case presenting a document from the other 'ashir is possible. The answer to this is that in the expression general wording is used but a specific meaning is intended, i.e., he used a word that includes all forms but the intended meaning is only one of the mentioned forms.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of a written document (khatt ibra' / ikhraj al-bara'ah) for the owner's claim to be believed when he says he paid zakat to another collector. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs for each narration. Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir says no document is required; the narration in al-Mabsut (attributed to Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad) says it is required. The author explains the reasoning: al-Mabsut argues that since the owner makes a claim and a sign (the document) exists, presenting it becomes wajib. Al-Jami' al-Saghir argues that documents can be forged, so a document is not a reliable sign. The passage then notes a practical problem: if the requirement is general, it would be impossible to produce a document in three of the four tasdiq scenarios (year not passed, debt, direct payment). The resolution is that the general wording is meant specifically for the case of payment to another 'ashir, where a document is possible. Thus, the condition of a document applies only to that one scenario. The passage also reviews the four types of claims and where tasdiq is accepted for sabeam and trade goods.

Key Terms
تصدیق (tasdiq): The acceptance of the owner's statement regarding zakat without requiring further proof in certain cases.
اخراج البراۃ / خط ابراء (ikhraj al-bara'ah / khatt ibra'): A written release or receipt from the previous zakat collector confirming that payment was made.
عاشر ('ashir): The zakat collector, often appointed by the imam to collect zakat from apparent wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Mabsut, what is required for the owner's claim that he paid zakat to another 'ashir to be believed?
A) An oath alone is sufficient.
B) A written release from the other 'ashir must be presented.
C) Two witnesses are required.
D) The owner's statement is never believed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two transmitted positions on requiring a written receipt for the owner's tasdiq; the practical difference arises when the owner claims payment to another collector.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Equality of Muslim and Dhimmi in Tasdiq for Zakat Claims
Rule: Dhimmi is believed in same tasdiq cases as Muslim, with one exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule of tasdiq for dhimmis in zakat, identify the single exception, and explain the qiyas proof that the doubled zakat follows the same conditions as the base.

Core Idea
A dhimmi is believed in zakat claims exactly like a Muslim—because the doubled zakat mirrors the conditions of the base.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key principle: a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim rule) is treated identically to a Muslim in matters of being believed (tasdiq) regarding zakat claims. The only case where neither is believed is when the claim is that zakat on grazing animals was paid directly to the poor within the city. The reasoning is based on qiyas: the doubled zakat is analogous to the base zakat, so the same conditions and rules apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule and Its Scope
The rule states: whatever cases the Muslim is believed in, the dhimmi is also believed. This applies to all claims regarding zakat conditions (passing of year, freedom from debt, payment to another collector, direct payment to the poor).
The exception is for one specific claim: direct payment of sawa'im zakat to the poor in the city.
2
Identify the Exception
The one exception is when the person claims to have personally paid the zakat on grazing animals (sawa'im) to the poor within the city. In that case, the statement is not believed, for both Muslim and dhimmi.
3
Understand the Proof Structure: Qiyas
The proof is qiyas: the doubled zakat taken from the dhimmi (far') is analogous to the base zakat taken from the Muslim (asl). The common illa (effective cause) is that the same conditions (year, debt, intention) must be observed for both amounts. Therefore, the rules of tasdiq, which are part of those conditions, apply equally.
The illa is jaliyyah (evident) and extracted via tahqiq al-manat.
4
List the Conditions That Apply
The conditions for zakat liability (passing of a year, freedom from debt, intention of trade for trade goods) apply to both the base and the doubled amount. Tasdiq rules are part of verifying these conditions.
This is why the same tasdiq cases are recognized.
5
Apply to Scenarios
For each possible claim (denial of year, denial of debt, payment to another 'ashir, direct payment to poor for sawa'im), determine if the dhimmi is believed. He is believed in all except the last.
This mirrors the Muslim's treatment exactly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَا صُدِّقَ فِيْهِ الْمُسْلِمُ صُدِّقَ فِيْهِ الذَّمِّيُّ لأَنَّ مَا يُوحَدُ مِنْهُ ضِعْفَ مَا يُوحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِ فَيُراعى تِلْكَ الشَّرَائِط تحقيقاً لِلتَّضْعِيف ترجمہ اور جن صورتوں میں مسلمان کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے ان صورتوں میں ذمی کی تصدیق بھی کیجائے گی اس لئے ڈمی سے جولیا جاتا ہے وہ اس کا دو چند ہے جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے پس دو چند کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ان شر انکا کا بھی لحاظ ہو گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مسلمان کے بجائے ذمی عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور اس نے جولان حول کا انکار کیا یا قرضہ سے فارغ ہونے کا انکار کیا یا دوسرے عاشر کو ادا کرنے کا دعوی کیا۔ یا بذات خود شہر کے اندر رفقراء کو ادا کرنے کا دعوی کیا تو جن جن صورتوں میں مسلمان کے قول کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے ان ان صورتوں میں ذمی کے قول کی تصدیق بھی کی جائے گی اور پہلے بیان ہو چکا ہے کہ صرف ایک صورت میں مسلمان کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں کی جاتی اور وہ یہ کہ جب اس نے کہا کہ میں سوائم کی زکوۃ شہر کے اندر فقر کو ادا کر چکا اس کے علاوہ باقی تمام صورتوں میں تصدیق کی جاتی ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اس ایک صورت کے علاوہ میں ذمی کے قول کی تصدیق کی جائے گی ۔ اور اس صورت میں نہیں کیجائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذمی سے اس کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے اور مختلف ( جس کو دو چند کیا گیا) میں وہ تمام شرطیں ملحوظ ہوتی ہے جو مصنف علیہ (جس پر دو چند کیا گیا) میں ملحوظ ہوتی ہیں پس جس طرح مضعف علیہ ( جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے ) پر سال کا گذر نا دین سے فراغت ہونا اور تجارت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے اسی طرح مضعف ( جو ڈمی سے لیا گیا ہے ہمیں بھی ان شرطوں کا محوظ رکھنا ضروری ہے۔
He said: And in those cases in which the Muslim is believed, in those cases the dhimmi is also believed, because what is taken from him is double what is taken from the Muslim. Therefore, those conditions are taken into account to effectuate the doubling. Translation: And in the cases where the Muslim is believed, the dhimmi will also be believed, because what is taken from the dhimmi is double what is taken from the Muslim. So to establish the doubling, those conditions will also be considered. Explanation of the issue: If, instead of a Muslim, a dhimmi passes by the 'ashir and he denies the passing of a year, or denies being free from debt, or claims payment to another 'ashir, or claims to have personally paid to the poor within the city - then in whatever cases the Muslim's statement is believed, in those cases the dhimmi's statement will also be believed. And it has already been stated that there is only one case in which the Muslim's statement is not believed, and that is when he says, 'I have paid the zakat of grazing animals to the poor within the city.' Apart from this, in all remaining cases, his statement is believed. So similarly, the dhimmi will be believed in all cases except this one, and will not be believed in this case. The proof is that double is taken from the dhimmi as is taken from the Muslim, and in the multiplied (that which is doubled) all those conditions are observed that are observed in the base (that upon which the doubling is made). So just as for the base (taken from the Muslim) the passing of a year, being free from debt, and intention of trade are conditions, similarly for the multiplied (taken from the dhimmi) it is also necessary to observe these conditions.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the matn of al-Hidayah. It establishes that a dhimmi is treated equally to a Muslim in matters of tasdiq (being believed regarding zakat claims). The exception is the same: when the claim is that he paid zakat on grazing animals directly to the poor within the city - in that case, neither is believed. The reason given is that the dhimmi pays double the zakat (due to higher rates), and the conditions for the doubled amount must mirror the conditions for the base amount. The proof is a qiyas: the doubled amount is analogous to the base, so the same conditions (yearly cycle, freedom from debt, intention of trade for trade goods) apply to the doubled zakat. Therefore, the rules of tasdiq, which are part of those conditions, also apply equally. The commentator elaborates by listing the four cases (denial of passing of year, denial of being free from debt, claim of payment to another 'ashir, claim of direct payment to poor) and specifying that only the last one (direct payment for sawa'im) is not believed.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Islamic rule with a covenant of protection, who pays jizya and subject to different zakat rates.
مضعف (muda'af): The doubled amount (the zakat taken from the dhimmi).
مضعف علیہ (muda'af 'alayh): The base amount (the zakat taken from a Muslim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case is a dhimmi's statement regarding zakat NOT believed?
A) When he denies the passing of a year.
B) When he claims to have paid zakat to another 'ashir.
C) When he claims to have personally paid the zakat of grazing animals to the poor within the city.
D) Dhimmis are always believed in all cases.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi is believed in all zakat claims exactly like a Muslim, except for the claim of direct payment of sawa'im zakat to the poor in the city.

intermediate
10 min
Believing the Dhimmi in Zakat Claims
Ruling on dhimmi credibility in zakat claims, with proof from tadh'if.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the scenarios in which a dhimmi's claim about zakat is accepted, and explain the legal reason based on the doubling principle.

Core Idea
A dhimmi is believed in the same zakat claims as a Muslim, except when personal payment of livestock zakat in the city is claimed.

This passage clarifies an important rule of zakat collection: the collector must accept the word of a dhimmi taxpayer in the same situations where a Muslim's word is accepted. The ruling connects to the broader Hanafi principle that the dhimmi pays double the rate of a Muslim on trade goods, so the same conditions must be verified to ensure the doubling is justified.

Guided Path
1
Recap the Four Scenarios
The owner may claim: (1) the year hasn't passed, (2) he has debt, (3) he paid another collector, (4) he paid the poor himself. Identify which scenarios apply to livestock vs. trade goods.
2
Distinguish Between Trade Goods and Livestock
In trade goods, all four claims are accepted. In livestock, only the first three are accepted. The fourth (personal payment in the city) is not accepted for livestock.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Disagreement on Evidence
Jami' al-Saghir says no evidence is required; Mabsut requires written proof in all cases. The author of Hidayah resolves this by interpreting 'general' wording as referring only to the case where payment to another collector is claimed, where evidence is possible.
4
State the Core Ruling
The dhimmi is believed in exactly the same scenarios as the Muslim. Only one exception: when a Muslim claims to have personally paid the zakat of livestock within the city, he is not believed, and likewise the dhimmi is not believed.
5
Analyze the Proof (Talil)
The proof is based on tadh'if: since the dhimmi pays double what a Muslim pays, the same conditions (passing of year, freedom from debt, trade intent) must be observed for the dhimmi to establish the doubling.

Source Text

ثُمَّ فِيْمَا يصدق فى السَّوَائِم واموال التجارة میں نظر ب نظر کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ سوائم اور اموال التجارت میں صاحب مال کے قول کی چار چار صورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ اس نے عاشر سے کہا کہ میری ملک میں جو مال ہے اس پر حولان حول نہیں ہوا۔ دوم یہ کہ اس نے کہا کہ میرے ذمہ قرضہ ہے سوم یہ کہ اس نے کہا کہ دوسرے عاشر کو جو اس سال میں پر تھا زکوۃ ادا کر چکا چہارم یہ کہ میں بذات خود فقراء کو زکوۃ ادا کر چکا۔ سابق میں یہ بات بھی گذر چکی ہے کہ اموال التجارت میں چاروں صورتوں کے اندر صاحب مال کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے اور سوائم میں اول کی تین صورتوں میں تصدیق کی جاتی ہے اس تفصیل کے بعد مصنف ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اموال التجارت اور سوائم میں جن جن صورتوں میں صاحب مال کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے ان تمام صورتوں میں جامع صغیر کے مطابق اخراج براءت شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور مبسوط کے مطابق شرط ہے اس عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مبسوط کے بیان کی رو سے تمام صورتوں میں اخراج براوت یعنی تحریک ثبوت کا پیش کرنا ضروری ہے۔ حالانکہ ایک صورت کے علاوہ اخراج براوت ممکن ہی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ جب مالک نے یہ کہا کہ ابھی حولان حول نہیں ہوا یا میرے ذمہ قرضہ ہے یا میں فقراء کو دے چکا ہوں تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں کیا تحریر پیش کی جا سکتی ہے ہاں اگر اس نے یہ کہا کہ میں دوسرے عاشر کوز کو دے چکا ہوں تو اس صورت میں دوسرے عاشر کی دی ہوئی تحریر کا پیش کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عبارت میں مجاز اعام بول کر خاص مراد لیا ہے یعنی بولا تو ایسا لفظ جو تمام صورتوں کو شامل ہے مگر مراد مذکورہ صورتوں میں سے ایک ہی صورت ہے۔
قَالَ وَمَا صُدِّقَ فِيْهِ الْمُسْلِمُ صُدِّقَ فِيْهِ الذَّمِّيُّ لأَنَّ مَا يُوحَدُ مِنْهُ ضِعْفَ مَا يُوحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِ فَيُرَاعى تِلْكَ الشَّرَائِط تحقيقاً لِلتَّضْعِيف
ترجمہ اور جن صورتوں میں مسلمان کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے ان صورتوں میں ذمی کی تصدیق بھی کیجائے گی اس لئے ذمی سے لیا جاتا ہے وہ اس کا دو چند ہے جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے پس دو چند کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ان شر انکا کا بھی لحاظ ہو گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مسلمان کے بجائے ذمی عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور اس نے جولان حول کا انکار کیا یا قرضہ سے فارغ ہونے کا انکار کیا یا دوسرے عاشر کو ادا کرنے کا دعوی کیا۔ یا بذات خود شہر کے اندر فقراء کو ادا کرنے کا دعوی کیا تو جن جن صورتوں میں مسلمان کے قول کی تصدیق کی جاتی ہے ان ان صورتوں میں ذمی کے قول کی تصدیق بھی کی جائے گی اور پہلے بیان ہو چکا ہے کہ صرف ایک صورت میں مسلمان کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں کی جاتی اور وہ یہ کہ جب اس نے کہا کہ میں سوائم کی زکوۃ شہر کے اندر فقر کو ادا کر چکا اس کے علاوہ باقی تمام صورتوں میں تصدیق کی جاتی ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اس ایک صورت کے علاوہ میں ذمی کے قول کی تصدیق کی جائے گی ۔ اور اس صورت میں نہیں کیجائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذمی سے اس کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے اور مختلف ( جس کو دو چند کیا گیا) میں وہ تمام شرطیں ملحوظ ہوتی ہے جو مصنف علیہ (جس پر دو چند کیا گیا) میں ملحوظ ہوتی ہیں پس جس طرح مضعف علیہ ( جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے ) پر سال کا گذر نا دینے سے فراغت ہونا اور تجارت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے اسی طرح مضعف ( جو ذمی سے لیا گیا ہے ) میں بھی ان شرطوں کا محوظ رکھنا ضروری ہے۔
Then, regarding what is believed in livestock and trade goods, the gist of the matter is that it has passed previously that in livestock and trade goods, there are four scenarios for the statement of the owner: first, he says to the collector that the wealth in my ownership has not had a year pass over it; second, he says that there is a debt upon me; third, he says that he has paid zakat to another collector in that year; fourth, that he himself has paid zakat to the poor. It has also passed previously that in trade goods, the owner is believed in all four scenarios, and in livestock, he is believed in the first three scenarios. After this detail, the author of Hidayah says that in all these scenarios where the owner is believed in trade goods and livestock, according to Jami' al-Saghir, producing evidence is not a condition, but according to Mabsut, it is a condition. The meaning of this statement is that according to Mabsut, in all cases producing evidence (written proof) is necessary, although in all but one case it is impossible, because when the owner says that a year has not passed, or there is a debt, or he has given to the poor, what written proof can be presented? Yes, if he says that he has paid to another collector, then presenting a document from that collector is possible. The answer is that in the expression, general is used but specific is intended, i.e., a word encompassing all cases is spoken but only one specific case is meant. He said (Arabic): And in whatever a Muslim is believed, a dhimmi is believed in it, because what is taken from him is double what is taken from a Muslim, so those conditions are observed to actualize the doubling. Translation: In the cases where a Muslim is believed, a dhimmi is also believed, because what is taken from a dhimmi is double what is taken from a Muslim. So to establish the doubling, those conditions will also be considered. Explanation of the issue: If a dhimmi passes by the collector instead of a Muslim, and he denies the passing of the year, or denies being free of debt, or claims to have paid to another collector, or claims to have paid the poor himself in the city, then in every case where a Muslim's word is believed, the dhimmi's word will also be believed. It has been stated before that only in one case is a Muslim not believed, and that is when he says that he has paid the zakat of livestock to the poor within the city. Apart from that, in all other cases he is believed. So similarly, except for this one case, the dhimmi's word will be believed, and in that case it will not be believed. The proof is that double is taken from the dhimmi compared to the Muslim, and in the multiplied (the one that is doubled) all the conditions are observed that are observed in the base (the one on which it is doubled). So just as passing of the year, freedom from debt, and intention of trade are conditions for the base (what is taken from a Muslim), so too these conditions must be observed in the multiplied (what is taken from a dhimmi).
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the credibility of a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state) regarding claims about zakat or ushr. The author first recaps four scenarios in which the owner of livestock or trade goods might claim exemption from zakat: (1) the year hasn't passed, (2) he has debt, (3) he paid another collector, (4) he paid the poor himself. For trade goods, all four are accepted; for livestock, only the first three. There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: according to Jami' al-Saghir, the owner need not produce evidence; Mabsut requires it. The author resolves this by interpreting 'evidence' in a general sense while meaning only one specific case. The core ruling is that a dhimmi is believed in the same scenarios as a Muslim, except for the case where a Muslim claims to have personally paid zakat of livestock within the city—in that case, he is not believed, and likewise the dhimmi is not believed. The reason given is that dhimmi pays double the tax (usually ushr), so the same conditions (yearly cycle, freedom from debt, trade intent) must be established to ensure the doubling is justified.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, who pays jizyah and is subject to ushr at double the rate of a Muslim on trade goods.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Accepting the claim of the taxpayer without requiring proof, in certain scenarios.
عشر (ushr): The tax (one-tenth or one-twentieth) levied on traders, also used interchangeably with zakat on trade goods.
تضعیف (tadh'if): Doubling; the principle that the dhimmi's tax rate is double that of a Muslim, which justifies applying the same conditions to both.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which scenario is a Muslim's word regarding zakat not accepted, and therefore a dhimmi's word is also not accepted?
A) When he claims the year has not passed on his trade goods.
B) When he claims to have paid the zakat of livestock to the poor within the city.
C) When he claims to have paid another collector for livestock.
D) When he claims to have a debt on his trade goods.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a dhimmi is believed in the same zakat-related claims as a Muslim, based on the principle of tadh'if (doubling), with the sole exception of claiming personal payment of livestock zakat within the city.

Zakat — Almsgiving

When a Harbi Trader Is Believed: Exception for Lineage and Umm Walad
Ruling that harbi trader is not believed in ushr claims except for umm walad and children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that a harbi trader is not believed in claims regarding goods liable for ushr, and identify the two exceptions for lineage and umm walad along with the legal reasoning (ta'lil).

Core Idea
A harbi trader is believed only in lineage claims because paternity removes property attribute, exempting from ushr.

When a harbi trader enters Dar al-Islam with goods, he must pay ushr as a protection fee. He is not believed in any excuse to avoid payment, such as claiming a year has not passed or that he has already paid. However, he is believed in two specific matters: if he claims that female slaves are his umm walad (mothers of his children) or that accompanying children are his offspring. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this exception and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the harbi trader's statement about his goods or accompanying persons. The general ruling: his statement is not believed regarding excuses for ushr. The exception: he is believed in claims of lineage (children) and umm walad.
The passage explicitly states: 'يُصَدِّقُ الْحَرْبِيُّ إِلَّا فِى الْجَوَارِى' – 'The harbi is believed except regarding female slaves' – meaning he is not believed in other claims.
2
Understand the basis of ushr
Ushr from a harbi is a fee for protection (himaya), not a religious zakat. It is due immediately upon granting aman, regardless of the passage of a year. This is the key rationale for why his excuses are rejected.
Passage says: 'لأنَّ الأخذَ مِنْهُ بِطَرِيقِ الْحِمَايَةِ' – 'because taking from him is by way of protection'.
3
Identify the general rule (not believed)
The harbi is not believed if he claims: (1) no year has passed, (2) he owes a debt, (3) he has paid another collector, or (4) he himself has given the ushr amount to the poor. These are rejected because they are irrelevant to the basis of ushr.
The text lists these four cases and explains each rejection.
4
Identify the two exceptions
Exception 1: Claiming a female slave is an umm walad (mother of his child). Exception 2: Claiming that children with him are his offspring. In these cases, his word is accepted and no ushr is taken on those individuals.
The passage says: 'غَيْرَ أَنَّ إِقْرَارَةَ بِنَسْبٍ مَنْ فِى يَدِهِ مِنْهُ صَحِيحٌ' – 'his acknowledgment of lineage is valid'.
5
Trace the reasoning (ta'lil)
The exception is based on two principles: (1) Acknowledgment of lineage is valid even from a non-Muslim. (2) Once paternity is established, the individual loses the attribute of being property (mal) and thus is not subject to ushr, which is only taken from wealth.
The text states: 'فَانْعَدَمَتْ صِفَةُ المَالِيةِ فِيهِنَّ' – 'so the quality of being wealth is negated from them'.

نہیں ہے ۔
The harbi will be believed regarding female slaves if he says they are his umm walad, or regarding boys with him if he says they are his children. (Arabic): The harbi is believed except regarding female slaves if he says they are mothers of his children, or boys with him if he says they are his children, because taking from him is by way of protection, and what wealth is in his hand needs protection. However, his acknowledgment of the lineage of a person in his possession is valid, and similarly the acknowledgment of umm walad status, because umm walad is based on that (childbirth). So the quality of being wealth is removed from them, and the (tax) is not obligatory except from wealth. Translation: The harbi trader will not be believed except regarding female slaves when he says they are mothers of his children, or regarding boys with him when he says they are his children, because taking ushr from a harbi is for protection, and whatever wealth is in his possession is in need of protection. But his acknowledgment of lineage of a person in his possession is valid, and similarly the acknowledgment of being umm walad, because umm walad is based on that (childbirth). So the quality of being wealth is negated from them, and ushr is not obligatory except from wealth. Explanation of the issue: If a harbi trader enters our land (Dar al-Islam) with goods for trade, then passes by the collector with the goods, and says any of the mentioned statements – e.g., that a year has not passed, or that he owes a debt, or that he has paid ushr to another collector, or that he himself has given the ushr amount to the poor – then in none of these cases will he be believed; rather, the collector will take ushr from him. Yes, if he has female slaves with him and he says they are his children, or boys, then in these two cases his word will be believed, and ushr will not be taken from those slaves or boys. The proof for taking ushr from a harbi trader is that ushr is taken from him because the ruler of Dar al-Islam protects his wealth. And whatever wealth he possesses is in need of protection. So when the Muslims protect his wealth, the right of protection (ushr) must be taken. He is not believed in the four mentioned cases because there is no benefit in believing him. Because if he says the year has not passed, it will be said that the passing of a year is not a condition for making ushr obligatory on a harbi; rather, ushr becomes obligatory due to protection. And the harbi obtains protection from the mere grant of aman. So after granting aman, ushr becomes obligatory whether the year passes or not. And if he says he owes a debt, he will not be believed, because a debt incurred in Dar al-Harb cannot be claimed in Dar al-Islam. If the harbi says he has paid another collector, his statement will be disregarded because what is taken from him is the fee for protection, and protection is obtained through the aman itself. And if he says he himself has given to the poor, he will not be believed because his belief is against his own words? The author of Hidayah says: whoever is in the possession of a harbi, his acknowledgment of lineage from him is valid, i.e., saying 'he is my son or daughter' or 'they are the mothers of my children' – we will accept this acknowledgment, because his being a harbi does not contradict having offspring and lineage.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage deals with the credibility of a harbi (enemy trader) who enters Dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman) for trade. The ushr (customs duty) is imposed on him as a fee for protection. The ruling states that a harbi is not believed in any of the standard excuses (no year passed, debt, paid another collector, paid the poor) because the basis of the tax is protection, not a yearly cycle or debt status. However, he is believed in two specific matters: (1) if he claims that a female slave is his umm walad (mother of his child), and (2) if he claims that children accompanying him are his offspring. The reason is that acknowledgment of lineage is valid even from a non-Muslim, as lineage is not related to the tax. Once he acknowledges paternity, the slaves or children cease to be considered 'wealth' subject to ushr, because property claims on free persons are invalid. The passage thus establishes a clear exception to the general rule that a harbi's statements about his goods are not accepted.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim from hostile territory who enters Dar al-Islam with aman for trade.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; upon the master's death, she becomes free.
عشر (ushr): A tax (one-tenth) levied on the goods of harbi traders as a fee for protection by the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a harbi trader not believed when he claims that a year has not passed on his goods?
A) Because the year condition does not apply to harbi traders
B) Because he is a disbeliever and thus not trustworthy
C) Because he must pay ushr immediately upon protection, regardless of the year
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
A harbi trader is believed in claims of lineage and umm walad because these affect property status, but not in other claims that would reduce the protection fee (ushr).

Tasdiq of Harbi: Exemption for Umm Walad and Children
Ruling with rational proof (qiyas) regarding exception to Harbi's credibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding a Harbi trader's claim of umm walad or children and explain the rationale based on 'ushr as compensation for property protection.

Core Idea
A Harbi's claim of lineage or umm walad is accepted because it removes property status; 'ushr is only on property.

This passage from al-Hidayah discusses an exception to the general rule that a Harbi trader is not believed in claims that reduce his 'ushr liability. When it comes to his female slaves (claiming they are umm walad) or boys (claiming they are his children), his word is accepted. We will explore the legal reasoning and its basis in the nature of 'ushr as a compensation for protection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Understand that a Harbi is generally not credited in claims that reduce 'ushr liability (e.g., year not passed, debt, prior payment).
This establishes the default presumption.
2
Identify the exception
Note the two specific cases: claiming female slaves as umm walad or boys as his children. Also, note that the text says the Harbi is 'credited except' in these matters, meaning the exception is only for these claims.
These are the only exceptions acknowledged by the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the rationale (illa)
The 'ushr is wajib as compensation for the protection of property. When the Harbi claims lineage or umm walad status, the attribute of being property (maliyyah) is removed from those individuals. 'Ushr is only taken from property, so they become exempt.
This is a qiyasi reasoning: the illa of protection applies only to property-like assets.
4
Contrast with other claims
Other claims (e.g., year not passed, debt) do not negate the property attribute; they only attempt to reduce liability on property. Hence they are not credited.
The distinction hinges on whether the claim pertains to the nature of the asset as property or to incidental conditions.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور حربی تاجر کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی مگر باندیوں میں درانحالیکہ وہ کہتا ہے کہ یہ میری اولاد کی مائیں ہیں یا ایسے لڑکوں میں جو اس کے ساتھ ہیں درانحالیکہ وہ کہتا ہے کہ یہ میری اولاد ہیں کیونکہ حربی سے عشر لینا تمایت و حفاظت کی مجہ ہے اور جو کچھ مال اس کے قبضہ میں ہے وہ حمایت و حفاظت کا محتاج ہے۔ مگر جو آدمی اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اس کے نسب کا اقرار اس کی طرف سے صحیح ہے پس یوں ہی ام ولد ہونے کا اقرار ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد ہونا تو ولد ہونے پر مبنی ہے پس باندیوں میں مال ہونے کی صفت معدوم ہوگئی۔ اور عشر لینا واجب نہیں

اولاد کی مائیں ہیں تو ہم اس اقرار کو مان لیں گے کیونکہ اس کا حرفی ہونا استیلا د اور نسب کے منافی نہیں ہے ۔ اس لئے کہ استیلا دو نسب جس طرح دار الاسلام میں ثابت ہوتا ہے اسی طرح دار الحرب میں بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے پس جب باندیوں کے بارے میں ام ولد ہونے کا اقرار اور لڑکوں کے بارے میں اولاد ہونے کا اقرار بیج ہے تو ان میں عشر وغیرہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ام ولد اور اولاد میں مال ہونے کی صفت معدوم ہو گئی ہے۔ اور عشر مال میں سے لیا جاتا ہے نہ کہ غیر مال سے اس لئے ان میں عشر نہ لیا جائے گا۔
The Harbi is credited except regarding female slaves if he says they are mothers of his children, or boys with him if he says they are his children, because the taking from him is by way of protection, and the wealth in his hand needs protection. However, his affirmation of lineage of one in his hand from him is valid, so likewise the affirmation of being an umm al-walad, because it is based on it. So the attribute of being property ceases in them, and the tithe is not obligatory except from property.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with rational proof regarding the credibility (tasdiq) of a Harbi trader's claims when passing the 'ushr collector. The general rule is that a Harbi is not believed in claims that would reduce or exempt his trade goods from 'ushr, such as claiming the year has not passed, that he owes debt, that he already paid 'ushr, or that he distributed it to the poor. However, there are two exceptions recognized by the Hanafi school: if the Harbi claims that his female slaves are ummahat awlad (mothers of his children) or that the boys accompanying him are his children. In these two cases, his statement is accepted, and no 'ushr is taken from those persons. The reason is that the rationale (illa) for taking 'ushr from a Harbi is the protection (himaya) granted by the Islamic state to his property. But the claim of lineage (nasab) or umm al-walad status pertains to personal status, not property. Since lineage is established in dar al-harb as it is in dar al-Islam, the Harbi's acknowledgment of his own child is valid, and once a child is acknowledged, the attribute of being property (maliyyah) ceases for the slave mother (umm walad) because she becomes free upon the father's death, and for the child, he is free. 'Ushr is only taken from property, and these persons are not property. Thus they are exempt.

Key Terms
حربی (harbī): A non-Muslim from a hostile territory (dar al-harb) who enters dar al-Islam with aman (safe passage) for trade.
تصدیق (taṣdīq): Crediting the Harbi's claim without requiring proof.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon her master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept a Harbi's claim that his female slave is an umm walad for exemption from 'ushr?
A) Because all claims of Harbi are accepted.
B) Because umm walad status removes the property attribute, and 'ushr is only on property.
C) Because the Quran directly exempts umm walad from tax.
D) Because the Harbi is under oath.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a Harbi trader's claim that his slaves are his children or their mothers is credited for exemption from 'ushr because these are personal status matters that negate the property attribute, and 'ushr is only taken from property.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Rates of 'Ushr for Muslim, Dhimmi, and Harbi
Determination of 'ushr rates based on protection needs and reciprocity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rates of 'ushr for Muslim, dhimmi, and harbi traders, explain the Hanafi rationale for each rate, and identify the relied-upon position for taking from small amounts.

Core Idea
The 'ushr rate reflects protection need: Muslim 2.5%, dhimmi 5%, harbi 10% — small amounts always excused.

This lesson examines the graded system of 'ushr (trade tax) for traders passing through the Islamic state. You will learn the specific rates for Muslims, dhimmis, and harbis, the reasoning behind each rate, and how the Hanafi school resolves a difference of opinion regarding small amounts of harbi property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories and their rates
Locate the three categories (Muslim, dhimmi, harbi) and their respective rates: rub'u 'ushr (1/40 = 2.5%), nisfu 'ushr (1/20 = 5%), and 'ushr (1/10 = 10%).
These rates are fixed in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the rationale for each rate
Muslim: pure zakat (fard). Dhimmi: double zakat because greater need for state protection. Harbi: not zakat but a protection fee based on reciprocity (mujazah).
The dhimmi rate is analogized to the Banu Taghlib case.
3
Note the nisab requirement for Muslim and dhimmi
For Muslim and dhimmi, the standard nisab (200 dirhams) is required because what is taken is zakat or its double.
No nisab is required for harbi in the same way; instead, the threshold is 50 dirhams or 'little property'.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on small harbi amounts
In al-Jami' al-Saghir: nothing taken if less than 50 dirhams unless the hostile state takes from small amounts. In Kitab al-Zakah: nothing taken regardless of reciprocity because small amounts are always excused.
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) presents both but favors Kitab al-Zakah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is from Kitab al-Zakah: small amounts (less than 50 dirhams) are always exempt, even if the hostile state takes from small amounts.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسلمان سے ربع عشر ذمی سے نصف عشر اور حربی سے عشر لیا جائے گا
قَالَ وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِ رُبْعُ عُشْرِ وَمِنَ الذِّمِّي نِصْفُ الْعُشْرِ وَ مِنَ الْحَرْبِي الْعُشْرُ هَكَذَا أَمَرَ عُمَرَ سَعَاتَهُ وَإِنْ ى بِخَمْسِينَ دِرْهَما لَمْ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ شَيْ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونُوا يَأْخُذُونَ مِنَّا مِنْ مِثْلِهَا لأَنَّ الأَخذَ مِنْهُم بِطَرِيقِ الْمُجَازَاةِ بِخِلافِ الْمُسْلِمِ وَالدّمِّى لِأَنَّ الْمَاحُوذَ زَكوةُ أَوْ ضِعْفَهَا فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ النِّصَابِ وَهُذَا فِى الْجَامِع الصَّغِيرِ وَ فِي كِتَابِ الزَّكوة لَا تَأخُذُ مِنَ الْقَلِيلِ وَإِنْ كَانُوا يَا حُدُونَ مِنَّا مِنْه لأنَّ الْقَلِيلَ لَمْ يَزَلْ عَفُوا وَلِأَنَّهُ لا يحتاج إلى الحِمَايَة
ترجمہ کہا کہ مسلمان تاجر سے چالیسواں حصہ لیا جائے گا اور ذمی سے بیسواں اور حربی تاجر سے دسواں حصہ لیا جائے گا۔ ایسا ہی حضرت عمر نے اپنے سائی حضرات کو حکم فرمایا تھا اور اگر حربی پچاس درہم کے ساتھ گذرا تو اس سے کچھ نہ لیا جائے گا مگر یہ کہ اس قلیل مال سے وہ ہم سے لیتے ہوں کیونکہ ” بیوں سے لینا بطور بدلہ کے ہے۔ برخلاف مسلمان اور ذمی کے کہ جولیا جاتا ہے وہ زکوۃ ہے یا ز کوۃ کا دو چند ہے اس لئے نصاب کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور یہ جامع صغیر میں ہے اور کتاب الز کو میں ہے کہ عربی کے قلیل مال سے کچھ مت لوا اگر چہ
حر بی لوگ ہم سے ایسے مال نے لے لیتے ہیں کیونکہ قلیل مال ہمیشہ عفور ہا ہے اور اس لئے کہ قلیل مال حفاظت کا محتاج بھی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا کہ مسلمان تاجر سے اس کے مال کا چالیسواں حصہ لیا جائے گا اور ذمی تاجہ سے اس کے مال کا بیسواں حصہ اور حربی تاجر سے دسواں حصہ لیا جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے زکوۃ وصول کرنے والے عاملوں اور عاشروں کو اسی کا حکم فرمایا تھا چنانچہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا ارشاد ہے خُذُوا مِنَ المُسلِم رُبعَ الْعَشْرِ وَمِنَ الدِّمِّي نِصْفَ الْعَشْرِ وَمِنَ الْحَرْبِي الْعَشْر “ حضرت عمر کا یہ فیصلہ چونکہ صحابہ کی موجودگی میںتھا اور صحابہ میں سے کسی نے کوئی اختلاف بھی نہیں کیا، اس لئے یہ اجتماع ہو گیا۔ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلمان سے چالیسواں حصہ لے لیا جاتا ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے مَا تُوْا رُبعَ عُشْرِ اَمْوَالِكُمْ مِنْ كُلِّ اَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمًا دِرْهَم . یعنی تم اپنے مال کا چالیسواں حصہ دو ہر چالیس درہم سے ایک درہم اور عاشر کے لئے زکوۃ لینے کی ولادیت اس لئے ہے کہ مسلمان حمایت و حفاظت کا محتاج ہے اور ذمی بہ نسبت مسلمان کے حمایت کا زیادہ محتاج ہے۔ کیونکہ چور ڈمی کا مال لوٹنے کی زیادہ طمع کرتے ہیں پس جب دمی اپنے مال کی حفاظت میں زیادہ محتاج ہے تو اس سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے جیسا کہ بنو تغلب سے مسلمانوں کی زکوۃ کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے اور حربی بہ نسبت ذمی کے ایسا ہے جیسا کہ ذمی بہ نسبت مسلمان کے چنا نچہ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیں کہ حربیوں کی شہادت ذمیوں کے خلاف قبول نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ ذمیوں کی شہادت مسلمانوں کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جاتی اور ذمیوں کی شہادت جر بیوں کے خلاف اور موافق قبول کی جاتی ہے جیسا کہ مسلمانوں کی شہادت ذمی کے خلاف اور موافق قبول کی جاتی ہے پس جس
From the Muslim is taken one-fourth of a tenth, from the dhimmi half of a tenth, and from the harbi a tenth. Thus Umar commanded his officials. And if he (the harbi) passes with fifty dirhams, nothing is taken from him unless they take from us the like of it, because taking from them is by way of reciprocity, contrary to the Muslim and dhimmi, because what is taken is zakat or double of it, so nisab is necessary. And this is in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and in Kitab al-Zakah: Do not take from a little (property), even if they take from us from it, because little property has always been excused and because it does not need protection.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage establishes the rates of 'ushr (trade tax) for three categories of traders passing through the Islamic state's customs. The matn states: from the Muslim trader, one-fourth of a tenth (i.e., 2.5% = 1/40) is taken; from the dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state), half of a tenth (i.e., 5% = 1/20); and from the harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory with aman), a full tenth (10% = 1/10). This ruling is traced to Caliph Umar's instruction to his officials, which was accepted by the Companions without dissent, effectively forming an ijma' (consensus). The Sharh explains the rationale: The Muslim pays zakat on his trade goods at the rate of 2.5% as prescribed by the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) in the hadith 'Pay one-fourth of a tenth of your wealth; for every forty dirhams, one dirham.' The dhimmi pays double that (5%) because he is in greater need of protection from the state, as thieves are more eager to rob dhimmis. This is analogous to the case of Banu Taghlib, who were required to pay double the Muslim zakat. The harbi pays the highest rate (10%) because the amount taken from him is not zakat but a fee for protection (himaya) and also operates on the principle of reciprocity (mujazat): if his state takes a similar tax from Muslim traders, we take the same. The passage also addresses nisab (minimum threshold): For Muslim and dhimmi, nisab is required because it is zakat or its double. For the harbi, if he passes with less than fifty dirhams, nothing is taken, unless the hostile state takes from Muslims even small amounts. This exception is from al-Jami' al-Saghir, but the preferred view in Kitab al-Zakah is that nothing is taken from a small amount regardless, because small amounts have always been excused and do not require significant protection. This last point reflects an intra-Hanafi difference: in the Jami' al-Saghir, reciprocity is considered, but in the later Kitab al-Zakah, the exemption of small amounts is absolute.

Key Terms
ربع عشر (rub'u 'ushr): One-fourth of a tenth, i.e., 2.5% (1/40) – the zakat rate for Muslim traders.
نصف عشر (nisfu 'ushr): Half of a tenth, i.e., 5% (1/20) – the rate for dhimmi traders as double zakat.
مجازاة (mujāzāh): Reciprocity – taking from harbi traders an amount equal to what their state takes from Muslim traders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Kitab al-Zakah), what is the ruling on taking 'ushr from a harbi trader with goods worth 30 dirhams?
A) Take 3 dirhams (10%) because he is a harbi.
B) Take nothing because it is less than nisab and small amounts are always exempt.
C) Take only if the harbi's state takes from small amounts of Muslim traders.
D) Take 1.5 dirhams (5%) because it is half the rate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi 'ushr system grades tax rates based on protection need and reciprocity, but small amounts are always excused in the relied-upon view.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
12 min
Rates of 'Ushr for Muslim, Dhimmi, and Harbi Merchants
Establishes the fractions for 'ushr and their justifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rates of 'ushr (1/40, 1/20, 1/10) for Muslim, dhimmi, and harbi merchants, and explain the justifications of zakat obligation, need for protection, and reciprocity as per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The rate of 'ushr increases with the trader's need for protection and is modified by reciprocity for harbis.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the rates of 'ushr—a levy on merchandise of traders entering Muslim territory. Drawing from the practice of 'Umar and rational analogies, the school distinguishes three categories: Muslim (1/40), dhimmi (1/20), and harbi (1/10). The justifications blend zakat rulings, protective service, and reciprocal treatment, leading to nuanced exceptions for small amounts and unknown rates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rates
State the fractions: Muslim pays 1/40 (rub' al-'ushr), dhimmi pays 1/20 (nisf al-'ushr), harbi pays 1/10 (al-'ushr). These are derived from the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.
The Arabic terms are literal: 'ushr = tenth, rub' = quarter, nisf = half.
2
Examine the primary proof
The proof is the command of 'Umar to his collectors, which was not contested by the Companions, forming an ijma sukuti (tacit consensus). Also, the Prophet's hadith on zakat supports the rate for Muslims.
The imperative 'khudhu' indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the rational justification
The justification differs by category: Muslim pays zakat (1/40) because he needs protection; dhimmi pays double (1/20) because he needs more protection; harbi pays double of dhimmi (1/10) primarily due to reciprocity (mu'awadah) but also protection.
The analogy: harbi is to dhimmi as dhimmi is to Muslim in terms of protection need.
4
Understand the exception for small amounts
For a harbi with 50 dirhams or less, nothing is taken unless the enemy state takes such small amounts from our traders. The preferred view (in al-Mabsut) is that small amounts are always exempt ('afw).
This resolves an apparent contradiction between taking for reciprocity and overlooking small amounts.
5
Handle the scenario of unknown reciprocal rate
If a harbi passes with 200 dirhams and the enemy's rate is unknown, take 1/10 (default). If known, take that rate. If they take nothing, we take nothing to encourage good conduct; if they take everything, we take only 1/10 to avoid treachery.
This follows 'Umar's instruction: 'If it perplexes you, then take one-tenth.'

سے لیا جاتا ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی حربی پچاس درہم کے ساتھ عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا تو اس سے کچھ نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ ہاں اگر وہ اس قدر قلیل مقدار سے ہمارے لوگوں سے لیتے ہیں تو پھر ہم بھی لیں گے کیونکہ حربیوں سے لینا بطریق مجازات ہے جو معاملہ وہ ہمارے ساتھ کریں گے وہی ہم بھی ان کے ساتھ کریں گے حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا فرمان بھی اسی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے کیونکہ فاروق اعظم رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے جب عاشروں کو مقرر کیا تو آپ سے دریافت کیا گیا کہ کم ناخذ مما مر به الحربی یعنی ہم لوگ حربی کے مال سے کس قدر وصول کریں تو آپ نے پوچھا کہ کم يأخذون منا ؟ وہ ہم سے کتنا لیتے ہیں؟ لوگوں نے کہا کہ عشر لیتے ہیں آپ نے فرمایا خذوا منهم العشر تم بھی ان سے عشر وصول کرو اس جگہ ایک سوال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ مصنف کی عبارت میں منافات ہے کیونکہ یہ پہلے کہا گیا ہے کہ ذمیوں اور حربیوں سے عشر لینا بطریق حمایت ہے اور یہاں کہا گیا ہے کہ حربیوں سے لینا بطریق مجازات ہے۔ جواب: حربیوں سے مطلقاً لینا تو حمایت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مقدار معین یعنی دسواں حصہ لینا مجازات اور بدلے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اب اس صورت میں منافات کا اعتراض واقع نہ ہوگا۔
اس کے برخلاف مسلمان اور ذمی کہ ان سے جو لیا جاتا ہے وہ زکوۃ ہے۔ یا زکوۃ کا دو چند ہے یعنی مسلمان سے زکوۃ لی جاتی ہے اور دمی سے زکوۃ مسلم کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے پس چونکہ ان سے زکوۃ یا زکوۃ کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے اس لئے نصاب کا ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ اس نصاب سے زکوۃ یا زکوۃ کا دو چند لیا جائے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مال قلیل سے بدلے کے طور پر لینا جائز ہے یہ جامع صغیر میں ہے۔ اور مبسوط کے کتاب الزکوۃ میں ہے کہ عربی کے قلیل مال سے عاشر کچھ نہ لے۔ اگر چہ حربی لوگ ہم سے ایسے مال سے لے لیتے ہیں کیونکہ قلیل مال ہمیشہ عفور ہے اب اگر اس میں سے عشر لیا گیا تو ی ظلم ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قلیل مال حفاظت کا محتاج بھی نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ عاشر حفاظت ہی کی وجہ سے لینے کا مستحق ہے۔
قَالَ وَإِنْ مَرَّ حَرْبِيٌّ بِمِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ وَلَا يُعْلَمُ كَمْ يَأْخُذُونَ مِنَّا يَأْخُذُ مِنْهُ الْعُشْرُ لِقَوْلِ عُمَرَ فَإِنْ أَعْيَاكُمْ فَالْعُشْرُ وَإِنْ أَنَّهُمْ يَأْخُذُونَ مِنَّا رُبْعَ عُشْرٍ أَو نِصْفَ عُشْرٍ يَأْخُذُ بِقَدْرِهِ وَإِنْ كَانُوا يَأْخُذُونَ الْكُلَّ لَا يَأْخُذُ الْكُلَّ لأَنَّهُ غَدْرٌ وَإِنْ كَانُوا لَا يَأْخُذُونَ اصْلاً لَا يَأْخُذُ لِيَتْرُكُوا الْأَخْذَ مِنْ تُجَّارِنَا وَلِأَنَّا أَحَقُّ بِمَكَارِمِ الْأَخْلَاقِ
ترجمہ اور اگر حربی دو سو درہم کے ساتھ گذرا اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ وہ لوگ ہم سے کس قدر لیتے ہیں تو عاشر اس سے عشر لے لے۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر تم کو تھکا دے تو عشر لے لو۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم ہے کہ حربی لوگ ہم سے چالیسواں حصہ یا بیسواں حصہ لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عاشر بھی اسی قدر لے اور اگر معلوم ہو کہ حربی لوگ ہم سے کل مال لے لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عاشر کل مال نہ لے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو بد عہدی ہے۔ اور اگر حربی لوگ ہم سے کچھ نہ لیتے ہوں تو ہمارا عاشر بھی کچھ نہ لے گا تا کہ ہمارے تاجروں سے بھی لینا چھوڑ دیں اور اس لئے کہ ہم اخلاق میں زیادہ مستحق ہیں۔
Book of Zakah. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidaya, Volume 3. [Introductory lines about istila and lineage omitted as they are from previous context]. The Muslim trader is charged one-quarter of a tenth (1/40), the dhimmi one-half of a tenth (1/20), and the harbi one-tenth (1/10). He said: One-tenth of a tenth is taken from the Muslim, half of a tenth from the dhimmi, and a full tenth from the harbi. Thus did 'Umar command his collectors. And if he (a harbi) passes with fifty dirhams, nothing is taken from him unless they (the harbis) take from us something similar, because taking from them is by way of reciprocity, unlike the Muslim and dhimmi, since what is taken is zakat or its double, so a nisab is necessary. This is in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And in Kitab al-Zakah: Do not take from a small amount even if they take from us such, because a small amount has always been overlooked and because it does not need protection. Commentary: The text states that from a Muslim merchant one-quarter of a tenth (1/40) is taken, from a dhimmi one-half of a tenth (1/20), and from a harbi merchant one-tenth (1/10). Thus did 'Umar command his collectors. And if a harbi passes with fifty dirhams, nothing is taken from him unless they take from us a similar small amount, because taking from them is by way of reciprocity. Contrary to the Muslim and dhimmi, for what is taken is zakat or its double, so nisab is necessary. This is in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And in Kitab al-Zakah: Do not take from a small amount even if they take from us such, because a small amount has always been overlooked and because it does not need protection. Explanation: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: From a Muslim trader, one-fortieth of his wealth is taken; from a dhimmi trader, one-twentieth; from a harbi trader, one-tenth. The proof is that 'Umar commanded his zakat collectors and 'ushr collectors thus, and his statement was in the presence of the Companions without dissent, so it constitutes consensus. The rational proof is that from the Muslim one-fortieth is taken because the Prophet said: "Give one-fortieth of your wealth, for every forty dirhams one dirham." And the 'ashir (collector) is authorized to take zakat because the Muslim needs protection, and the dhimmi needs protection even more than the Muslim because thieves covet the dhimmi's wealth more. So when the dhimmi is more in need of protection, double what is taken from the Muslim is taken from him, just as double the zakat is taken from Banu Taghlib. The harbi is to the dhimmi as the dhimmi is to the Muslim. For evidence, the testimony of harbis against dhimmis is not accepted, just as the testimony of dhimmis against Muslims is not accepted; but the testimony of dhimmis against harbis is accepted, just as the testimony of Muslims against dhimmis is accepted. So just as double is taken from the dhimmi relative to the Muslim, double is taken from the harbi relative to the dhimmi. Al-Quduri says: If a harbi passes the 'ashir with fifty dirhams, nothing is taken from him unless they take from our people a similar small amount, because taking from harbis is a transaction of reciprocity. The statement of 'Umar also indicates this: when he appointed the 'ashirs, he was asked, "How much shall we take from what a harbi passes with?" He asked, "How much do they take from us?" They said, "They take a tenth." He said, "Take a tenth from them." Here a question may arise: there is contradiction in the author's text, because earlier it was said that taking from dhimmis and harbis is by way of protection, and here it is said that taking from harbis is by way of reciprocity. The answer: Taking from harbis absolutely is due to protection, but the specific amount (i.e., one-tenth) is due to reciprocity. Thus no contradiction remains. In contrast, what is taken from Muslims and dhimmis is zakat or its double: from Muslims zakat, from dhimmis double the Muslim's zakat. Since it is zakat or its double, nisab is necessary. The author of al-Hidayah says: Taking from a small amount as reciprocity is permissible. This is in al-Jami' al-Saghir. In al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Zakah, it says: The 'ashir should not take from a small amount even if the harbis take from us such, because a small amount has always been overlooked, and taking one-tenth from it would be oppression. Another proof: a small amount does not need protection, and the 'ashir is entitled to take only because of protection provided. He said: And if a harbi passes with two hundred dirhams and it is not known how much they take from us, he takes one-tenth from him due to the statement of 'Umar: "If it perplexes you, then (take) one-tenth." And if it is known that they take from us one-quarter of a tenth or one-half of a tenth, he takes accordingly. And if they take everything, he does not take everything because that would be treachery. And if they take nothing at all, he takes nothing so that they may leave off taking from our traders, and because we are more deserving of noble conduct.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, a commentary on al-Hidayah, explains the rates of 'ushr (customs duty/tithe) imposed on merchandise of non-Muslim traders entering Muslim territory. The text is a combination of the original matn from al-Hidayah and its commentary. It begins by stating the basic rule: from a Muslim merchant, one-fortieth (1/40 or rub' al-'ushr) of the merchandise is taken; from a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim subject), one-twentieth (1/20 or nisf al-'ushr) is taken; and from a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) trader, one-tenth (1/10 or al-'ushr) is taken. This is attributed to the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, who instructed his tax collectors accordingly. The passage then addresses two scenarios: (1) If a harbi passes with a small amount (fifty dirhams), nothing is generally taken, unless the harbi state takes similarly small amounts from Muslim traders, in which case reciprocity ('mu'awadah') dictates that we take as they take. (2) If a harbi passes with two hundred dirhams (the nisab for zakat) and we do not know their rate, we take one-tenth by default, based on 'Umar's instruction. If we know their rate (e.g., 1/40 or 1/20), we take the same. If they take all our traders' goods, we do not take all (that would be treachery). If they take nothing, we take nothing to encourage them to stop and because we are more virtuous. The commentary resolves an apparent contradiction: the basis for taking from harbis is both protection (himayah) and reciprocity (mu'awadah). The absolute taking is for protection, while the specific amount is determined by reciprocity. For Muslims and dhimmis, the levy is zakat (or double zakat) which requires nisab, hence a minimum threshold. The passage includes references to al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, indicating that these rulings are from the Zahir al-Riwayah of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentary by al-Quduri and the author of Ashraf al-Hidayah provides rational proofs and analogies to establish the rates, emphasizing the proportionality based on need for protection and reciprocal treatment.

Key Terms
عُشْر ('ushr): A tithe or one-tenth levied on merchandise of traders passing through Muslim territory.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim from enemy territory (dar al-harb) who enters dar al-Islam for trade with temporary security (aman).
مُجَازَاة (mu'awadah): Reciprocal treatment; taking from harbi traders in kind to match what they take from Muslim traders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rate of 'ushr taken from a dhimmi merchant according to the Hanafi school?
A) One-tenth (1/10)
B) One-twentieth (1/20)
C) One-fortieth (1/40)
D) None, dhimmis are exempt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school imposes graduated 'ushr rates based on the trader's religious status and the need for protection, adjusted by reciprocity for enemy traders.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Taking 'Ushr from Harbi Merchants: The Principle of Reciprocity
Explains the ruling with proof from 'Umar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on taking 'ushr from harbi merchants, explain the principle of muqabala (reciprocity), and apply the ruling to scenarios based on knowledge of the reciprocal rate.

Core Idea
The 'ushr from harbi merchants is a reciprocal tax, not zakat; its rate mirrors what they charge Muslim merchants.

This passage from the Hidaya commentary explains the Hanafi ruling on the 'ushr tax collected from harbi (non-Muslim enemy) merchants who enter Muslim lands under safe conduct. Unlike zakat, which is an act of worship with fixed nisab and rates, the 'ushr from harbis is a reciprocal levy based on the principle of muqabala (counter-treatment). The ruling is grounded in the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, who instructed his 'ashirs (tax collectors) to charge harbi merchants the same percentage that harbi authorities charge Muslim merchants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Determine that taking 'ushr from harbi merchants is a wajib duty on the 'ashir, not an act of worship but a reciprocal tax.
Distinguish from zakat: zakat is for Muslims and dhimmis, with fixed nisab and rates.
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the proof from 'Umar's hadith: 'If you are unable, then take 'ushr.' This indicates obligation when the reciprocal rate is unknown.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni proof, but it suffices for wajib.
3
Understand the principle of reciprocity (mujazat)
Grasp that the amount taken from harbi merchants is based on what they take from Muslim merchants. This is a form of istihsan and justice.
The text resolves an apparent contradiction: taking 'ushr absolutely is for protection (himaya), but the specific rate is for reciprocity.
4
Apply the ruling to three scenarios
Scenario 1: Unknown rate → take 'ushr (10%). Scenario 2: Known rate → take that exact proportion (e.g., 5% or 2.5%). Scenario 3: They take all → do not take all (treachery forbidden); some scholars allow taking all except enough to return home.
If they take nothing, we take nothing to encourage good conduct.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that some mashayikh say take all wealth except return expenses; others say take all without exception. The text does not give a definitive tarjih.
This shows the range of legitimate opinion within the school.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم كتاب الزكوة طرح ذمی سے اس کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے جو مسلمان سے لیا جاتا ہے تو اسی طرح حربی سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا۔ جو ذمی سے لیا جاتا ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی حربی پچاس درہم کے ساتھ عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا تو اس سے کچھ نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ ہاں اگر وہ اس قدر قلیل مقدار سے ہمارے لوگوں سے لیتے ہیں تو پھر ہم بھی لیں گے کیونکہ حربوں سے لینا بطریق مجازات دبلی ہے جو معاملہ وہ ہمارے ساتھ کریں گے وہی ہم بھی ان کے ساتھ کریں گے حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا فرمان بھی اسی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے کیونکہ فاروق اعظم رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے جب عاشروں کو مقرر کیا تو آپ سے دریافت کیا گیا کہ " کم ناخذ مما مر به الحربی یعنی ہم لوگ حربی کے مال سے کس قدر وصول کریں تو آپ نے پوچھا کہ کم يأخذون منا ؟" وہ مہم سے کتنا لیتے ہیں؟ لوگوں نے کہا کہ عشر لیتے ہیں آپ نے فرمایا "خذوا منهم العشر “ تم بھی ان سے عشر وصول کرو اس جگہ ایک سوال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ مصنف کی عبارت میں منافات ہے کیونکہ یہ پہلے کہا گیا ہے کہ ذمیوں اور حربیوں سے عشر لینا بطریق حمایت ہے اور یہاں کہا گیا ہے کہ حربیوں سے لینا بطریق مجازات ہے۔ جواب: حربیوں سے مطلقاً لینا تو حمایت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مقدار معین یعنی دسواں حصہ لینا مجازات اور بدلے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اب اس صورت میں منافات کا اعتراض واقع نہ ہوگا۔
اس کے برخلاف مسلمان اور ذمی کہ ان سے جو لیا جاتا ہے وہ زکوۃ ہے۔ یا ز کوۃ کا دو چند ہے یعنی مسلمان سے زکوۃ لی جاتی ہے اور دمی سے زکوۃ مسلم کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے پس چونکہ ان سے زکوۃ یا زکوۃ کا دو چند لیا جاتا ہے اس لئے نصاب کا ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ اس نصاب سے زکوۃ یا ز کوۃ کا دو چند لیا جائے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مال قلیل سے بدلے کے طور پر لینا جائز ہے یہ جامع صغیر میں ہے۔ اور مبسوط کے کتاب الزکوۃ میں ہے کہ عربی کے قلیل مال سے عاشر کچھ نہ لے۔ اگر چہ حربی لوگ ہم سے ایسے مال سے لے لیتے ہیں کیونکہ قلیل مال ہمیشہ عفور ہا ہے اب اگر اس میں سے عشر لیا گیا تو ی ظلم ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قلیل مال حفاظت کا محتاج بھی نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ عاشر حفاظت ہی کی وجہ سے لینے کا مستحق ہے۔ اگر حربی دوسو د ر اہم لے کر عاشر کے پاس سے گذرے اور عاشر کو معلوم نہیں کہ مسلمانوں سے کس قدر لیا جاتا ہے تو حربی سے عشر لیا جائے گا
قَالَ وَإِنْ مَرَّحَرْبِى بِمِائَتَى دِرْهَم وَلَا يُعْلَمُ كَمْ يَأْخُذُونَ مِنَّا يَأْخُذُ مِنْهُ الْعُشْرُ لِقَوْلِ عُمَر فَإِنْ أَعْيَاكُمْ فَالْعُشْرُ وَإِنْ أَنَّهُمْ يَأْخُذُونَ مِنَّا رُبْعَ عُشْرٍ أَو نِصْفُ عَشْرِ يَأْخُذُ بِقَدْرِهِ وَإِنْ كَانُوا يَأْخُدُونَ الكُل لا يأخُدُ الكُلَّ لأنه غدر وَإِنْ كَانُوا لَا يَأْخُذُونَ اصَلاَ لَا يَأْخُذُ لِيَتْرُكُوا الْأَخَذَ مِنْ تُجَارِنَا وَلِأَنَّا أَحَقُّ بِمَكَارِمِ الْأَخْلَاقِ
ترجمہ اور اگر حربی دو سو درہم کے ساتھ گذرا اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ وہ لوگ ہم سے کس قدر لیتے ہیں تو عاشر اس سے عشرلے لے ۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر تم کو تھکا دے تو عشر لے لو۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم ہے کہ حربی لوگ ہم سے چالیسواں حصہ یا بیسواں حصہ لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عاشر بھی اسی قدر لئے اور اگر معلوم ہو کہ حربی لوگ ہم سے کل مال لے لیتے ہیں تو ہمار ا عاشر کل مال نہ لے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو بد عہدی ہے۔ اور اگر حربی لوگ ہم سے کچھ نہ لیتے ہوں تو ہمارا عا شر بھی کچھ نہ لے گا تا کہ ہمارے تاجروں سے بھی لینا چھوڑ دیں اور اس لئے کہ ہم اخلاق کریمہ کے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔
كتاب الزكوة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حربی تاجر دو سو درہم یا اس سے زائد کے ساتھ عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور مسلمان عاشر کو اس کا علم نہیں کہ وہ ہمارے تاجروں سے کیا لیتے ہیں تو اس سے عشر لیا جائے گا۔ دلیل حضرت عمر کا قول ہے کہ فَإِنْ أَعْيَاكُمْ فَالْعُشْر یعنی اگر تم یہ جاننے سے عاجز ہو جاؤ کہ حربی تم سے کیا لیتے ہیں تو پھر تم دسواں حصہ لے لو۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم ہو کہ حربی لوگ ہم سے چالیسواں یا بیسواں حصہ لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عا شر بھی ان سے اس قدر لے گا۔ اور اگر معلوم ہو کہ حربی لوگ ہمارے تاجروں سے پورا مال لے لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عاشر حربی تاجر سے پورا مال نہ لے گا کیونکہ یہ تو بد عہدی ہے کہ امن دینے کے بعد پورا مال چھین لیا۔ اور غدر کرنا حرام ہے اگر چہ حر بی کفار ایسا کریں چنانچہ حربی لوگ اگر امن دینے کے بعد ہمارے تاجر کو مار ڈالیں تو ہم قتل نہیں کریں گے اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں ہمارا عاشر بھی پورا مال لے لے ۔ سوائے اس قدر مال کے جس سے وہ اپنے وطن پہنچ جائے کیونکہ ہم اس کو وطن پہنچانے پر مامور ہیں اللہ رب العزت کا ارشاد ہے" ثُمَّ ابْلِغُهُ مَا مَنَ : " پھر اس کو اس کے ٹھکانے یعنی وطن پہنچا دو اور بعض نے کہا کہ حربی تاجر سے پورا مال لے لیا جائے گا۔ اس کے پاس اس قدر بھی نہ چھوڑا جائے کہ وہ اپنے وطن پہنچ سکے۔ کیونکہ حربیوں سے بطریق مجازات کیا جاتا ہے پس جیسا سلوک وہ ہمارے ساتھ کرتے ہیں کہ ہمارے تاجروں سے پورا مال لے لیتے ہیں ویسا ہی ہم بھی ان کے ساتھ کریں گے تاکہ ان کو تنبیہ ہو اور اگر حربی ہم سے کچھ نہ لیتے ہوں تو ہمارا عاشر بھی کچھ نہ لے گا۔ تا کہ وہ ہمارے تاجروں سے لینا چھوڑ دیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے ہم سے کچھ نہ لے کر ہمارے ساتھ اخلاق کریمہ کا معاملہ کیا ہے پس ہم اخلاق کریمہ کے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume Three, Book of Zakat. The discussion: From a dhimmi, double of what is taken from a Muslim is taken; similarly from a harbi, double of what is taken from a dhimmi is taken. Sahib al-Quduri says: If a harbi passes by an 'ashir with fifty dirhams, nothing is taken from him. However, if they take such a small amount from our people, then we too will take, because taking from harbis is by way of muqabala (reciprocity) as a weak reason. Whatever treatment they give us, we will treat them likewise. The command of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) also points to this, because when Faruq al-A'zam appointed the 'ashirs, he was asked: 'How much do we take from the property of a harbi?' He asked: 'How much do they take from us?' The people said: 'They take 'ushr.' He said: 'Take 'ushr from them.' Here a question may arise: There is contradiction in the author's words, because earlier it was said that taking 'ushr from dhimmis and harbis is by way of protection (himaya), and here it is said that taking from harbis is by way of muqabala. Answer: Taking from harbis absolutely is due to protection, but taking the specific amount (one-tenth) is due to muqabala and retaliation. Thus no contradiction occurs. In contrast, from Muslims and dhimmis, what is taken is zakat, or double of zakat; i.e., zakat is taken from Muslims, and double of zakat from dhimmis. Since zakat or double of zakat is taken from them, the existence of nisab is necessary so that zakat or double of zakat is taken from that nisab. The author of Hidaya says: Taking from small wealth as exchange is permissible; this is in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And in al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Zakat, it says: The 'ashir should not take anything from small wealth of an Arab, even if the harbis take such wealth from us, because small wealth is always [عفور ها?] now if 'ushr is taken from it, it would be oppression. Second proof: Small wealth does not need protection, while the 'ashir deserves to take only because of protection. If a harbi passes by an 'ashir with two hundred dirhams and the 'ashir does not know how much is taken from Muslims, then 'ushr is taken from him. He said: And if a harbi passes with two hundred dirhams and it is not known how much they take from us, then 'ushr is taken from him, due to the saying of 'Umar: 'If you are unable, then 'ushr.' And if they take from us a quarter of 'ushr (2.5%) or half of 'ushr (5%), then he takes accordingly. And if they take the entire wealth, he does not take the whole, because that is treachery. And if they take nothing at all, he takes nothing, so that they leave off taking from our merchants, and because we are more deserving of noble morals. Translation: If a harbi passes with two hundred dirhams and it is not known how much they take from us, the 'ashir takes 'ushr. Because 'Umar said: If you are unable, then take 'ushr. And if it is known that the harbis take from us a quarter (2.5%) or a twentieth (5%), then our 'ashir takes accordingly. And if it is known that the harbis take the entire wealth from us, our 'ashir does not take the whole, because that is bad faith. And if the harbis take nothing from us, our 'ashir also takes nothing, so that they leave off taking from our merchants, and because we are more deserving of noble morals. Kitab al-Zakat, Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume Three. Explanation of the issue: If a harbi merchant passes by an 'ashir with two hundred dirhams or more, and the Muslim 'ashir does not know what they take from our merchants, then 'ushr is taken from him. Proof: The saying of 'Umar: 'If you are unable, then 'ushr' meaning if you are unable to know what the harbi takes from you, then take a tenth. And if it is known that the harbis take from us a quarter or a twentieth, then our 'ashir takes that amount from them. And if it is known that the harbis take the entire wealth from our merchants, our 'ashir does not take the entire wealth from the harbi merchant, because this would be bad faith—taking the entire wealth after giving aman. And treachery is haram, even if the harbi disbelievers do it. So if harbis kill our merchant after giving aman, we do not kill. And some mashayikh said: In this case, our 'ashir may take the entire wealth, except for an amount with which he can reach his homeland, because we are commanded to deliver him to his homeland. Allah Almighty says: 'Then convey him to his place of safety.' And some said: The entire wealth of the harbi merchant will be taken, and nothing will be left with him to reach his homeland, because dealing with harbis is by way of muqabala; as they treat our merchants by taking all their wealth, so we treat them, to deter them. And if the harbis take nothing from us, our 'ashir also takes nothing, so that they leave off taking from our merchants. Second proof: They have dealt with us with noble morals by taking nothing, so we are more deserving of noble morals.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on al-Hidayah, addressing the 'ushr taken from harbi (non-Muslim enemy) merchants who enter Muslim lands under aman. The ruling is based on the principle of reciprocity (muqabala) established by the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. The text first clarifies that the 'ushr from harbis is not zakat itself but a form of reciprocal tax, unlike the zakat taken from Muslims and dhimmis. Sahib al-Quduri's view is cited: if the harbi's wealth is below 200 dirhams (nisab), nothing is taken, but if the harbis take such small amounts from Muslims, then we reciprocate. The author then resolves an apparent contradiction: taking from harbis absolutely is for protection (himaya), but the specific rate (10%) is determined by reciprocity. The core ruling is that when the amount taken by harbis from Muslims is unknown, the default is 'ushr (10%) based on 'Umar's instruction. If the harbis take a different percentage (e.g., 2.5% or 5%), we take the same. If they take all wealth, we do not take all (that would be treachery); some scholars allow taking all except enough to return home, while others allow taking all in retaliation. If they take nothing, we take nothing to encourage good treatment. The proof from 'Umar's hadith is explicit, and the reasoning is based on justice and noble conduct.

Key Terms
عاشر ('ashir): The official tax collector appointed by the Muslim ruler to collect 'ushr from merchants at borders or checkpoints.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under a peace treaty (aman) with Muslims, i.e., an enemy subject who may enter Muslim lands temporarily under safe conduct.
عشر ('ushr): A one-tenth (10%) tax levied on merchandise of merchants entering Muslim lands, collected by the 'ashir.
مجازات (mujazat): Reciprocity or retaliation in treatment; the principle that the Muslim state treats harbi merchants based on how they treat Muslim merchants in their lands.
حمایت (himaya): Protection; the basis for taking 'ushr from dhimmis and harbis absolutely, as a fee for security provided by the state.
غدر (ghadr): Treachery, breach of trust; prohibited in Islam even towards enemies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is taken from a harbi merchant when the 'ashir does not know how much the harbis take from Muslim merchants?
A) Nothing
B) Double 'ushr (20%)
C) 'Ushr (10%)
D) The entire property

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school bases the 'ushr from harbi merchants on reciprocity: the rate is whatever they charge Muslim merchants, defaulting to 10% when unknown.
