intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Repeated Passage of Harbi and Annual 'Ushr
States that 'ushr is taken only once per year from a harbi merchant even on repeated passages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the frequency of 'ushr collection from a harbi merchant and explain the rationale based on istisal and the annual renewal of aman.

Core Idea
A harbi merchant pays 'ushr only once per year, no matter how many 'ashirs he passes; repeated collection would destroy his wealth.

Imagine a harbi merchant entering Muslim lands to trade. He passes a checkpoint and pays the 'ushr tax. A few months later, he passes another checkpoint. Must he pay again? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling based on the purpose of the tax and the nature of the safe-conduct (aman). This lesson unpacks that ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage to determine what the law says about taking 'ushr from a harbi who passes multiple 'ashirs within a year. The key phrase: 'he is not charged 'ushr until a year passes.'
The ruling applies regardless of whether the harbi passes the same or a different 'ashir.
2
Understand the Prohibition of Istisal
The text gives the first reason: repeated collection would eradicate the merchant's capital (istisal al-mal). Reflect on why istisal is prohibited – the right to collect is for protection, not destruction.
Istisal is a recognized harm in Hanafi usul.
3
Link to the Renewal of Aman
The second reason: the first aman (safe conduct) remains in effect for one year. After a year, a new aman is considered granted, allowing fresh collection without causing eradication.
The harbi is not permitted to stay more than a year without renewing aman.
4
Apply to Scenarios
Consider two scenarios: (1) the harbi returns to dar al-harb and re-enters after a year; (2) he stays within dar al-Islam and passes another 'ashir within the same year. Determine the ruling for each.
In the first case, 'ushr is taken again; in the second, not.
5
Confirm the Intra-Madhhab Consensus
The passage does not mention any disagreement among the Hanafi imams. This ruling is settled and found in the zahir al-riwayah.
No ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حربی ایک عاشر پر گذرا اور اس نے عشر ادا کر دیا پھر دوسرے پر گذرا تو اس سے عشر نہیں لیا جائے گا
.
قَالَ وَإِنْ مَرَّ الْحَرْبِيُّ عَلَى عَاشِرِ فَعَشَرَهُ ثُمَّ مَرَّ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى لَمْ يُعشْرُهُ حَتَّى يَحُولَ عَلَيْهِ الحَول لأنَّ الأخذ فى كُلِّ مَرَّةٍ إسْتِبْصَالُ الْمَالِ وَ حَقُّ الْأَخْذِ لِحِفْظِهِ وَلانَّ حُكْمَ الأمان الأَوَّلِ باقٍ وَبَعْدَ الحول يَتَجَدَّد الأمان لأنَّه لَا يُمْكِنُ مِنَ الْمُقَام إِلا حَوْلاً وَالْأَخُذُ بَعْدَهُ لَا يَسْتَاصِلُ الْمَالَ
ترجمہ اور اگر حربی کا گذر کسی عاشر پر ہوا پھر اس نے عشر وصول کر لیا پھر وہ حربی دوسری بار وہاں سے گذرا تو اس سے دوبارہ بشر نہ لے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس پر سال پلٹ جائے کیونکہ ہر بار عشر لینا تو مال کو جڑ سے نیست و نابود کر دینا ہوا۔ حالانکہ لینے کا حق حفاظت مال کے لئے تھا اور اس لئے کہ پہلے امان کا حکم باقی ہے اور سال گذرنے کے بعد امان نئی ہو جائے گی کیونکہ حربی کو یہاں مخبر نے کا قابو نہیں دیا کہ اور کے کیونکہ عربی کو ٹھہرنے گیا مگر ایک سال اور سال کے بعد عشر لینا استیصال نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تربی تاجر کا گذرنا عاشر پر نہوا اور عاشر نے اس سے عشر وصول کر لیا پھر کچھ دن کے بعد دار الحرب واپس جائے سے پہلے دوبارہ اس کا گذر عاشر کے پاس سے ہوا تو اس کی دو صورتین میں اس حربی کا دوبارہ گذرا ایک سال کے بعد ہوا ہوگا۔ یا اسی سال کے انا ر ہوا ہو گا اگر ایک سال بعد ہوا ہے تو عاشر اس سے دوبارہ عشر وصول کرے گا۔ اور اگر اسی سال کے اندر ہوا ہے تو عاشر دوبارہ عشر وصول نہ
A harbi passed by one 'ashir and paid 'ushr, then passed by another; so 'ushr will not be taken from him again. He said: And if a harbi passes by an 'ashir and he takes 'ushr from him, then he passes a second time, he is not charged 'ushr until a year passes, because taking every time would eradicate the wealth, while the right to take is for its protection; and because the first aman remains, and after a year aman is renewed, since he is not permitted to stay more than a year. And taking after that is not eradicating. Translation: If a harbi passes by an 'ashir and the 'ashir collects 'ushr, then the harbi passes a second time, the 'ashir will not collect 'ushr again until a year passes, because taking each time would destroy the wealth completely, whereas the right to take is for protection; and because the first aman remains in effect, and after a year new aman is established, as the harbi is not allowed to stay more than a year. Taking after that is not eradication. Explanation: If a harbi merchant passes by an 'ashir and the 'ashir collects 'ushr, then after some days before returning to dar al-harb he passes again by the 'ashir, there are two scenarios: either the second passage occurs after a year or within the same year. If after a year, the 'ashir will collect 'ushr again; if within the year, the 'ashir will not collect again.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage states a ruling-with-reasoning about the frequency of 'ushr collection from a harbi merchant. The principle: 'ushr is taken only once per year, even if the harbi passes multiple 'ashirs. The reason is that repeated collection within a year would eradicate the merchant's capital (istisal al-mal), while the justification for taking 'ushr is to provide protection. The first aman (safe conduct) given to the harbi lasts for one year, during which his goods are protected. If he passes another 'ashir within that year, no additional 'ushr is due because the obligation has already been fulfilled. After a year, the aman is considered renewed, and a new 'ushr may be taken, as that would not be eradication but a fresh charge. The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid destroying the merchant's wealth and to uphold the original purpose of the tax: protection, not exploitation.

Key Terms
حول (hawl): A lunar year; the period after which the aman is renewed and a new 'ushr may be taken.
امان (aman): Safe conduct granted to a harbi to enter Muslim lands for trade, initially valid for one year.
استیصال (istisal): Eradication or complete destruction of the merchant's capital due to repeated taxation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How often is 'ushr taken from a harbi merchant who passes multiple 'ashirs within a year?
A) Every time he passes
B) Once per year
C) Twice per year
D) Only if he stays more than a month

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits 'ushr collection to once per year from a harbi merchant to avoid eradication of his wealth, based on the principle that the right to collect is for protection.

Determining the Tithe from a Harbi Merchant Based on Reciprocity
Explains how much 'ushr to take based on what the harbi takes from Muslim merchants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on 'ushr from a harbi merchant, identify the proof from Umar (RA), and apply the principle of reciprocity to determine the correct amount.

Core Idea
The 'ushr from a harbi merchant is based on reciprocity, not a fixed 10%; the default is 10% only when unknown.

This lesson explains a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding trade with harbi merchants. The amount of customs duty (ushr) is determined by what the harbi state imposes on Muslim merchants. The primary proof is the saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA), which shows that reciprocity governs the rate, and defaulting to one-tenth is only when the reciprocal rate is unknown.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the collection of 'ushr from a harbi merchant. The ruling is that it is wajib, but the amount varies based on what the harbi takes from Muslims.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the saying of Umar (RA): 'Fa in ahyakum fa al-'ushr' (If you are unable to know, then take the tenth). This is a Qawl Sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fa al-'ushr' indicates obligation. The condition 'in ahyakum' shows that the default applies only when the reciprocal rate is unknown, implying that when known, the reciprocal rate should be taken.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute when the harbi takes all goods: should the collector also take all? Some say no, due to prohibition of treachery and Quranic command to convey to safety; others say yes, as retribution.
The preferred view is to leave enough for the harbi to return home.
5
Apply the principle to scenarios
Apply the reciprocity rule: if harbi takes 1/40, we take 1/40; if they take nothing, we take nothing; if unknown, default 1/10.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حربی تاجر دو سو درہم یا اس سے زائد کے ساتھ عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور مسلمان عاشر کو اس کا علم نہیں کہ وہ ہمارے تاجروں سے کیا لیتے ہیں تو اس سے عشر لیا جائے گا۔ دلیل حضرت عمر کا قول ہے کہ فَانُ احْيَاكُمْ فَالْعُشْر یعنی اگر تم یہ جاننے سے عاجز ہو جاؤ کہ حربی تم سے کیا لیتے ہیں تو پھر تم دسواں حصہ لے لو۔ اور اگر یہ معلوم ہو کہ حربی لوگ ہم سے چالیسواں یا بیسواں حصہ لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عا شر بھی ان سے اس قدر لے گا۔ اور اگر معلوم ہو کہ حربی لوگ ہمارے تاجروں سے پورا مال لے لیتے ہیں تو ہمارا عاشر حربی تاجر سے پورا مال نہ لے گا کیونکہ یہ تو بد عہدی ہے کہ امن دینے کے بعد پورا مال چھین لیا۔ اور غدر کرنا حرام ہے اگر چہ حر بی کفار ایسا کریں چنانچہ حربی لوگ اگر امن دینے کے بعد ہمارے تاجر کو مار ڈالیں تو ہم قتل نہیں کریں گے اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں ہمارا عاشر بھی پورا مال لے لے ۔ سوائے اس قدر مال کے جس سے وہ اپنے وطن پہنچ جائے کیونکہ ہم اس کو وطن پہنچانے پر مامور ہیں اللہ رب العزت کا ارشاد ہے" ثُمَّ ابْلِغُهُ مَا مَنَ : " پھر اس کو اس کے ٹھکانے یعنی وطن پہنچا دو اور بعض نے کہا کہ حربی تاجر سے پورا مال لے لیا جائے گا۔ اس کے پاس اس قدر بھی نہ چھوڑا جائے کہ وہ اپنے وطن پہنچ سکے۔ کیونکہ حربیوں سے بطریق مجازات کیا جاتا ہے پس جیسا سلوک وہ ہمارے ساتھ کرتے ہیں کہ ہمارے تاجروں سے پورا مال لے لیتے ہیں ویسا ہی ہم بھی ان کے ساتھ کریں گے تاکہ ان کو تنبیہ ہو اور اگر حربی ہم سے کچھ نہ لیتے ہوں تو ہمارا عاشر بھی کچھ نہ لے گا۔ تا کہ وہ ہمارے تاجروں سے لینا چھوڑ دیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے ہم سے کچھ نہ لے کر ہمارے ساتھ اخلاق کریمہ کا معاملہ کیا ہے پس ہم اخلاق کریمہ کے زیادہ الائق ہیں۔
Explanation of the issue: If a harbi merchant passes by the tithe collector with two hundred dirhams or more, and the Muslim tithe collector does not know what they take from our merchants, then tithe is taken from him. The proof is the saying of Hadrat Umar: 'Fa in ahyakum fa al-'ushr' meaning if you are unable to know what the harbi takes from you, then you take one-tenth. And if it is known that the harbi people take one-fortieth or one-twentieth from us, then our tithe collector will also take that amount from them. And if it is known that the harbi people take the entire property from our merchants, then our tithe collector will not take the entire property from the harbi merchant because this would be breach of covenant after granting aman, and treachery is forbidden even if the harbi disbelievers do it. Just as if the harbi people kill our merchant after granting aman, we do not kill (in retaliation). Some mashayikh have said that in this case our tithe collector may take the entire property except for enough wealth to enable him to reach his homeland, because we are commanded to convey him to his homeland. Allah the Almighty says: 'Then convey him to his place of safety.' Others said that the entire property will be taken from the harbi merchant and nothing will be left to enable him to reach his homeland, because retribution is practiced against the harbis; so just as they treat us by taking all property from our merchants, we will treat them similarly to warn them. And if the harbi takes nothing from us, our tithe collector will also take nothing, so that they may abandon taking from our merchants. A second proof is that by taking nothing from us they have dealt with us with noble character, and we are more deserving of noble character.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining the fiqh ruling on how much 'ushr (tithe) should be taken from a harbi merchant who enters Muslim lands with trade goods. The Hanafi position is that the amount is determined by reciprocity. The primary source is the saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA), the second Caliph, who is a major authority in Hanafi fiqh. The ruling states: if the Muslim collector does not know how much the harbi state takes from Muslim merchants, the default is one-tenth (10%) of the goods. If it is known that they take a lesser fraction (like 1/40 or 1/20), then the same fraction is taken. If they take the entire goods, the Muslim collector should not take all, as that would be treachery (ghadr) which is haram. There is a difference of opinion among later scholars (mashayikh) whether the harbi should be left with enough to return home, citing the Quranic command (Quran 9:6: 'then grant him protection so that he may hear the words of Allah, and then convey him to his place of safety'), or whether retribution (mujazat) is applied by taking everything. The passage also notes that if the harbi takes nothing from Muslims, then nothing is taken from him, as an incentive for good treatment. This ruling is based on Hanafi principles of aman (safe conduct) and reciprocity in mu'amalat.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): An enemy non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, not under Muslim protection.
عشر (ushr): The tithe or one-tenth tax on goods of a harbi merchant passing through Muslim lands.
عاشر (ashir): The tax collector appointed to collect 'ushr from merchants at borders or checkpoints.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default 'ushr rate from a harbi merchant if the Muslim collector does not know what the harbi state takes from Muslim merchants?
A) One-fortieth (2.5%)
B) One-tenth (10%)
C) The entire property
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines 'ushr from harbi merchants on the basis of reciprocity, with the default of one-tenth when the reciprocal rate is unknown, and the preferred view leaves enough for the harbi's return when the enemy takes all.

No Repeated Tithe Within the Year from the Same Harbi
Ruling on repeated 'ushr from the same harbi within a year, with proof from Umar (RA)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that 'ushr is not taken more than once per year from a harbi and explain the proof from the practice of Umar (RA).

Core Idea
A harbi pays 'ushr only once per year — repeated taking destroys wealth and violates the purpose of the tax.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Islamic taxation: the prohibition against taking 'ushr from the same harbi merchant more than once within a single year. The Hanafi school bases this on the principle of preserving wealth (hifz al-mal) and the continuation of the aman for the year. We will analyze the ruling and its proof from the incident of Umar (RA) with a Christian merchant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening Arabic sentence: if a harbi passes a tithe collector and pays, then passes again, do not take tithe again until a year passes. This is the core ruling.
The ruling applies as long as the harbi remains in dar al-Islam under the same aman.
2
Understand the reasoning (istisal and aman)
The commentary gives two reasons: (1) taking repeatedly would destroy (istisal) the wealth, contradicting the purpose of the tax; (2) the first aman remains in effect for the year, so no new liability arises until it expires.
Istisal means uprooting or complete destruction; tax law aims to avoid this.
3
Locate the proof from Umar's story
Find the story narrated via al-'Inayah: a Christian merchant complained to Umar that his horses would be lost if 'ushr was taken repeatedly. Umar ordered not to take it again. The direct command: 'If you have taken the tithe once, do not take it again.'
This is a qawl sahabi (saying of a companion) used as proof.
4
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider a harbi who passes a checkpoint in January and again in June: no 'ushr. But if he passes in January of the next year (after a full year), 'ushr is due again because a new aman is assumed.
The passage also discusses if the harbi stays over a year: he becomes a dhimmi subject to jizyah, so the second-year 'ushr may not practically arise.
5
Note the refinement from Fath al-Qadir
The author of Fath al-Qadir points out that a harbi is normally not permitted to stay a full year; if he does, jizyah is imposed, and the case of a second-year 'ushr may not occur. This resolves apparent contradictions in al-Hidayah's wording.
This shows the importance of precise legal analysis across multiple commentaries.

جاتی ۔ صاحب فتح القدیر نے کہا ہے کہ KALONنُ مِنَ الْمُقَامِ الاحولاً " میں انتظا الا زائد ہے اور سہو کا تب ہے تو اب حاصل یہ ہوا لَا کہ عربی کے واسطے دار الا اسلام کے اندر ایک سال قیام کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ حربی کو پورے ایک سال قیام کی اجازت نہیں ہوتی ۔ بلکہ ایک سال سے کم کی اجازت ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ حربی جب دارالاسلام میں داخل ہو گا تو امام اس سے یہ کہے گا کہ اگر تو نے پورے سال قیام کیا تو تجھ پر جزیہ ہو گا اب اگر اس نے ایک سال قیام کیا اور امام نے اس پر جزیہ مقرر کر دیا تو اب اس کے لئے دار الحرب وت کرواپس جانا ممکن نہ ہوگا بلکہ وہ ذمی بن کر دار الاسلام میں زندگی کے دن پورے کرے گا۔

صاحب فتح القدیر کی اس تصیح عبارت کے بعد صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت میں تناقض لازم آئے گا۔ اس طور پر کہ شروع مسئلہ میں کہا گیا ہے کہ حربی اگر عاشر کے پاس سے دوبارہ گذرے تو اس سے دوبارہ عشر نہیں لیا جائے گا الا یہ کہ اس پر سال گذر جائے یعنی اگر ایک سال
A harbi passed by a tithe collector and paid the tithe, then passed by another; tithe will not be taken from him again until a year passes.

He said: If a harbi passes by a tithe collector and he takes the tithe from him, then he passes another time, he should not take the tithe from him again until a year elapses, because taking in each occurrence would be destroying the wealth, while the right to take is for its preservation; and because the first aman remains in effect, and after a year the aman is renewed because he cannot stay except for a year, and taking after that does not destroy the wealth.

Translation: And if a harbi passes by a tithe collector and he collects the tithe, then that harbi passes by that place a second time, he will not take tithe again until a year passes by him, because taking tithe every time would utterly destroy the wealth, while the right to take was for the preservation of wealth; and because the first aman continues, and after a year the aman will be renewed because the harbi is not permitted to stay except for one year, and taking after a year is not destructive.

Explanation of the issue: If a harbi merchant passes by a tithe collector and the collector takes the tithe, then after some days before returning to dar al-harb he passes by the tithe collector again, there are two possibilities: his second passing occurs after a year or within the same year. If after a year, the collector will take tithe again. If within the same year, the collector will not take tithe again. The proof is that if within a year tithe is taken repeatedly, the poor man's entire property would become subject to tithe, leaving nothing, while the right to take tithe from a harbi was only for preservation of wealth. A second proof is that within the year the first aman remains, and he has already paid tithe under it, so the collector should not take tithe again in one year. The command of Umar (RA) also supports this. According to the author of al-'Inayah, there is a story: A Christian (nasrani) passed by the tithe collector of Umar with his horses, and the collector took tithe. Before returning to dar al-harb, he passed by the same collector again within the same year. The collector intended to take tithe again. The Christian said: If you take tithe every time, all my horses will be gone. So the Christian left the horses and went to Umar. When he entered Madinah, he went to the Prophet's mosque, placed his hands on the door frame, and said: O Amir al-Mu'minin, I am an old Christian. Umar said: I am a follower of the religion of Ibrahim. The Christian narrated the whole story. Umar said: Your grievance will be heard. He lowered his head and returned. The Christian thought Umar took his complaint lightly. But when he reached his horses, he found a letter from Umar already arrived, saying: 'If you have taken the tithe once, do not take it again.' Seeing this, the old Christian said: If this religion has such justice, it is surely the true religion, and he became Muslim. From this incident, it is learned that if a harbi has not returned to dar al-harb, tithe will not be taken from him twice in one year. Yes, if he remains in dar al-Islam after a year, at the start of the second year tithe will be taken again, because after a year aman is renewed, and with renewed aman, tithe becomes obligatory again. Also, taking tithe after a year does not cause destruction of wealth. Renewal of aman after a year is necessary because a harbi cannot stay in dar al-Islam for more than a year; he is not given permission to stay longer. The author of Fath al-Qadir said that the phrase 'la yumkinu min al-muqami illa haulan' contains a slight excess and error. So the outcome is that a harbi cannot stay in dar al-Islam for a full year. This is correct because a harbi is not granted permission to stay for a full year; rather, permission is for less than a year. Thus, when a harbi enters dar al-Islam, the imam will say to him: 'If you stay for a full year, jizyah will be imposed on you.' Then if he stays for a year and the imam imposes jizyah on him, it will not be possible for him to return to dar al-harb; rather, he will become a dhimmi and spend the rest of his life in dar al-Islam.

After this correction by the author of Fath al-Qadir, there would be an apparent contradiction in the wording of Hidayah, because at the beginning of the issue it is said that if a harbi passes by a tithe collector again, tithe is not taken from him again unless a year passes, i.e., if a year...
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from al-Hidayah, dealing with the rule of repeated tithe on the same harbi merchant within one year. The core ruling is: once a harbi has paid 'ushr, he is not liable again within the same year, even if he passes the same or a different 'ashir multiple times. The reasoning is twofold: (1) taking repeatedly would destroy the merchant's capital, contradicting the purpose of the tax (which is to raise revenue while preserving wealth); (2) the initial aman (safe conduct) remains valid for one year, so no new liability arises. After a year, if the harbi is still present, a new aman is assumed, and 'ushr is due again. However, the commentary introduces a critical refinement from Fath al-Qadir: a harbi is normally not permitted to stay a full year; if he does, he becomes a dhimmi and subject to jizyah, so the case of a second year 'ushr may not practically arise. The passage concludes by noting an apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah's wording, but this is resolved by understanding the exact legal scenario. The story of Umar (RA) with the Christian merchant serves as a powerful illustration of Islamic justice and the basis for this ruling. The story itself functions as a proof (qawl sahabi) supporting the rule. The Hanafi position is clear: no second 'ushr within the year.

Key Terms
استیصال (istisal): The complete destruction or uprooting of wealth, which is avoided in tax policy.
امان (aman): Safe conduct granted to a harbi allowing him to enter and trade in Muslim lands temporarily.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim from a hostile state, not under Muslim protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is 'ushr not taken again from a harbi within the same year?
A) Because the harbi has already become a dhimmi
B) Because repeated taking would destroy his wealth and the first aman remains
C) Because the harbi has returned to dar al-harb
D) Because 'ushr is only due once in a lifetime

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'ushr is taken only once per year from a harbi who remains under the same aman, to prevent destruction of his wealth.

When Can a Harbi Be Charged 'Ushr Multiple Times?
Explaining the ruling on repeated 'ushr from a harbi with proofs from Umar (RA)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the frequency of 'ushr from a harbi based on the duration of aman and the precedent of Umar (RA).

Core Idea
A harbi's 'ushr is taken once per aman period; returning to Dar al-Harb triggers a new aman and a new 'ushr.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani explains when a harbi trader can be subjected to 'ushr multiple times within a year. The key is whether the same aman (safe conduct) still applies. Using the famous incident of Umar (RA), the Hanafi school establishes that 'ushr is not a per-transaction fee but an annual levy tied to the aman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Taking 'ushr from a harbi. What is the ruling? It is wajib once per aman period, not repeatedly within the same year.
Distinguish 'ushr from zakat: 'ushr is a levy on non-Muslims for protection of trade.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the command of Umar (RA) to his customs officer: 'If you have taken 'ushr once, do not take it again.'
This is a qawl sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'la ta'khudh' indicates prohibition. The reasoning is that taking 'ushr twice within the same aman would lead to depletion of the harbi's property (istisal), which defeats the purpose of protection.
Also, the aman remains valid throughout the year unless the harbi returns to Dar al-Harb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (unspecified) hold that 'ushr should be taken every time the harbi passes. The Hanafi school rejects this, citing Umar's instruction and the principle of avoiding depletion.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if 'ushr were taken each time, the harbi's entire wealth could be consumed, discouraging trade. The Hanafi rule protects the trader and encourages commerce.
If the harbi leaves Dar al-Islam and returns, a new aman is formed, and 'ushr is taken again.

لفظ [حَوْلَ] غلط ہے جیسا کہ بیان ہوا تو مطلب یہ ہوا کہ حربی کو ایک سال ٹھہرنے پر قابو نہیں دیا گیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حربی ایک سال تک دارالاسلام میں ٹھہرارہا اور امام کو اس کے حال کا علم نہیں ہو يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ عَشَرَهُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ رَجَعَ بِأَمَانٍ جَدِيدٍ وَكَذَا الْأَخْذُ بَعْدَهُ لَا يُفْضِي إِلَى الِاسْتِيصَالِ ترجمہ اور اگر اس سے عشر لے لیا پھر وہ دارالحرب کی طرف واپس چلا گیا، پھر وہ اسی روز واپس آ گیا تو بھی اس سے عشر لے گا کیونکہ وہ جدید امان کے ساتھ آیا ہے اور یونہی اس کے بعد عشر لینا استیصال کی جانب مفضی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عاشر نے حربی تاجر سے عشر لے لیا پھر وہ حربی تاجر دار الحرب جا کر اسی دن واپس آ گیا تو ان سے دوبارہ عشر لیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ حربی جب دار الحرب جا کر واپس آیا تو نئے امان کے ساتھ آیا ہے پس اس نئے امان کی وجہ سے اس سے دوبارہ عشر وصول کیا جائے گا۔ اور دار الحرب جا کر واپس آنے کے بعد عشر لینا استصلاح مال کا بھی سبب نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی دوبارہ عشر لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
He will do it. The proof for this is that if he passes by the 'ashir repeatedly within one year and the 'ushr is taken repeatedly, the poor man's entire wealth will be consumed by 'ushr, and nothing will remain with him, whereas the right to take 'ushr from a harbi was only for the protection of property. The second proof is that within the year, the rule of the first aman remains, and he has paid 'ushr on its basis, so the 'ashir will not take 'ushr again within one year. This is supported by the command of Umar (RA). According to the narration of Sahib al-'Inayah, a Christian passed by the 'ashir of Umar with his horses; the 'ashir took 'ushr from this harbi Christian. Before returning to Dar al-Harb, within the same year he passed by the same 'ashir again. The 'ashir intended to take 'ushr again, so the Christian said: 'If you take 'ushr every time, all my horses will be finished...' Then the Christian went to Umar. Umar wrote to the 'ashir: 'If you have taken 'ushr once, do not take it again.' The Christian became Muslim. From this incident it is understood that if a harbi has not returned to Dar al-Harb, 'ushr will not be taken from him twice in one year. However, if the harbi remains in Dar al-Islam after one year, 'ushr will be taken again at the start of the second year, because after a year there is a renewal of aman... The author of Fath al-Qadir said that in the phrase 'la yumkinu min al-muqam al-hawla', the word 'al-hawla' is superfluous and a scribal error... The response is that if the harbi stayed for a year and the imam was unaware, then 'ushr will be taken again. If 'ushr was taken and then he returned to Dar al-Harb and came back the same day, 'ushr will be taken again because he comes with a new aman, and taking 'ushr after that does not lead to total depletion.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the action of Caliph Umar (RA). The issue is whether a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) can be subjected to 'ushr (tithe) multiple times within the same year if he passes the customs officer repeatedly without returning to Dar al-Harb. The Hanafi ruling is that 'ushr is taken only once per year as long as the same aman (safe conduct) is in effect. The proof is the instruction of Umar to his officer: 'If you have taken 'ushr once, do not take it again.' This ensures the harbi's property is not entirely depleted, since 'ushr is justified by the protection granted. However, if the harbi remains in Dar al-Islam for a full year, the aman is considered renewed, and 'ushr is taken again for the new year. A special case is when the harbi returns to Dar al-Harb and comes back the same day; this constitutes a new aman, so 'ushr is taken again even within the same year, and there is no depletion because he left and returned voluntarily. The passage also resolves an apparent contradiction in the Hidayah regarding the possibility of a harbi staying for a full year; the relied-upon position is that a harbi is not allowed to stay for more than a year unless he becomes a dhimmi.

Key Terms
عشر (ʿushr): A tithe (10%) taken from the property of a harbi or dhimmi when they bring goods into Dar al-Islam for trade.
حربي (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim from enemy territory (Dar al-Harb) who does not have a permanent covenant with the Islamic state.
أمان (amān): A pledge of safety granted to a harbi, allowing him to enter Dar al-Islam for a limited period.
استیصال (istiṣāl): Complete depletion or extermination of property, which is to be avoided when levying 'ushr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A harbi trader pays 'ushr to the 'ashir in January. He stays in Dar al-Islam without returning to Dar al-Harb. In August of the same year, he passes the 'ashir again with new goods. According to the Hanafi ruling based on Umar's instruction, what should the 'ashir do?
A) Take 'ushr again because it is a new transaction.
B) Not take 'ushr until the next year because the same aman is still valid.
C) Take double 'ushr because he did not leave.
D) Take only half 'ushr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that 'ushr is taken once per aman period; a new aman (by leaving and returning to Dar al-Harb) allows a new levy, but within the same continuous stay, repeated 'ushr is prohibited.

Ushr on Wine and Pork: The Hanafi Protection Rationale
Dispute on taxation of a dhimmi's wine and pork

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on 'ushr for a dhimmi's wine and pork, explain the protection rationale, and distinguish between the views of al-Shafi'i, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Wine is taxed because Muslims protect it for vinegar; pork is not taxed because it must be destroyed.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical tax scenario: A dhimmi merchant passes the customs officer ('ashir) carrying wine or pork. The Hanafi school holds a nuanced position that differentiates between the two, based on the principle of state protection (himayah) and the nature of the goods. We will dissect the arguments of the various imams to understand why wine is taxable but pork is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Recognize that a dhimmi passes with wine or pork. The relied-upon Hanafi ruling (zahir al-riwayah) is that 'ushr is taken on wine (by valuing it) but not on pork.
The phrase 'عُشِرَ الْخَمْرُ' means from its value (قيمة).
2
Contrast Hanafi with Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i holds that neither wine nor pork has legal value in Islam, so no 'ushr is taken. The Hanafi response distinguishes by the protection rationale.
3
Analyze intra-Hanafi differences
Imam Zufar holds both are taxable because they are considered property by dhimmis. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if carried together, both are taxable (pork as subsidiary); if separately, only wine.
Zufar and Abu Yusuf are within the Hanafi school but their views are not the relied-upon (mufta bihi).
4
Grasp the two key rationales
First, the mithli/qimi distinction: wine is a fungible (mithli) and 'ushr is taken on its value; pork is a unique item (qimi) but the protection principle overrides. Second, the protection principle: Muslims protect their own wine for making vinegar, so they protect it for others; they do not protect pork—it must be destroyed.
This is the wajh al-farq (reason for distinction) stated in the text.
5
Apply the protection principle
The mufta bihi (fatwa) position is to tax wine but not pork, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This resolves the practical scenario faced by a Hanafi 'ashir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ مَرَّ ذِمِيٌّ بِخَمْرٍ أَوْ خِنْزِيرٍ عُشِرَ الْخَمْرُ دُونَ الْخِنْزِيرِ وَقَوْلُهُ عُشِرَ الْخَمْرُ أَيْ مِنْ قِيمَتِهَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يُعَشِّرُهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ لَا قِيمَةَ لَهُمَا وَقَالَ زُفَرُ يُعَشِّرُهُمَا لِاسْتِوَائِهِمَا فِي الْمَالِيَّةِ عِنْدَهُمْ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يُعَشِّرُهُمَا إِذَا مَرَّ بِهَا جُمْلَةً كَأَنَّهُ جَعَلَ الْخِنْزِيرَ تَبَعًا لِلْخَمْرِ فَإِنْ مَرَّ بِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ عَلَى الِانْفِرَادِ عُشِرَ الْخَمْرُ دُونَ الْخِنْزِيرِ وَوَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ عَلَى الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ الْقِيمَةَ فِي ذَوَاتِ الْقِيَمِ لَهَا حُكْمُ الْعَيْنِ وَالْخِنْزِيرُ مِنْهَا وَذَوَاتُ الْأَمْثَالِ لَيْسَ لَهَا هَذَا الْحُكْمُ وَالْخَمْرُ مِنْهَا وَلِأَنَّ حَقَّ الْأَخْذِ لِلْحِمَايَةِ وَالْمُسْلِمُ يَحْمِلُ خَمْرَ نَفْسِهِ لِلتَّخْلِيلِ فَكَذَا يَحْمِيهَا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ وَلَا يُحْمَى خِنْزِيرُ نَفْسِهِ بَلْ يَجِبُ قَتْلُهُ بِالْإِسْلَامِ فَكَذَا لَا يُحْمِيهِ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ
And if a dhimmi passes with wine or pork, 'ushr is taken on the wine, not on the pork. His statement 'ushr on wine' means from its value. Al-Shafi'i said: 'Do not take 'ushr on both because they have no value.' Zufar said: 'Take 'ushr on both because they are equal in being considered property among the disbelievers.' Abu Yusuf said: 'Take 'ushr on both when he passes with them together, as if he made the pork a follow-up to the wine. But if he passes with each individually, 'ushr is taken on the wine, not on the pork. The reason for the distinction according to the apparent [relied-upon] position is that value in items of value has the ruling of the specific item itself, and pork is among them; while fungible items (mithliyyat) do not have this ruling, and wine is among them. Also, because the right to take is for protection, and a Muslim protects his own wine for making vinegar, so he protects it for others as well; but he does not protect his own pork — rather it must be killed (destroyed) by Islam — so likewise he does not protect it for others.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-party dispute regarding the imposition of 'ushr on wine and pork when a dhimmi carries them for trade. The relied-upon Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) holds that 'ushr is taken on wine by valuing it, but not on pork. The reason is that wine, although haram for Muslims, can be used for making vinegar, so it has potential lawful use; Muslims protect their own wine for this purpose. Therefore, the state can also protect it and levy 'ushr. Pork, on the other hand, has no lawful use for Muslims; it must be destroyed. Since Muslims do not protect their own pork, they do not protect it for others. Additionally, wine is a fungible (mithli) item, so 'ushr is taken on its value, not on the specific substance. Pork is a unique item (qimi) but the rationale of protection does not apply. Imam al-Shafi'i rejects 'ushr on both because they have no value in Islamic law. Imam Zufar says both are subject to 'ushr because the disbelievers consider both as property. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if carried together, both are taxed (pork as subsidiary to wine); if carried separately, only wine is taxed.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living permanently under the protection of the Islamic state, subject to jizyah and other rules.
قيمة (qīmah): Value; here, 'ushr is taken as 10% of the value of wine, not of the substance itself.
ذوات القيم (dhawāt al-qiyam): Non-fungible items that are unique and valued individually, like animals or pork.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawāt al-amthāl): Fungible items that can be replaced by similar ones, like wine (by volume).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, why is 'ushr taken on a dhimmi's wine but not on his pork?
A) Because wine is a fungible item and pork is not.
B) Because Muslims protect wine for making vinegar but do not protect pork.
C) Because wine is more valuable than pork.
D) Because the dhimmi owns wine but not pork.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between taxing wine and not taxing pork rests on the principle of state protection (himayah), which is based on the potential lawful use of wine (for vinegar) and the obligation to destroy pork.

Harbi's Ushr Upon Returning from Dar al-Harb
Ruling on tithe for harbi trader returning same day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of 'ushr for a harbi who re-enters Dar al-Islam after returning to Dar al-Harb and explain the legal basis of a new aman.

Core Idea
Returning to Dar al-Harb nullifies the aman; a new entry requires a new tithe.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah addresses a specific case: a harbi trader who has already paid 'ushr, then returns to Dar al-Harb, and comes back the very same day. The Hanafi ruling is that he must pay 'ushr again. This might seem repetitive, but the reasoning hinges on the nature of the aman contract, which is terminated by returning to hostile territory. Understanding this principle clarifies why the obligation is renewed and also addresses the concern that repeated tithes could completely deplete the trader's wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific scenario? A harbi trader who has already been tithed returns to Dar al-Harb and then re-enters Dar al-Islam on the same day. The ruling is that 'ushr is taken again.
The ruling is specific to the harbi's re-entry, not a general rule for all entries.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text gives the reason: 'because he returned with a new aman' (لأنه رجع بأمان جديد). This is the core proof – the first aman ended when he went back to Dar al-Harb.
This is a qiyas-based reasoning: new aman equals new obligation.
3
Address the potential objection
The text preempts an objection: repeated tithes might lead to complete depletion (استيصال) of wealth. It responds that taking tithe after that does not lead to depletion because each entry is a separate obligation.
This shows the Hanafi concern for fairness – the ruling does not cause unjust harm.
4
Note the Hanafi position's authority
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is presented without internal dispute, making it the mufta bihi position. However, other schools may differ on whether the aman is truly terminated by a brief return.
The cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih', meaning there is legitimate difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پورا ہو کر دوسرا سال شروع ہو جائے تو دوبارہ عشر لیا جائے گا اس عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے حربی ایک سال سے زائد دار الاسلام میں قیام کر سکتا ہے اور اگر آگے چل کر لا يمكن من المقام الاحولا ، کہا اور لفظ الا غلط ہے جیسا کہ بیان ہوا تو مطلب یہ ہوا کہ حربی کو ایک سال ٹھہبر نے پر قابو نہیں دیا گیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حربی ایک سال تک دارالاسلام میں ٹھہرارہا اور امام کو اس کے حال کا علم نہیں ہو سکا تو ایسی صورت میں اس سے دوبارہ عشر لے لیا جائے گا۔
عشر لیا گیا پھر وہ دارالحرب چلا گیا دوبارہ عاشر پر گذرا تو پھر عشر لیا جائے گا
وَإِنْ عَشَّرَهُ فَرَجَعَ إِلى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنْ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ عَشَرَهُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ رَجَعَ بِأَمَانِ جَدِيدٍ وَكَذَا الْأَخْدَ بعدَهُ لَا يُفْضِي إِلَى الاسْتِيُصَال
ترجمہ اور اگر اس سے عشر لے لیا پھر وہ دارالحرب کی طرف واپس چلا گیا، پھر وہ اسی روز واپس آ گیا تو بھی اس سے عشر لے گا کیونکہ وہ جدید امان کے ساتھ آیا ہے اور یونہی اس کے بعد عشر لینا استیصال کی جانب مفضی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عاشر نے حربی تاجر سے عشر لے لیا پھر وہ حربی تاجر دار الحرب جا کر اسی دن واپس آ گیا تو ان سے دوبارہ عشر لیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ حربی جب دار الحرب جا کر واپس آیا تو نئے امان کے ساتھ آیا ہے پس اس نئے امان کی وجہ سے اس سے دوبارہ عشر وصول کیا جائے گا۔ اور دار الحرب جا کر واپس آنے کے بعد عشر لینا استبلاک مال کا بھی سبب نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی دوبارہ عشر لینے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
(Urdu explanation:) When a full year passes and the second year begins, then tithe will be taken again. From this expression it is understood that a harbi can reside in Dar al-Islam for more than one year... (Arabic:) And if he was tithed, then he returned to Dar al-Harb, then he came out that very day, he is tithed again because he returned with a new aman. And likewise, taking tithe after that does not lead to complete depletion.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the tithe on a harbi trader who returns to Dar al-Harb and comes back the same day. The key principle is that upon returning to Dar al-Harb, the previous aman is considered terminated. When he re-enters Dar al-Islam, he does so with a new aman, which justifies levying the tithe again. The text also addresses a potential objection that repeated tithes would deplete his wealth entirely (استيصال), stating that this is not the case because the tithe is only due upon each new entry with a new aman. The Hanafi position is clear: each new entry triggers a new obligation of 'ushr, regardless of how frequent.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under a covenant (dhimmi) and is from a hostile territory (Dar al-Harb).
عشر (ushr): A tithe of one-tenth levied on goods brought by a non-Muslim trader entering Dar al-Islam.
امان (aman): A safe conduct or guarantee of protection granted to a non-Muslim entering Dar al-Islam temporarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a harbi trader tithed again if he returns to Dar al-Harb and comes back the same day?
A) Because his goods have increased in value.
B) Because he is considered a new entrant with a new aman.
C) Because the first tithe was invalid.
D) Because the imam can take tithe arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a harbi's 'ushr is tied to the aman; a return to Dar al-Harb nullifies the aman, so a fresh entry triggers a fresh obligation to pay 'ushr.

Tithe on Dhimmi's Wine and Pigs: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on tithe from dhimmi carrying wine or pigs with multiple opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tithe for a dhimmi's wine and pigs, distinguish it from the positions of al-Shafi'i, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf, and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
Tithe on a dhimmi's wine is wajib; on a pig, it is not — because the pig's value is like the pig itself, which Muslims cannot own.

When a dhimmi trader passes a customs station ('ashir') with wine and pigs, is the tithe (ushr) due? The Hanafi school answers: only on the wine, not the pig. But other imams differ. This lesson unpacks the dispute, focusing on the Hanafi reasoning based on the distinction between qimi and mithli property and the concept of protection (himayah). Understanding this case sharpens your ability to apply usul categories to real rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core issue: are a dhimmi's wine and pigs subject to tithe (ushr) when they cross an 'ashir? This is a question of trade tax on non-Muslim subjects.
The tithe is a 10% levy on trade goods of dhimmis as compensation for state protection.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The zahir al-riwayah (reliable narration) holds that wine is tithed by its value, but pig is not. The proof is twofold: (1) qimi vs. mithli distinction — pigs are qimi (value is like the actual pig, which cannot be owned by Muslims), so taking value is like taking the pig itself; wine is mithli, so value is separate and permissible. (2) The basis of tithe is protection (himayah): Muslims protect wine (for lawful vinegar) but not pigs (must be abandoned).
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the 'two').
3
Contrast with opposing schools
Al-Shafi'i: neither is tithed because they have no value in Islam. Zufar: both are tithed because non-Muslims consider them property. Abu Yusuf: if carried together, both tithed (pig as follower); if separate, only wine tithed.
Abu Yusuf and Zufar are Hanafi themselves, but their views are weaker (marjuh).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to objections
The Hanafi response: property status from non-Muslims is not the basis; Islamic protection is. Zufar's objection (equal property value) is rebutted by noting that protection is not granted to pigs. Shafi'i's objection (no value in Islam) is rebutted by the qimi/mithli distinction — wine may have no intrinsic value but its value is separate (mithli) and thus can be taken.
The tarjih is clear: the position of the 'two' is the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the mufta bihi Hanafi view: only wine is tithed. Under Shafi'i: neither. Under Zufar: both. Under Abu Yusuf: both if together, wine only if separate. The fatwa in the Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
In practice, a Hanafi judge would rule: 'Tithe on wine, not on pig.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ مَرَّ ذِمِيٌّ بِخَمْرٍ اَوْ خِنْزِيرٍ عُشِرَ الْحَمُرُ دُونَ الْخِنْزِيرِ وَقَوْلُهُ عُشَرَ الْخَمْرُ أَي مِنْ قِيمَتِهَا وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعُى لَا يُعَشِرُهُمَا لأَنَّهُ لَا قِيْمَةَ لَهُمَا وَ قَالَ زُفُرُ يُعَشِّرُهُمَا لِإِسْتِوَائِهِمَا فِى الْمَالِيَّةِ عِندَهُمْ وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوْسُفَ يُعَشِرُهُمَا إِذَا مَرَّبِهَا جُمْلَةً كَأَنَّهُ جَعَلَ الْخِنْزِيرَ تَبْعًا لِلْخَمْرِ فَإِنْ مَرَّ بِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ عَلَى الْإِنْفِرَادِ عُشِرَ الْخَمْرُ دُونَ الْخِنْزِيرَ وَ وَجْهُ الْفَرَقِ عَلَى الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ الْقِيْمَةَ فِى ذَوَاتِ الْقِيمِ لَهَا حُكْمُ الْعَيْنِ وَالخِنْزِيرُ مِنْهَا وَ ذَوَاتُ الْأَمْثَالِ لَيْسَ لَهَا هَذَا الْحُكْمُ وَالْحَمُرُ مِنْهَا وَلَانَّ حَقَّ الْاَحْدِ  ِللحِمَايَةِ وَالْمُسْلِمُ يُحْمِلْ خَمْرَ نَفْسِهِ لِلتَّخْلِيلِ فَكَذَا يُحْمِيْهَا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ وَلَا يُحْمَى خِنْزِيرَ نَفْسِهِ بَلْ يَجِبُ تَسُهُ بِالْإِسْلَام فَكَذَا لَا يُحْمِيهِ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ
And if a dhimmi passes with wine or pig, the wine is tithed but not the pig. And his saying 'the wine is tithed' means from its value. And al-Shafi'i said: He does not tithe both because there is no value for them. And Zufar said: He tithes both because they are equal in property value according to them (the non-Muslims). And Abu Yusuf said: He tithes both when he passes with them together, as if he made the pig a follower of the wine; but if he passes with each separately, the wine is tithed and not the pig. And the distinguishing reason according to the apparent (narration) is that value (price) in things of value (qimi) has the ruling of the thing itself, and the pig is among them; while things of measurement (mithli) do not have this ruling, and wine is among them. And because the right of taking (tithe) is for protection, and the Muslim protects his own wine for making vinegar, so likewise he protects it for others; but he does not protect his own pig, rather it is obligatory to abandon it upon Islam, so likewise he does not protect it for others.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the tithe (ushr) on a dhimmi trader's goods that include wine and pigs. The Hanafi position (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the 'two' or 'طرفين') is that wine is tithed (by its value) but pig is not. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that neither is tithed because they have no value in Islamic law. Imam Zufar holds that both are tithed because non-Muslims consider them valuable property. Imam Abu Yusuf makes a distinction: if they are carried together, both are tithed (pig as a follower of wine); if separately, only wine is tithed. The Hanafi reasoning (from the 'apparent' i.e., Zahir al-Riwayah) is based on a distinction between qimi (items valued by price) and mithli (items measured by weight/volume). Pigs are qimi, so their value is like the actual pig, which cannot be owned by Muslims, so no tithe on pig. Wine is mithli, so its value is not like the actual wine, so it can be tithed by value. Additionally, the right to tithe is based on protection (himayah). Since Muslims protect their own wine (for lawful use like vinegar), they protect others' wine too, entitling them to tithe it. But they do not protect pigs (must abandon them), so no tithe on pigs.

Key Terms
ذوات القیم (dhawat al-qimah): Items that are evaluated by their market price (qimi), meaning they are not measured by weight or volume (mithli).
ذوات الامثال (dhawat al-amthal): Items that are measured by weight, volume, or count (mithli), such that one unit is interchangeable with another.
حمایت (himayah): Protection or safeguard; the basis for the right to levy tithe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on tithe from a dhimmi carrying only a pig?
A) The pig is tithed by its value.
B) The pig is tithed only if carried with wine.
C) No tithe is taken on the pig.
D) The pig is tithed only if its value exceeds 200 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school tithes a dhimmi's wine (by value) but not pigs, based on the qimi/mithli distinction and the principle of protection (himayah).

Dispute on Taking Ushr from Dhimmi's Wine and Pig
Explains four positions on taxing dhimmi's wine and pig

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi positions on taking 'ushr from a dhimmi's wine and pig, and explain the reasoning behind the sideen's preferred view.

Core Idea
The sideen rule: 'ushr on wine (dhawat al-amthal) but not on pig (dhawat al-qim).

This passage from the commentary of al-Hidayah presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on taxing a dhimmi merchant's wine and pig. The four positions reflect different applications of qiyas and istihsan. Understanding the distinction between dhawat al-qim and dhawat al-amthal is crucial to grasping the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four positions
List each position: sideen, Shafi'i, Zufar, Abu Yusuf. Note the ruling each gives.
The sideen are Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the sideen's first proof
Understand the distinction between dhawat al-qim (pig) and dhawat al-amthal (wine) and why it leads to different rulings.
Dhawat al-qim: taking the price equals taking the item itself.
3
Examine the protection argument
The sideen argue that 'ushr is compensation for protection. Muslims protect wine (for vinegar) but must abandon pig, so they do not protect pig.
This is a second independent proof.
4
Compare with opposing views
See how Shafi'i, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf differ and their proofs.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on taba'iyya (subordination).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The sideen's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
Al-Marghinani presents it as the primary view in al-Hidayah.

میں ایسا نہیں ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ مکاتب کے پاس اگر شمر اور خنزیر ہوں اور وہ بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا تو خمر مولی کی ملک ہو جائے گا لیکن خنزیر مولی کی ملک نہ ہوگا اور بسا اوقات شئی تبعا ثابت ہو دینا واجب ہے تو وہ دوسرے کے خنازیر کی حفاظت بھی نہیں کرے گا۔ پس جب خنازیر کی حفاظت نہیں پائی گئی تو ان کا عشر بھی نہ لیا جائے۔
Book of Zakat: ... He protects for others, but not his own pig, rather due to being Muslim leaving it is wajib, so similarly he will not protect for others. Explanation: The issue is that if a dhimmi passes by the tax collector with wine or pig or both intending trade and its value reaches two hundred dirhams, then there are four sayings: (1) According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), one-tenth is taken from the value of wine, but the ushr of pig is not taken. (2) According to Imam Shafi'i, ushr of neither is taken. (3) According to Imam Zufar, the tax collector takes ushr of both wine and pig. (4) According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the rule is that if the dhimmi merchant passes with both together, the tax collector takes ushr of both; if he passes separately, ushr of wine is taken and ushr of pig is not. ...
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of al-Hidayah presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imposition of 'ushr (tithe) on a dhimmi merchant who passes a tax collector with wine and/or pig. The four positions are clearly delineated: (1) the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) allows 'ushr on wine but not on pig; (2) Imam al-Shafi'i denies 'ushr on both due to lack of legal value; (3) Imam Zufar obligates 'ushr on both because they are considered property among non-Muslims; (4) Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on whether the items are carried together or separately, applying a principle of subordination (taba'iyya). The commentary then provides the evidence for each position, including the Shafi'i argument that wine and pig lack property value (maliat), Zufar's argument that they are property for dhimmis, Abu Yusuf's nuanced view based on the subordination of pig to wine, and finally the sideen's dual reasoning: first, that pig belongs to the category of dhawat al-qim (valuables) where taking its price is equivalent to taking the pig itself, which is forbidden for Muslims, while wine belongs to dhawat al-amthal (fungibles) where taking its price is not like taking the wine itself; second, the 'ushr is due in exchange for protection, and Muslims protect wine (for conversion to vinegar) but are obliged to abandon pig, hence they do not provide protection for pig. The passage illustrates the sophisticated qiyas and istihsan used by Hanafi jurists.

Key Terms
عشر (‘ushr): A tenth tax levied on trade goods of dhimmis passing through Muslim territory.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection, subject to jizya and certain regulations.
خمر (khamr): Alcoholic wine; legally impure and forbidden for Muslims.
خنزير (khinzīr): Pig; considered najis and haram for Muslims; has no monetary value in Islamic law.
ذوات القيم (dhawāt al-qiyam): Valuables: goods that are unique and not fungible; taking their price is equivalent to taking them.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawāt al-amthāl): Fungibles: goods that can be replaced by similar ones; taking their price is not equivalent to taking them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sideen (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on taking 'ushr from a dhimmi's pig?
A) 'Ushr is taken from both wine and pig.
B) 'Ushr is taken from pig only.
C) 'Ushr is taken from wine but not from pig.
D) 'Ushr is taken from neither.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between wine (dhawat al-amthal) and pig (dhawat al-qim) in 'ushr: 'ushr is taken on wine value but not on pig because taking the pig's price is like taking the pig itself, which is haram.

Ruling on Child and Woman from Banu Taghlib Passing with Goods
States ruling on 'ushr liability for a minor and woman from Banu Taghlib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'ushr liability for a minor and an adult woman from Banu Taghlib when passing a tax collector, and explain the basis for the minor's exemption.

Core Idea
A minor from Banu Taghlib owes no 'ushr; an adult woman owes the same double rate as a man.

Banu Taghlib are a Christian Arab tribe who, under Hanafi law, pay double the 'ushr rate of Muslims instead of jizya. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that this obligation applies to adults regardless of gender, but minors are exempt entirely because they are not legally accountable (mukallaf). The ruling reinforces two important principles: the significance of legal capacity in taxation and the equal treatment of men and women in financial obligations under Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects
Note the two categories mentioned: a minor child (صبي) and a woman (امرأة) from Banu Taghlib who are passing a tax collector with goods.
The text uses 'صبي' for a minor and 'امرأة' for a woman.
2
Recall the general rule for Banu Taghlib
Banu Taghlib pay double the 'ushr of Muslims, a rule established earlier in the chapter on grazing animals (باب السوائم). This rate applies to adult men.
The double rate is in lieu of jizya.
3
Apply the rule to each case
For the minor: no 'ushr is due because they are not mukallaf (legally responsible). For the woman: she must pay the same amount as a man – double 'ushr.
The ruling for the woman shows that gender does not affect liability.
4
Note the cross-reference
The text refers back to باب السوائم for the detailed proof. This cross-reference reinforces that the rate is established and consistent.
The cross-reference is a common feature in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہنو تغلب کا بچہ اور عورت عاشر پر گذرے تو کیا لازم ہے
مَرَّ صَبِيٌّ أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ مِنْ بَنِي تَعْلِبَ بِمَالٍ فَلَيْسَ عَلَى الصَّبِيِّ شَيْءٌ وَعَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ مَا عَلَى الرَّجُلِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا فِي بَابِ السَّوَائِمِ
ترجمہ اور اگر بنو تغلب کا بچہ یا عورت مال لے کر گذری۔ تو بچہ پر کچھ نہیں ہے۔ اور عورت پر اس قدر ہے جو مرد پر ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو باب سوائم میں گذر چکی۔
تشریح مسئله عاشر کے پاس سے مال لے کر بنو تغلب کا نا بالغ بچہ گذرا یا عورت گذری تو بچہ پر عشر وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ البتہ عورت پر اس قدر واجب ہوگا جو تعلبی مرد پر واجب ہوتا ہے یعنی مسلمانوں سے دو چند دلائل باب السوائم میں بیان ہو چکے ہیں وہاں ملاحظہ فرمائیں ۔
What is obligatory when a child or woman of Banu Taghlib passes the tax collector? ... If a boy or woman from Banu Taghlib passes with goods, then there is nothing on the boy, and on the woman what is on the man, due to what we mentioned in the chapter of grazing animals. Explanation: ...
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the hidayah. Banu Taghlib are a Christian tribe who pay double the 'ushr of Muslims (as established in earlier chapters). Here, two specific exemptions/affirmations are given: a minor (non-baligh) child from Banu Taghlib is not liable for any 'ushr when passing the tax collector, because they are not legally responsible. An adult woman, however, is liable to the same amount as an adult Taghlibi man, which is double the 'ushr of a Muslim. The reasoning is referenced to the earlier discussion in the chapter on grazing animals (bab al-sawa'im), where the rate for Banu Taghlib was set at double that of Muslims. This shows that gender does not affect the tax liability for adult dhimmis; both men and women owe the same amount.

Key Terms
بني تغلب (Banū Taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe residing in Muslim territory, subject to double 'ushr instead of jizya.
صبي (ṣabiyy): A minor child who has not reached puberty; not legally accountable (mukallaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a minor boy from Banu Taghlib passes a tax collector with trade goods, what 'ushr is due?
A) Half the normal 'ushr
B) Double the normal 'ushr
C) No 'ushr is due
D) The same as for an adult woman

Key Takeaway
Banu Taghlib adults (men and women) owe double 'ushr; minors owe nothing.

Ruling on Passing with 100 Dirhams While Having Another 100 at Home
Explains that no 'ushr is taken when goods are below nisab and home goods are not under protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for 'ushr obligation on trade goods and apply them to scenarios where goods are split between transit and home.

Core Idea
Goods below nisab incur no 'ushr; goods at home are outside the tax collector's protection.

This short passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a common scenario: a merchant passes a tax checkpoint carrying less than the nisab (200 dirhams) while having additional goods at home. The ruling highlights two fundamental principles: the nisab threshold and the requirement that goods must physically come under the collector's protection (himaya) for 'ushr to be levied. Understanding these conditions prevents confusion about whether home goods can be combined with carried goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the merchant doing? Passing a tax collector with 100 dirhams of goods. What is the ruling? The collector takes nothing.
Not even from the home goods.
2
List the conditions for 'ushr obligation
In Hanafi fiqh, 'ushr on trade goods requires: (1) the goods reach nisab (200 dirhams or equivalent), (2) a full lunar year (hawl) passes, (3) the goods physically pass through the checkpoint and come under the collector's protection.
Nisab is also a condition for zakat, but here the checkpoint adds the himaya condition.
3
Apply conditions to each portion
Carried 100 dirhams: less than nisab, so no 'ushr. Home 100 dirhams: not physically present at checkpoint, so not under himaya, hence no 'ushr.
The home goods are not combined with carried goods for nisab because they are not under the same protection.
4
Derive the legal principle
The tax collector's protection (himaya) is limited to goods that physically pass him. Goods not passing him are outside his jurisdiction, even if they would complete nisab when aggregated.
This prevents the collector from claiming tax on goods never brought within his control.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کوئی شخص عاشر پر سود را ہم لے کر گذرا اور اس نے کہا کہ سودراہم میرے گھر میں ہیں تو عاشر صرف سو دراہم کی زکوۃ وصول کرے گا
مَنْ مَرَّ عَلَى عَاشِرٍ بِمِائَةِ دِرْهَمٍ وَأَخْبَرَهُ أَنَّ لَهُ فِي مَنْزِلِهِ مِائَةً أُخْرَى قَدْ حَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَوْلُ لَمْ يَأْخُذْ الَّتِي مَرَّ بِهَا لِقِلَّتِهَا وَمَا فِي بَيْتِهِ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ تَحْتَ حِمَايَتِهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی ایک سو درہم لے کر عاشر کے پاس سے گزرا اور عاشر کو خبر دی کہ میرے گھر میں دوسرے سو درہم ہیں کہ اس پر بھی سال گذر گیا ہے تو عاشر ان سو درہم کی زکوۃ نہ لے گا جن کو ساتھ لے کر گذرا ہے کیونکہ وہ قلیل ہیں اور جو اس کے گھر میں ہیں وہ عاشر کی حفاظت میں داخل نہیں ہوئے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص ایک سو درہم کے ساتھ عاشر کے پاس سے گزرا اور اس نے عاشر کو بتا یا کہ ایک سو درہم میرے گھر میں ہیں اور دونوں پر سال گزر گیا ہے تو عاشر نہ ان سو دراہم کی زکوۃ لے گا جن کو ساتھ لے کر وہ گذرا ہے اور نہ ان کی جو اس کے گھر میں ہیں کیونکہ جو درہم اس کے ساتھ ہیں وہ تو نصاب سے کم ہیں۔ اور جو اس کے گھر میں ہیں وہ عاشر کی حمایت اور حفاظت میں نہیں آئے ۔ اور چونکہ نصاب سے کم میں زکوۃ وعشر واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ اس لئے ان ایک سو دراہم میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی جن کو لے کر وہ عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا ہے اور جو عاشر کی حمایت میں داخل نہ ہوں ان میں زکوۃ لینے کا حق عاشر کو نہیں ہوتا ۔ اس لئے ان کی زکوۃ بھی عاشر نہ لے گا۔
If someone passes the tax collector with one hundred dirhams and informed him that he has another hundred in his house which a full year has passed, he does not take the one he passed with because of its smallness, and what is in his house has not come under his protection. ...
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This ruling clarifies a specific scenario: A person passing a tax collector (ashir) carries 100 dirhams of trade goods and informs the collector that he has another 100 dirhams at home, both have been in his possession for a full year (hawl). The tax collector cannot collect zakat (here 'ushr) from either amount. The reason is twofold: The 100 dirhams being carried are less than the nisab (which is 200 dirhams for cash/goods), so no zakat is due on them individually. The 100 dirhams at home, although when combined with the carried amount would reach nisab, are not under the protection (himaya) of the tax collector because they are not physically with the person during the crossing. The tax collector's jurisdiction extends only to goods that pass through his checkpoint. Therefore, neither amount is subject to 'ushr. The commentary emphasizes that the collector only collects on goods that come under his direct protection during transit.

Key Terms
عاشر (‘āshir): The tax collector responsible for collecting 'ushr from merchants passing through checkpoints.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum threshold for zakat/‘ushr liability, here 200 dirhams for trade goods.
حمایت (ḥimāyat): Protection; the 'ashir provides protection to goods passing through, which is the basis for collecting 'ushr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the tax collector not take 'ushr from the 100 dirhams at home?
A) Because it is less than nisab
B) Because it has not come under the tax collector's protection
C) Because the owner did not declare it
D) Because it has not completed a full year

Key Takeaway
The obligation of 'ushr on trade goods requires both nisab (200 dirhams) and physical passage under the tax collector's protection.

Merchant's Authorization Exempts Trade Goods from 'Ushr
Ruling on exemption from 'ushr for authorized merchants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that exempts a merchant from paying 'ushr on trade goods at a checkpoint and apply the ruling to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Authorization to pay zakat elsewhere exempts trade goods from local 'ushr collection.

This lesson presents a key exception in Hanafi zakat law. While 'ushr is generally collected on trade goods passing through a checkpoint, the collector must refrain if the merchant has authorization to pay zakat elsewhere. Understanding this ruling prevents double taxation and clarifies the interaction between local and central zakat administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
A merchant passes a checkpoint with trade goods (bida'ah). What is the tax collector's action according to the text?
The ruling is that the collector does NOT take 'ushr.
2
Identify the condition
What specific condition triggers this exception? Find the Arabic term for 'authorized' and understand its significance.
Condition: the merchant is ma'dhun (authorized) to pay zakat elsewhere.
3
Understand the rationale
Why does the Hanafi school allow this exception? Consider the purpose of 'ushr as a zakat collection mechanism.
Rationale: to prevent double taxation and respect delegation of zakat payment.
4
Apply to a contrasting case
What would the ruling be if the merchant had no authorization? State the default rule.
Without authorization, the collector must take 'ushr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کوئی شخص عاشر پر دو سو دراہم بضاعت کے لے کر گذرا اس سے عشر نہیں لیا جائے گا
فَلَوْ مَرَّ بِمِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ بِضَاعَةً لَمْ يُعَشِّرْهَا لِأَنَّهُ مَأْذُونٌ بِأَدَاءِ زَكَاتِهَا

If someone passed with two hundred dirhams as trade goods, he does not pay 'ushr on them because he is authorized to pay its zakat.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This short ruling presents an exception to the general rule that a tax collector can take 'ushr from trade goods passing through his checkpoint. If the merchant has authorization (ma'dhun) from the authorities to pay the zakat on those goods in his own town or to the proper authorities elsewhere, then the 'ashir does not take 'ushr. This prevents double taxation. The rationale is that the 'ushr is essentially a zakat collection mechanism for trade goods, and if the obligation is already being fulfilled elsewhere, the local collector should not interfere. The merchant must have explicit permission or a system in place for paying zakat at his place of residence.

Key Terms
بضاعة (biḍā‘ah): Trade goods, merchandise, specifically for commercial purposes.
مأذون (ma’dhūn): Authorized; here meaning the merchant has permission or a mandate to pay zakat on these goods elsewhere, so the tax collector refrains.

Key Takeaway
The 'ashir may not collect 'ushr if the merchant has a valid authorization to pay zakat elsewhere.

Banu Taghlib Child and Woman Passing the 'Ashir
States the ruling for child and woman of Banu Taghlib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat liability for a child and a woman of Banu Taghlib when passing the 'ashir, and explain the basis of the treaty.

Core Idea
Minor child exempt; woman pays double—treaty binds Banu Taghlib adults.

The passage from al-Hidayah presents a specific ruling for the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib. While Muslims pay standard zakat, Banu Taghlib agreed to pay double. This lesson focuses on two categories: a minor boy and a woman. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct application at the 'ashir checkpoint.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The passage distinguishes between a boy (sabi) and a woman (imra'ah) from Banu Taghlib. Determine their legal status for zakat.
The child is not mukallaf (legally responsible); the woman is an adult.
2
Apply the treaty rule
Banu Taghlib agreed to pay double the zakat rate of Muslims. This is a fixed treaty obligation for adults.
3
Determine liability for the child
The passage states 'nothing is due from the boy' because he is not obligated to pay zakat due to lack of legal capacity.
This is consistent with general Hanafi rule: minors are not liable for zakat.
4
Determine liability for the woman
The woman must pay the same as a man of Banu Taghlib, which is double the Muslim rate. The proof is referenced from the chapter on grazing animals.
The proof likely addresses the treaty terms; for women, the obligation is the same as for men in this context.
5
Note the specificity
This ruling is exclusive to Banu Taghlib due to their treaty; other dhimmis may have different arrangements (e.g., jizya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَرَّ صَبِيٌّ أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ مِنْ بَنِي تَغْلِبَ بِمَالٍ فَلَيْسَ عَلَى الصَّبِيِّ شَيْءٌ وَعَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ مَا عَلَى الرَّجُلِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا فِي بَابِ السَّوَائِمِ
If a boy or a woman from Banu Taghlib passes with wealth, then nothing is due from the boy, and on the woman what is due on the man, for what we mentioned in the chapter on grazing animals.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Zakat in al-Hidayah. It addresses the case of a minor boy or a woman from the Christian tribe Banu Taghlib passing by the tax collector (ashir) with trade goods. The ruling: the boy pays nothing because he is not liable for zakat. The woman pays double the amount that a Muslim man would pay, as Banu Taghlib agreed to pay double the zakat of Muslims. The proof is referenced from the earlier section on grazing animals (Bab al-Sawa'im).

Key Terms
عاشر (al-ashir): The tax collector appointed by the state to collect zakat and 'ushr from passing merchants.
بنو تغلب (Banu Taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe that agreed to pay double the zakat of Muslims as part of their treaty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only half of what a Muslim man would pay.

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Zakat Collection When Wealth is Split Between Traveler and Home
Ruling on zakat collection when wealth is split between person and home.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that prevent the 'ashir from collecting zakat: (1) wealth must reach the nisab and (2) wealth must be under the 'ashir's physical protection.

Core Idea
Zakat is collected only on full nisab under the 'ashir's physical control.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario where a traveler carrying less than nisab informs the tax collector (ˈāshir) of additional wealth at home. The ruling teaches the precise limits of the 'āshir's authority: he cannot collect on wealth that is below nisab or beyond his reach. Understanding this ruling clarifies two foundational principles in Hanafi zakat law: the necessity of complete nisab being present with the payer, and the requirement of territorial/physical control for collection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The traveler has 100 dirhams with him (below the silver nisab of 200 dirhams) and another 100 dirhams at home that have been in his possession for one full year. He informs the 'ashir of both amounts.
Focus on the two separate holdings.
2
Extract the first reason
The 'ashir does not take zakat on the 100 dirhams the traveler carries because 'it is small' (liqillatiha) — i.e., it is below the nisab. The zakat obligation only applies to complete nisab.
200 dirhams is the nisab for silver in Hanafi law.
3
Extract the second reason
The 'ashir does not take zakat on the 100 dirhams at home because 'what is in his house has not come under his protection' (lam yadkhul tahta himayatihi). The 'ashir's authority is limited to wealth that is physically present and under his control.
Himaa refers to the 'ashir's protective authority over wealth presented to him.
4
Combine the reasoning
Both reasons independently prevent collection. The traveler escapes zakat on both amounts: the carried wealth fails the nisab condition, and the home wealth fails the protection condition. Neither condition can be satisfied by combining the two amounts.
Combining wealth across locations is not recognized for zakat collection at a checkpoint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ مَرَّ عَلَى عَاشِرٍ بِمِائَةِ دِرْهَمٍ وَأَخْبَرَهُ أَنَّ لَهُ فِي مَنْزِلِهِ مِائَةً أُخْرَى قَدْ حَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَوْلُ لَمْ يُعَشِّرِ الَّتِي مَرَّ بِهَا لِقِلَّتِهَا وَمَا فِي بَيْتِهِ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ تَحْتَ حِمَايَتِهِ
Whoever passes by a tax collector with one hundred dirhams and informs him that he has another hundred in his house upon which a year has passed, he does not take [zakat] on that which he passed with because of its smallness, and what is in his house has not come under his protection.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This is a ruling about zakat collection at a checkpoint. If a traveler has only 100 dirhams with him (less than the nisab of 200 dirhams for silver), and tells the tax collector he has another 100 dirhams at home that have been in his possession for a year, the tax collector does not take zakat from him on either amount. The 100 dirhams he carries are below nisab, so no zakat is due. The 100 dirhams at home are not under the tax collector's physical control or protection, so he cannot collect them. This underscores that the 'ashir's authority is limited to what is present and reachable.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation; 200 dirhams for silver.
حماية (himaa): The 'ashir's protective authority over wealth physically presented to him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the 'ashir not take any zakat from the traveler in the scenario?
A) Because the traveler did not complete a year on the wealth.
B) Because both amounts are below the nisab individually and the home wealth is not under the 'ashir's protection.
C) Because the 'ashir does not have the right to collect zakat on wealth at home.
D) Because the traveler is a dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
The 'ashir's authority to collect zakat requires both the wealth to reach the nisab and to be physically under his protection; neither condition is met when wealth is split between person and home.
