Passing the 'Ashir with Bida'a and Mudaraba: The Hanafi Retraction
Ruling on bida'a and mudaraba when passing the 'ashir, with Abu Hanifa's retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for bida'a and mudaraba when passing the 'ashir, explain why Abu Hanifa initially differed, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The 'ashir takes no zakat from a mudarib or bida'a carrier unless the mudarib's profit share reaches nisab.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a person carrying investment capital (bida'a or mudaraba) passes by the 'ashir (tax/zakat collector). The ruling hinges on who bears the zakat obligation. Initially, Imam Abu Hanifa held a stricter view based on the mudarib's strong control, but he later retracted to the position of the two companions (Sahibayn). Understanding this retraction illuminates the Hanafi methodology of weighing ownership versus authority in zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two investment types
Recognize bida'a (agent gets no profit) and mudaraba (agent gets profit share). Both involve a carrier who is not the full owner.
Bida'a is like a commission-free agency; mudaraba is profit-sharing.
2
State the default ruling for both
For bida'a: no 'ushr because carrier is not authorized to pay zakat. For mudaraba: same rule applies per the book (Sahibayn's view).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's initial opinion
He argued that the mudarib has a strong right—owner cannot stop him from trading after goods are purchased—so he is treated like an owner and must pay.
The strength of right (quwwat al-haqq) is the key rationale.
4
Understand the retraction
Abu Hanifa later retracted to the view that the mudarib is neither owner nor deputy for zakat; thus no payment is due. This became the mufta bihi.
Retraction indicates the later, more authoritative position.
5
Apply the exception
If the mudarib's share of profit reaches nisab, zakat is taken from him on that profit because he owns it.
This is consistent: the mudarib pays zakat only on what he owns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَلَوْ مَرَّ بِمِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ بِضَاعَةً لَمْ يُعَشِّرْهَا لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَأْذُونٍ بِأَدَاءِ زَكَاتِهَا. قَالَ: وَكَذَا الْمُضَارَبَةُ، يَعْنِي إِذَا مَرَّ الْمُضَارِبُ بِهِ عَلَى الْعَاشِرِ. وَكَانَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ يَقُولُ أَوَّلاً يُعَشِّرُهَا لِقُوَّةِ حَقِّ الْمُضَارِبِ، حَتَّى لَا يَمْلِكُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ نَهْيَهُ عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ فِيهِ بَعْدَ مَا صَارَ عَرُوضًا، فَنَزَلَ مَنْزِلَةَ الْمَلِكِ. ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى مَا ذَكَرَ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَالِكٍ وَلَا نَائِبٍ عَنْهُ فِي أَدَاءِ الزَّكَاةِ، إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ يَبْلُغُ نَصِيبُهُ نِصَابًا فَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ مَالِكٌ لَهُ.
If he passes with two hundred dirhams as bida'a, he does not pay 'ushr on it because he is not authorized to pay its zakat. He said: Likewise mudaraba, i.e., when the mudarib passes with it before the 'ashir. Abu Hanifa used to say initially: He pays 'ushr on it due to the strength of the mudarib's right, such that the owner of the capital cannot prevent him from disposing of it after it becomes trade goods, so he is treated as an owner. Then he retracted to what is mentioned in the book, which is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) opinion, because he is neither an owner nor a deputy for the owner in paying zakat, unless there is profit in the capital such that his share reaches nisab, then it is taken from him because he owns it.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage first states the ruling for bida'a (an investment where the agent gets no profit share): if a person passes the 'ashir with 200 dirhams as bida'a, no 'ushr is taken because the carrier is not authorized by the owner to pay zakat. The same ruling applies to mudaraba (profit-sharing partnership). However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that the mudarib should pay zakat because his right is strong—once he purchases trade goods, the owner cannot prevent him from trading, so he is like an owner. Later, Abu Hanifa retracted to the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the mudarib does not pay because he is neither owner nor agent for zakat. An exception: if the mudarib's share of profit reaches nisab, then zakat is taken from him because he owns that share. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view after Abu Hanifa's retraction.

Key Terms
بضاعة (bida'a): An investment where the owner gives capital to an agent to trade, and all profit goes to the owner; the agent gets no share.
مضاربة (mudaraba): A profit-sharing partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor; profit shared as agreed.
عاشر ('ashir): A tax or zakat collector at borders or toll points.
قوة الحق (quwwat al-haqq): The strength of the right; here, the mudarib's strong entitlement to trade without owner interference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifa retract his initial opinion on mudaraba zakat?
A) He realized the mudarib's right is weak.
B) He accepted that the mudarib is not the owner nor an authorized agent for zakat.
C) He was overruled by the Sahibayn.
D) The capital had to be in cash form.

Key Takeaway
The 'ashir does not take zakat from a mudarib or bida'a carrier; the mudarib only pays zakat on his own profit share if it reaches nisab.

Zakat on Mudarabah Capital: The Tax Collector Dispute
Explanation of zakat liability for bida'ah and mudarabah when passing a tax collector

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between bida'ah and mudarabah regarding zakat liability and state the final Hanafi position on the tax collector's authority over mudarabah capital.

Core Idea
The mudarib is not liable for zakat on capital; he is neither owner nor agent for zakat.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about zakat on investment capital. The tax collector (عاشر) is empowered to collect zakat from Muslims' merchandise. The question arises: when a mudarib (investment worker) passes by with capital, can the tax collector take zakat from him? The answer traces an evolution in Imam Abu Hanifa's own thought and culminates in the relied-upon position of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Understand the bida'ah ruling
Identify the ruling for bida'ah (all profit to owner). Why is the worker not liable?
The worker is only an agent for trade, not for zakat.
2
Examine the mudarabah dispute
Note Abu Hanifa's initial view: the tax collector should take zakat because the mudarib has a strong right, akin to ownership.
The key reasoning: the mudarib cannot be prevented from trading after goods are bought.
3
Trace the retraction
Understand why Abu Hanifa later retracted to the Sahibayn's view: the mudarib is neither owner nor agent for zakat.
The proof: لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَالِكٍ وَلَا نَائِبَ عَنْهُ فِي أَدَاءِ الزَّكَاةِ.
4
Apply the exception
Identify when zakat is taken from the mudarib: only if his share of profit reaches nisab, because then he is owner of that share.
This preserves the principle that zakat is due on owned wealth.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
State the final operative position: no zakat on capital; only on mudarib's profit share if it reaches nisab.
This is the correct fatwa according to the later Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

نفع کل کا کل مالک کو دیدے کام کرنے والے کا اس میں کوئی نفع نہیں ہوتا اب مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص بضاعت کے طور پر دو سو درہم لے کر عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا تو عاشر اس کا عشر نہ لے گا۔ کیونکہ اس شخص کو مالک کی طرف سے فقط تجارت کی اجازت حاصل ہے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے پس اگر عاشر اس سے کچھ لے گا بھی تو وہ زکوۃ کے علاوہ ہوگا حالانکہ عاشر کو ز کوۃ کے علاوہ لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ مذکورہ بالا حکم مضاربت کا بھی ہے قَالَ وَكَذَا الْمُضَارَبَةُ يَعْنِي إِذَا مَرَّ الْمُضَارِبُ بِهِ عَلَى الْعَاشِرِ وَكَانَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ يَقُولُ أَوَلاَ يُعَشِّرُهَا لِقُوَّةِ حَقِّ الْمُضَارِبِ حَتَّى لَا يَمْلِكُ رَبُّ الْمَالِ نَهْيَهُ عَنِ التَّصَرُّفِ فِيهِ بَعْدَ مَا صَارَ عُرُوضًا فَنَزَلَ مَنْزِلَةَ الْمَلِكِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَالِكٍ وَلَا نَائِبَ عَنْهُ فِي أَدَاءِ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ فِي الْمَالِ رِبْحٌ يَبْلُغُ نَصِيبَهُ نِصَابًا فَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ مَالِكُ لَهُ ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ یہی حکم مضاربت کا ہے یعنی جب مضارب مال لے کر عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور ابوحنیفہ پہلے کہتے تھے کہ عاشر اس سے زکوۃ لے گا۔ حق مضاربت کے قومی ہونے کی وجہ سے حتی کہ روپیہ کی تجارتی سامان ہو جانے کے بعد رب المال اس کو اس میں تصرف کرنے سے منع کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہو گا پس مضارب بمنزلہ مالک کے قرار دیا گیا پھر ابو حنیفہ نے اس کی طرف رجوع کیا جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے اور یہی قول صاحبین کا ہے کیونکہ مضارب حقیقت مالک نہیں ہے اور نہ مالک کی طرف سے اداز کو تو میں نائب ہے مگر یہ کہ مال میں اس قدر نفع ہو کہ اس کا حصہ نصاب کو پہنچ جائے تو اس میں سے لے لیا جائے گا کیونکہ مضارب اس کا مالک ہے۔ تشریح مضاربت یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے دوسرے کو دو سو روپیہ دیا کہ اس سے تجارت کر دو اور جو کچھ نفع ہو وہ ہم دونوں کے درمیان مقبلاً آدھا آدھا ہے اب صورت یہ ہے کہ مضارب بقدر نصاب مال مضاربت لے کر عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا تو عاشر اس سے زکوۃ نہیں لے گا حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول اول یہ ہے کہ عاشر اس سے زکوۃ لے گا کیونکہ مضارب کا حق قوی ہے حق کہ جب مضارب نے روپیہ کا سامان خرید لیا تو مالک کو اختیار نہیں کہ وہ مضارب کو تجارتی تصرف سے منع کرے پھر گویا مضارب مالک کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ البتہ نارنجی طرح مالک سے عشر لیتا ہے اسی طرح مضارب سے بھی وصول کر لے گا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ نے پھر اپنے قول اول سے اس قول کی طرف رجوع کیا جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے اور یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ مضارب نہ تو مال کا مالک ہے اور نہ ادائے زکوۃ میں اس کا نائب ہے بلکہ فقط تجارت کرنے میں نائب ہے جہاں مضارب جب نہ مالک ہے اور نہ ادائے زکوۃ میں اس کا نائب ہے تو مضارب سے زکوۃ کس طرح کی جاسکتی ہے ہاں اگر مال میں اس قدر نفع ہوا کہ مضارب کا حصہ بقدر نصاب ہو گیا تو اس سے زکوۃ لی جائے گی کیونکہ مضارب اپنے حصہ کا مالک ہے۔
Book of Zakat. Explanation: In lexicology, bida'ah means a piece or portion of wealth; in terminology, bida'ah is that the owner gives money to a person, and he trades with it, and all the profit is given to the owner; the worker has no share. Now the issue: if a person passes by the tax collector with two hundred dirhams as bida'ah, the tax collector will not take its 'ushr, because this person only has permission from the owner for trade, not for paying zakat. So if the tax collector takes anything from him, it would be other than zakat, while the tax collector has no authority to take other than zakat. The same ruling applies to mudarabah. He said: and similarly mudarabah, meaning when the mudarib passes by the tax collector with it, and Abu Hanifa used to say that he should not take its 'ushr due to the strength of the mudarib's right, so much so that the owner of the capital does not have the right to prohibit him from disposing of it after it becomes goods, so he is treated as owner. Then he retracted to what is mentioned in the book, and it is the opinion of both of them, because he is not an owner and not an agent for him in paying zakat, unless there is profit in the capital that reaches nisab for his share, then it is taken from him because he is the owner of it. Translation: The author said that the same ruling applies to mudarabah, i.e., when the mudarib passes by the tax collector with the capital, and Abu Hanifa first said that the tax collector would take zakat from him, due to the strength of the mudarib's right; even after the money becomes trade goods, the owner cannot prevent him from transacting, so the mudarib is considered like an owner. Then Abu Hanifa retracted to what is mentioned in the book, and this is the opinion of the Sahibayn, because the mudarib is not actually the owner, nor is he an agent for the owner in paying zakat. Unless there is so much profit in the capital that his share reaches nisab, then zakat is taken from it, because the mudarib is the owner of that share. Explanation: Mudarabah is that one person gives another two hundred rupees to trade and whatever profit occurs is divided half and half between them. Now the case: if the mudarib passes by the tax collector with mudarabah capital amounting to nisab, the tax collector will not take zakat from him. Imam Abu Hanifa's first opinion is that the tax collector will take zakat, because the mudarib's right is strong; when the mudarib has bought goods with the money, the owner cannot prevent him from transacting, so the mudarib is like an owner. Then Imam Abu Hanifa retracted from his first opinion to the one in the book, which is the opinion of the Sahibayn; the proof is that the mudarib is neither the owner nor the agent for paying zakat; he is only an agent for trade. Since the mudarib is neither owner nor agent for zakat, how can zakat be taken from him? Yes, if there is so much profit that the mudarib's share reaches nisab, then zakat will be taken from him, because the mudarib is the owner of his share.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of zakat on mudarabah capital when passing a tax collector. The author first defines bida'ah (an investment where all profit goes to the owner) and then states that the same ruling applies to mudarabah (profit-sharing partnership). The core issue: the tax collector (عاشر) is authorized to collect zakat from Muslims' merchandise. For bida'ah, since the worker is only an agent for trade and not for zakat, the tax collector cannot take zakat. For mudarabah, Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that the mudarib's strong right over the capital makes him like an owner, so the tax collector could take zakat. However, he later retracted to the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), which is also the relied-upon position: the mudarib is neither the owner nor the agent for zakat, so no zakat is taken from the capital. An exception arises when the mudarib's share of profit reaches nisab, in which case zakat is taken from his share because he owns it. The commentary explains the reasoning and the retraction dispute.

Key Terms
بضاعت (biḍāʿah): An investment where the owner gives capital to another to trade, and all profit belongs to the owner; the worker receives no share.
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A partnership between capital provider (rabb al-mal) and worker (mudarib) where profit is shared; losses borne by capital provider.
عشر (ʿushr): The zakat levy taken by the state tax collector (عاشر) on merchandise passing through.
نائب (nāʾib): Agent or deputy; in this context, someone who acts on behalf of the owner in fulfilling an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final Hanafi position, when does the tax collector take zakat from a mudarib?
A) Always, because the mudarib controls the capital.
B) Never, because the mudarib is not the owner.
C) Only if the mudarib's share of profit reaches nisab.
D) Only if the owner authorizes the mudarib to pay zakat.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib is not liable for zakat on mudarabah capital because he is neither owner nor agent for zakat; the exception is his profit share if it reaches nisab.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Ruling on Zakat for a Ma'dhun Slave's Merchandise
Ruling on zakat for a ma'dhun slave's merchandise when passing a tax collector

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on taking 'ushr from a ma'dhun slave and distinguish it from the mudarabah case based on liability.

Core Idea
A ma'dhun slave's debt-free merchandise is subject to 'ushr because he acts for himself, unlike a mudarib.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi zakat law: a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) passes a tax collector with merchandise. The ruling is that the tax collector takes 'ushr (one-tenth) unless the slave has debt covering his property. However, a qiyas analogy to mudarabah would suggest no 'ushr, leading to an intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding the distinction between the two cases is key to applying the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from al-Quduri
Identify the base ruling: the tax collector takes 'ushr from the ma'dhun slave if he has no debt. This is the position in the matn.
Al-Quduri's text is the reference point.
2
Recognize the qiyas analogy to mudarabah
Some Hanafi jurists, including Abu Yusuf, noted that Abu Hanifa's second opinion in mudarabah (no 'ushr on the mudarib) could be analogized to the slave, since both hold property belonging to another and act as agents.
The qiyas is based on ownership belonging to the master/capital owner.
3
Analyze the distinction that overrides the qiyas
The slave acts for himself (li nafsihi) and bears liability, so he needs protection from the tax. The mudarib acts as an agent, so the capital owner needs protection. This distinction justifies the different ruling.
Liability pattern is the differentia.
4
Note the uncertainty about Abu Hanifa's retraction
Abu Yusuf expressed doubt whether Abu Hanifa retracted from his first opinion on the slave, as he did in mudarabah. The text implies that even if retraction occurred in mudarabah, it does not apply here due to the distinction.
This uncertainty does not change the mufta bihi.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that 'ushr is taken from the ma'dhun slave unless he has debt covering his property. If the master is present, 'ushr is taken from the master.
This is the fatwa according to al-Quduri and the majority.

Book of Zakat. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Three. A ma'dhun slave passed by the tax collector with two hundred dirhams and he has no debt, then the tax collector takes 'ushr from him. Opinions of the jurists: And if a slave who is authorized (ma'dhun lah) passes by with two hundred dirhams and he has no debt, he [the tax collector] takes 'ushr from him. Abu Yusuf said: I do not know whether Abu Hanifa retracted from this or not. And the qiyas of his second opinion in mudarabah—and it is the opinion of both of them—is that he does not take 'ushr from him, because the ownership of what is in his hand belongs to the master, and he has the authority to dispose; so he becomes like the mudarib. And it is said in the distinction between them that the slave acts for himself, so much so that he does not return the liability to the master, so he is the one in need of protection; while the mudarib acts by way of agency, so that he returns the liability to the owner of the capital, so the owner of the capital is the one in need of protection. Therefore, the retraction in the case of the mudarib is not a retraction from him in the case of the slave. And if his master is with him, it is taken from him [the master], because ownership belongs to him. Except when the slave has a debt that covers his property, due to absence of ownership or due to occupation. Translation: And if a ma'dhun slave in trade passes by the tax collector with two hundred dirhams and he has no debt, the tax collector takes 'ushr from him. Imam Abu Yusuf said: I do not know whether Abu Hanifa retracted from this or not. And by qiyas on his second opinion in mudarabah, which is the opinion of both of them, he would not take 'ushr from him, because whatever is in the slave's hand is the master's property, and the slave only has the right to trade; so the ma'dhun slave becomes like the mudarib. And explaining the distinction between them, it is said that the slave acts for himself, so much so that no liability falls on the master; therefore the slave himself needs protection. The mudarib acts as an agent, so all liability falls on the capital owner; thus the capital owner needs protection. So Abu Hanifa's retraction in the mudarabah case is not a retraction in the slave case. And if the master of the ma'dhun slave is with him, then 'ushr is taken from the master, because ownership is his. Except when the slave has a debt that covers all his property, because then the master's ownership is absent or occupied. Explanation: A ma'dhun slave in trade is a slave who has been given permission by his master to trade. Al-Quduri stated that if a ma'dhun slave in trade passes by the tax collector with two hundred dirhams and has no debt, the tax collector takes 'ushr from him. Imam Abu Yusuf said: I do not know whether the Imam (Abu Hanifa) retracted from this opinion of obligation of 'ushr to non-obligation or not, as retraction in the mudarabah case is established. However, in the mudarabah case, the Imam's second opinion is that 'ushr is not taken from the mudarib; similarly, 'ushr should not be obligatory on the ma'dhun slave. The proof of this qiyas is that just as the mudarib is neither owner nor agent for paying zakat, so too the property in the ma'dhun slave's hand is all the master's property; the slave is neither owner nor authorized to pay zakat on behalf of the master. He is only given authority for trade. But those who hold that 'ushr is obligatory on the ma'dhun slave and not on the mudarib distinguish between the two: the ma'dhun slave acts for himself, so no liability falls on the master. Therefore, when the slave acts for himself, he needs protection and protection.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted by his master to trade) who passes a tax collector with merchandise. The source text from al-Quduri states that the tax collector takes 'ushr from the slave if he has no debt. Abu Yusuf expresses uncertainty whether Abu Hanifa retracted from this position, as he did in the mudarabah case. By qiyas on Abu Hanifa's second opinion in mudarabah, the tax collector should not take 'ushr, because the slave's property belongs to the master and he is merely an agent for trade, like the mudarib. However, a distinction is made: the slave acts for himself (li nafsihi), meaning he bears the liability and needs protection, while the mudarib acts as an agent, so the capital owner needs protection. Therefore, Abu Hanifa's retraction in mudarabah does not imply retraction in the slave case. If the master is present, 'ushr is taken from the master. But if the slave has debt that covers all his property, no 'ushr is taken due to the master's ownership being absent or occupied. The commentary elaborates on these distinctions and the reasoning of the jurists.

Key Terms
عبد مأذون له (ʿabd ma'dhūn lahu): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade.
مولی (mawlā): Master or owner of the slave.
دین (dayn): Debt owed by the slave; if it covers the property, it affects ownership of the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the distinction made in the text, why is the ruling on a ma'dhun slave different from that on a mudarib?
A) The slave is owned by the master, while the mudarib is free.
B) The slave acts for himself and bears liability, while the mudarib acts as an agent.
C) The slave's capital is less than nisab.
D) The slave cannot own property at all.

Key Takeaway
The ma'dhun slave's distinct liability structure justifies the imposition of 'ushr, unlike the mudarib.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: 'Ushr on the 'Abd Ma'dhun
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas and talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the cases of a 'abd ma'dhun and a mudarib regarding the obligation of 'ushr, and explain why Abu Hanifa's retraction in the mudarabah case does not affect his ruling on the slave.

Core Idea
'Abd ma'dhun pays 'ushr because he acts for himself and needs protection; mudarib does not because liabilities fall on the capital owner.

In this passage, we encounter a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement: should a slave permitted to trade pay the trade tax ('ushr) when passing the tax collector? Abu Hanifa's initial ruling says yes, but his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani dissent, drawing an analogy to the mudarib (working partner) who does not pay. The author of Ashraf al-Hadaya defends Abu Hanifa's original position by highlighting a crucial distinction: the slave's personal liability versus the mudarib's agency. Understanding this distinction is key to mastering the Hanafi approach to qiyas and khiyār (retraction).

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling from the Matn
Begin by identifying the core ruling: if a permitted slave ('abd ma'dhun) passes by the tax collector with trade goods of 200 dirhams and has no debt, 'ushr is taken from him. This is the position recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Opposing Positions
Note the two opposing views: (1) The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no 'ushr is taken from the slave. (2) Abu Hanifa himself had a second opinion by qiyas to mudarabah that aligns with the Sahibayn, raising the question of whether he retracted his first opinion.
Abu Yusuf reports uncertainty about the retraction.
3
Analyze the Qiyas Argument
Understand the qiyas from mudarabah: the mudarib does not pay 'ushr because he does not own the capital and acts as an agent. The slave likewise does not own the goods (master owns) and only has permission to dispose. Therefore, by analogy, the slave should not pay. This is the Sahibayn's proof.
The illa (effective cause) is 'lack of ownership and acting as an agent'.
4
Examine the Distinction (Fariq)
The author presents the counter-argument: the slave acts for himself—his liabilities do not transfer to the master. He bears personal responsibility for debts, etc. Thus he is in need of protection (himaya) that the 'ushr provides (as a toll for safe passage). The mudarib, however, acts as a deputy; his liabilities fall on the capital owner, so the capital owner needs protection, not the mudarib.
This distinction blocks the qiyas and preserves Abu Hanifa's first opinion as consistent.
5
Apply the Thamarah and Additional Conditions
The practical consequence (thamarah): Under Abu Hanifa's first opinion, the tax collector takes from the slave; under the Sahibayn's view, he does not. Also note the two additional rulings derived: (1) if the master accompanies, 'ushr is taken from the master; (2) if the slave has a debt covering his entire wealth, no 'ushr is taken from anyone.
These conditions show the depth of the legal analysis.

ترجمہ اور اگر عبد ماذون له في التجارة دو سو درہم لے کر عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور اس غلام پر قرضہ بھی نہیں ہے تو عاشر اس سے عشر لے گا امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ مجھے معلوم نہیں کہ ابو حنیفہ نے اس سے رجوع کیا ہے یا نہیں اور مضاربت میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے دوسرے قول پر قیاس یہ ہے کہ عاشر اس سے عشر نہ لے گا اور یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے کیونکہ جو کچھ غلام کے پاس ہے وہ مولیٰ کی ملک ہے اور عبد ماذون کو ( فقط ) تجارتی تصرف کا حق ہے پس عبد ماذون لہ بھی مضارب کے مانند ہو گیا ہے اور دونوں کے درمیان فرق بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا گیا ہے کہ غلام اپنے واسطے تصرف کرتا ہے حتی کہ مولی پر کوئی ذمہ داری عائد نہیں ہوتی پس غلام مازون ہی حمایت کا محتاج ہوا اور مضارب نائب ہونے کی وجہ سے تصرف کرتا ہے حتی کہ تمام تر ذمہ داری رب المال پر عائد ہوتی ہے پس رب المال ہی حمایت کا محتاج ہوا۔ پس امام ابوحنیفہ کا مضارب کے مسئلہ میں اپنے قول سے رجوع کرنا عبد ما زون کے مسئلہ میں رجوع کرنا نہیں ہوگا اور اگر عبد ماذون لہ کا مولیٰ اس کے ساتھ ہو تو مولی سے عشر لے لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ملک تو اسی کی ہے مگر جبکہ غلام پر اس قدر قرضہ ہو کہ وہ اس کے تمام مال کو محیط ہے کیونکہ (اس صورت میں ) مولیٰ کی ملک معدوم ہے یا مشغول ہے۔

فرماتے ہیں یا یہ کہ یہ مال دین کے ساتھ مشغول ہو گیا ہے جیسا کہ صاحبین کہتے ہیں اور ملک کا معدوم ہو جانا یا مال کا دین کے ساتھ مشغول ہو جانا دونوں وجوب زکوۃ کے لئے مانع ہیں۔ اس لئے غلام کے ذمہ قرضہ ہو Book of Zakat: And if a slave who is permitted [to trade] passes by with two hundred dirhams and there is no debt upon him, the tax collector takes tithe from him. Abu Yusuf said: I do not know whether Abu Hanifa retracted from this or not. And the analogy of his second opinion in mudarabah (and it is the opinion of the two) is that he does not take tithe from him, because the ownership of what is in his hand belongs to the master and he has the right of disposal, so he becomes like the mudarib. And it is said in the distinction between them that the slave disposes for himself, so that he does not recourse with liability upon the master, so he is the one in need of protection. And the mudarib disposes by virtue of agency, so that he recourses with liability upon the owner of the capital, so the owner of the capital is the one in need of protection. So the retraction in the case of the mudarib is not a retraction from him in the case of the slave. And if his master is with him, it is taken from him, because ownership is his, except when there is a debt upon the slave that encompasses his wealth, due to the non-existence of ownership or due to occupancy. Translation: And if a slave permitted to trade passes by the tax collector with two hundred dirhams and there is no debt on that slave, then the tax collector takes tithe from him. Imam Abu Yusuf said: I do not know whether Abu Hanifa retracted from this or not. And by analogy to his second opinion in mudarabah, which is the opinion of the Sahibayn, that the tax collector does not take tithe from him, because whatever is with the slave is the property of the master, and the permitted slave only has the right of commercial disposal, so the permitted slave also becomes like the mudarib. And a distinction is made between them by saying that the slave disposes for his own sake, so that no liability falls on the master. Therefore the permitted slave himself is in need of protection. And the mudarib disposes as a deputy, so all liability falls on the owner of the capital, so the owner of the capital is in need of protection. So Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction from his first opinion in the case of mudarabah does not necessitate that he retracted from his opinion (obligation of tithe) in the case of the permitted slave. And if the master of the permitted slave is with him, then tithe is taken from the master, because the property in the possession of the slave is the master's property. Yes, if there is a debt on the slave that encompasses all his wealth, i.e., the wealth and debt are approximately equal, then nothing is taken from the permitted slave, whether the master is with him or not, because due to the attachment of the creditors' right, the ownership of the master has become non-existent according to Imam Abu Hanifa, or because the wealth has become occupied with the debt according to the Sahibayn. And the non-existence of ownership or the occupation of wealth with debt are both impediments to the obligation of zakat. Therefore, in the case of a debt on the slave, no tithe or anything is obligatory. Footnotes: In the mentioned issues, wherever the word 'ushr (tithe) is used, it does not specifically mean the tenth part, but the word 'ushr is also applied to the twentieth part and the fortieth part. Its determination can be made by context. For example, if a person passing with trade goods before the tax collector is a Muslim, then the fortieth part is taken from him; if he is a dhimmi, then the twentieth part; and if he is a harbi, then the tenth part. And the term 'ushr applies to all of them.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a slave permitted to trade ('abd ma'dhun) is liable for 'ushr (trade tax) on his merchandise when passing by the tax collector. The author begins with the ruling from the matn: if the slave has 200 dirhams and no debt, 'ushr is taken from him. Abu Yusuf then reports uncertainty whether Abu Hanifa retracted this ruling, as he did in the analogous case of mudarabah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'ushr is not taken from the slave because the property belongs to the master, and the slave only has the right to dispose, like a mudarib. However, the author presents a distinction: the slave acts for himself—his liabilities do not transfer to the master—so he needs the protection that 'ushr provides (as a toll for safe passage). In contrast, the mudarib acts as an agent; liabilities fall on the capital owner, who then is the one in need of protection. Hence, Abu Hanifa's retraction in the mudarabah case does not imply retraction here. The passage then addresses two additional rulings: (1) if the master accompanies the slave, 'ushr is taken from the master (since ownership is his); (2) if the slave has a debt equal to his entire wealth, no 'ushr is taken from anyone, because ownership is either extinguished (Abu Hanifa's view) or occupied (Sahibayn's view). The section concludes with a note that 'ushr can refer to a fortieth (for Muslims), twentieth (for dhimmis), or tenth (for harbis) depending on context.

Key Terms
عبد مأذون ('abd ma'dhun): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade.
عشر ('ushr): A tax or tithe levied on trade goods passing by a tax collector; the rate varies (1/10, 1/20, or 1/40) depending on the status of the trader.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner in a mudarabah (profit-sharing) contract who manages the capital.
عاشر ('ashir): The tax collector or customs official who collects 'ushr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a mudarib not pay 'ushr while a slave permitted to trade does (according to the mufta bihi opinion)?
A) Because the mudarib owns the capital, while the slave does not.
B) Because the mudarib acts for himself, while the slave acts as agent.
C) Because liabilities from the mudarib's transactions fall on the capital owner, while the slave's liabilities fall on himself.
D) Because the mudarib is a free person, while the slave is not.

Key Takeaway
The slave's independent liability makes him liable for 'ushr; the mudarib's agency exempts him.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Paying 'Ushr to Khawarij Tax Collector
Stating the ruling that 'ushr paid to Khawarij must be repaid to a just ruler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that 'ushr paid to Khawarij must be repaid to the just ruler and explain the legal basis of negligence (taqsir).

Core Idea
Payment to a rebel ruler does not discharge the obligation; negligence requires repetition.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in zakat: a Muslim passing through territory controlled by the Khawarij (a rebel group) and paying 'ushr to their tax collector. The Hanafi ruling, as stated in al-Hidayah, is that this payment is invalid and the person must pay again when he passes by the tax collector of the just ruler. The key legal reason is the person's own negligence in choosing to traverse that path.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying 'ushr to the Khawarij tax collector. The ruling: it is invalid and must be paid again.
The passage clearly states the ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle of negligence (taqsir). The person's choice to pass through rebel territory makes him responsible.
No explicit Quran or hadith text is cited; the reasoning is based on causality.
3
Apply the ruling
When the person later passes by the just ruler's tax collector, he must pay 'ushr again.
The payment to Khawarij does not count toward the obligation.
4
Note the absence of dispute
The text presents this as unanimous within the Hanafi madhhab; no contrary view is mentioned.
This indicates the ruling is well-established.

قَالَ وَمَنْ مَرَّ عَلَى عَاشِرِ الْخَوَارِجِ فِي أَرْضِ قَدْ غَلَبُوا عَلَيْهَا فَعَشَرَهُ يُنَى عَلَيْهِ الصَّدَقَةُ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا مَرَّ عَلَى عَاشِرِ اَهْلِ الْعَدْلِ لأنَّ التَّقْصِيرَ جَاءَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنه مَرَّ عَلَيْهِ

ترجمہ فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص کسی ایسی زمین میں جہاں خارجیوں کا تسلط ہو گیا ہے خارجیوں کے عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا اور خارجیوں کے عامل نے اس سے عشر لے لیا۔ تو دوبارہ اس سے صدقہ لیا جائے گا۔ یعنی جب وہ اہل عدل کے عاشر کے پاس سے گذرے کیونکہ تقصیر تو اس کی طرف سے ہوئی کہ وہ خارجی عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ: اگر کوئی مسلمان جس کا تعلق اہل سنت و الجماعت سے ہے خارجیوں کے عاشر کے پاس سے ایسی زمین میں گذرا جہاں خارجی غالب اور مسلط ہو گئے ہیں اور خارجیوں کے عاشر نے اس سے عشر بھی لے لیا ہے پھر یہ شخص اہل عدل کے عاشر کے پاس سے
He said: And whoever passes by the tax collector of the Khawarij in a land they have overcome, and he takes tithe from him, then the sadaqah (zakat) is repeated upon him. Meaning: when he passes by the tax collector of the just people, because the negligence came from him in that he passed by him.

Translation: He said: If a person passes by the tax collector of the Khawarij in a land where they have gained dominance, and the officer of the Khawarij takes tithe from him, then the sadaqah will be taken from him again. That is, when he passes by the tax collector of the just people, because the negligence came from his side that he passed by the Khawarij tax collector.

Explanation: If a Muslim who belongs to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah passes by the tax collector of the Khawarij in a land where the Khawarij have become dominant and overpowering, and the Khawarij tax collector takes tithe from him, then this person [when he] passes by the tax collector of the just people...
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with a brief proof. It addresses a scenario where a Muslim passes through territory controlled by the Khawarij (an early sect) and pays 'ushr to their tax collector. The ruling: this payment does not count; he must pay 'ushr again when he passes by the tax collector of the just ruler (the legitimate Islamic authority). The reason given is that the person was negligent (taqsir) by choosing to pass through that area under Khawarij control. Therefore, he bears responsibility and must pay again. The Urdu commentary elaborates that this applies specifically to a Muslim from Ahl al-Sunnah. The passage is incomplete but covers the main ruling and reasoning.

Key Terms
الخوارج (al-Khawarij): An early Islamic sect known for rebellion against established rulers; here, they are a group that has taken control of a territory.
أهل العدل (ahl al-'adl): The just rulers (the legitimate Islamic authority) from Ahl al-Sunnah.
تقصير (taqsir): Negligence or fault on the part of the person.

Paying zakah to an illegitimate authority does not fulfill the obligation; the payer must pay again to the just ruler due to his own negligence.

Khumus on All Minerals: The Hanafi Position vs. Al-Shafi'i
Dispute on khumus obligation for minerals extracted from mines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khumus for minerals from mines, identify the key hadith and analogy used, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
All mined minerals are subject to khumus, not zakat, because they are ghanimah from prior disbeliever possession.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling that khumus (one-fifth) is wajib on all minerals extracted from mines, including gold, silver, iron, lead, and copper. It then introduces the Shafi'i objection, which distinguishes between precious metals and other minerals. The commentary expands the arguments, citing the hadith 'fi al-rikaz al-khumus' and the analogy to booty. This lesson will dissect the proofs and the point of disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
Read the opening sentence. What is the ruling on minerals from a mine according to the Hanafi school? Note the types of minerals and land types mentioned.
The ruling applies to gold, silver, iron, lead, and copper, in both kharaji and 'ushri land.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Find where al-Shafi'i's view is quoted. What does he say about minerals? Under what condition does he require zakat?
Al-Shafi'i holds that minerals are mubah like game, except gold and silver which incur zakat without a year.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the hadith 'fi al-rikaz al-khumus' and the analogy to ghanimah. How do these prove khumus on all minerals?
The term 'rikaz' is derived from 'rakaza' (to bury), thus including buried minerals. Mines were in disbelievers' hands, so they are booty.
4
Examine the Shafi'i counter-dalil
The Shafi'i argument uses the mubah nature of minerals and the hadith of Bilal ibn al-Harith. What is the Hanafi response to these?
The Hanafi response argues that mines are not like hunting because of prior ownership, and the Bilal hadith is interpreted as referring to khumus, not zakat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two schools in this issue?
Hanafi: khumus (20%) on all mined minerals. Shafi'i: zakat (2.5%) only on gold/silver from mines; nothing on other minerals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ مَعْدنُ ذَهَبٍ أوْ فِضَّةٍ أَوْ حَدِيدٍ أَوْ رَصَاصٍ أَوْ صُفْرٍ وُجِدَ فِي اَرْضِ حَرَاجِ أَوْ عُشْرٍ فَفِيهِ الْحُمْسُ عِندَنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعَى لَاشَى عَلَيْهِ فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ مُبَاحٌ سَبَقَتْ يَدُهُ إِلَيْهِ كَالصَّيْدِ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ الْمُسْتَخْرَجُ ذَهَبًا أَوْ فِضَّةٌ فَيَجِبُ فِيهِ الزَّكوة وَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ الْحَوْل فِى قَوْلِ لِأَنَّهُ بِمَاء كُلَّهُ وَالْحَوْل لِلتَنْمِيَةِ وَلَنَا قَوْلَهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَفِي الرِّكَازِ الْخُمْسُ وَهُوَ مِنَ الركز فأطلق عَلَى الْمَعْدَنِ وَلِأَنَّهَا كَانَتْ فِي أَيْدِى الْكَفَرَةِ وَحُوتُهَا أَيْدِينَا غَلَبَةً فَكَانَتْ غَيْمَةً وَفِي الْغَنَائِمِ الْخَمْسُ بِخِلَافِ الصَّيْدِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي يَدِ أَحَدٍ إِلَّا أَنَّ لِلْعَادِمِينَ يدًا حُكْمةً لِتُؤْتِهَا عَلَى الظَّاهِرِ وَامَّا الْحَقِيقَةُ فَلِلْوَاحِدِ فَاعْتَبَرُنَا الْحُكْمِية فِي حَقِّ الْحُمْسِ وَالْحَقِيقَةٌ فِى حَقِّ الْأَرْبَعَةِ الأَحْمَاسِ حَتَّى كَانَتْ  ِللو 
 وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُم مِّنْ شَيْ فَإِنَّ اللهِ حُمَسه 
 عَنْ رَبِيعَةَ بْنِ عَبدِ الرَّحْمَانَ عَنْ غَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عُلَمَائِهِمْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَطَعَ لِبِلالِ بْنِ الحَارِثِ المُزَنِي مَعَادِنُ بِالقَبْلِيَةِ وَهِيَ نَاحِيَةُ الْفُرْعِ فَتِلْكَ المَعَادِنُ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهَا إلى اليوم إِلَّا الزكوة 
 قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الرِّكَازِ
He said: A mine of gold, silver, iron, lead, or copper found in kharaji or 'ushri land has the khumus (one-fifth) according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: There is nothing upon it because it is permissible (mubah) which his hand preceded to, like the game (sayd), except if the extracted is gold or silver, then zakat is obligatory and the passing of a year (hawl) is not required in one of his sayings because it is all growth (nama) and the hawl is for growth. Our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'And in rikaz is khumus' and it is from 'rakaza' so he applied it to the mine. And because they (the mines) were in the hands of the disbelievers and our hands conquered them, so they became booty, and in booty is the khumus, unlike game because it was not in anyone's hand, except that the conquerors have a hukmi (legal) hand for its apparent ownership, but the real ownership is for the finder. So we consider the hukmi hand for the right of khumus and the real hand for the four-fifths, so that it becomes for him. And know that whatever you take as booty, for Allah is its fifth. From Rabi'ah ibn Abd al-Rahman, from more than one of their scholars, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) granted Bilal ibn al-Harith al-Muzani the mines of al-Qabaliyyah, which is in the region of al-Fur', and those mines, until today, nothing is taken from them except zakat. He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'In rikaz...'
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) from the Hanafi school on the obligation of khumus (one-fifth) for minerals extracted from mines, including gold, silver, iron, lead, and copper, whether found in kharaji (taxed) or 'ushri (tithe) land. The text then presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who separates between precious metals and other minerals, and discusses the conditions for zakat. The Hanafi position is argued using two main proofs: first, the hadith 'fi al-rikaz al-khumus,' where rikaz includes minerals as it is derived from 'rakaza' (to bury), and second, the analogy to ghanimah (booty) because the land and its contents were previously in the possession of disbelievers, and the Muslims conquered them by force. The commentator clarifies that unlike hunting (sayd), which is a permissible object without prior ownership, mines have a 'hukmi' (legal) hand of the conquerors, thus the khumus applies. The Shafi'i view is refuted: the Hanafi school considers minerals as booty subject to khumus, not zakat, and hence no annual condition applies. The Quranic verse (al-Anfal 8:41) is cited to support the khumus on booty. The passage also references a hadith from the Muwatta of Imam Malik about Bilal ibn al-Harith's mine concession, though the Hanafi scholar notes that the wording in the hadith uses 'zakat' but the context is interpreted as khumus.

Key Terms
معدن (ma'dan): A mine or source of minerals, including gold, silver, iron, lead, copper, etc.
ركاز (rikaz): Treasure or minerals buried in the earth; includes both buried treasure (kanz) and minerals (ma'dan).
خمس (khumus): One-fifth; the obligatory share on rikaz and mines.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing, because it is mubah
B) Zakat (1/40) with the condition of a year
C) Khumus (one-fifth)
D) Khumus only if the mineral is gold or silver

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, all minerals from mines are subject to khumus, not zakat, based on the hadith of rikaz and the analogy to booty.

The Hanafi Ruling on Minerals: Khums vs. Zakat
Inter-madhhab dispute on minerals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on minerals (khums is wajib on all meltable minerals), state the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Minerals from conquered lands are ghanimah, requiring one-fifth (khums), not zakat.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on minerals (ma'adin) and its difference with the Shafi'i school. The Hanafi school holds that khums (one-fifth) is wajib on all meltable minerals found, regardless of land type, while the Shafi'i school limits obligation to zakat on gold and silver only. We will examine the proofs from Quran, hadith, and rational argument, and analyze the refutation of the Shafi'i evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the Hanafi ruling clearly: meltable minerals (gold, silver, iron, copper, etc.) from any land (ushri or kharaji) require payment of one-fifth (khums) immediately upon extraction.
This is a wajib obligation, not fard, because the dalil is ahad and qiyas.
2
Examine the first proof: Quranic verse on ghanimah
Surah al-Anfal (8:41) commands one-fifth for Allah from spoils (ghanimah). The Hanafis argue that minerals from conquered lands are ghanimah because the land and its contents were in non-Muslim possession before conquest.
The verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah in its application to minerals.
3
Examine the second proof: Hadith of Rikaz
The Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'In rikaz is khums.' When asked what rikaz is, he replied, 'Gold and silver that Allah created in the earth on the day the earth was created.' The Hanafis interpret rikaz as including minerals (ma'adin).
This hadith is ahad but considered strong by Hanafis.
4
Examine the rational argument
All mineral lands were originally in non-Muslim hands; when Muslims conquer them, these lands and their contents become spoils of war (ghanimah). Therefore, one-fifth is wajib. This distinguishes minerals from ownerless property like game, which requires no payment.
The comparison to game is a direct rebuttal of the Shafi'i analogy.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Shafi'i argues that minerals are like ownerless property (mubah) and no payment is due, citing the Bilal ibn al-Harith hadith. The Hanafi response: minerals are not mubah because they were conquered, and the Bilal hadith is munqati' (disconnected) and thus unreliable.
The distinction between actual and legal possession resolves the question of who keeps four-fifths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة
تشریح معدن کی تین قسمیں ہیں۔ اول : جامد جو پگھل جاتی ہے اور ڈھالنے سے ڈھل جاتی ہے جیسے سونا چاندی لوہا را نگ، پیتل، دوم: جامد جو پچھلتا نہیں جیسے چونا، سرمہ، ہڑتال ، یاقوت، نمک ، سوم : غیر جامد جیسے پانی ، قیر قیر : سیاہ رنگ کی ایک چیز جس کو کشتی پر ملتے ہیں تا کہ پانی اندر نہ آئے ۔ نفط : ایک قسم کا معدنی تیل جو بہت جلد آگ پکڑ لیتا ہے اور جس سے آگ جلانے کا کام لیتے ہیں اور اس سے علاج بھی کرتے ہیں عقلی طور پر باب کے مسائل پندرہ قسموں پر مشتمل ہیں کیونکہ سونا یا چاندی جو برآمد ہوا ہے وہ معدن ہوگا یا کنز ہوگا پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک کی دو دو قسمیں ہیں کیونکہ وہ یا تو دار الاسلام کی زمین سے برآمد ہوا ہو گا یا دارالحرب کی زمین سے ان میں سے پھر ہر ایک کی تین تین قسمیں ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ یا تو وہ ایسے جنگل میں پایا جائے گا جس کا کوئی مالک نہیں ہے یا ملوکہ زمین میں پایا جائے گا یا گھر میں پایا جائے گا یہ بارہ قسمیں ہوئیں پھر خاص طور پر کنز کی تین قسمیں ہیں کیونکہ جو گھر برآمد ہوا ہے اس پر اہل اسلام کے سکہ کا نشان ہوگا یا اہل جاہلیت کے سکہ کا یا اس کا حال مشتبہ ہوگا پندرہ اقسام میں سے پہلی قسم کا حکم یعنی جو پکھل جاتا ہے اور ڈھل جاتا ہے جیسے چاندی سونا او با را انگ اور پینیل ہمارے نزدیک ان کا حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ چیز میں عشری زمین میں پائی جائیں یا خراجی زمین میں ۔ ان میں شمس یعنی پانچواں واجب ہوگا۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ سونے اور چاندی کے علاوہ معدن میں کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے ہاں اگر سونا یا چاندی برآمد ہو تو اس میں زکوۃ یعنی چالیسواں حصہ واجب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ معدن مباح ہوتا ہے اس کا کوئی مالک نہیں ہوتا لہذا جس کے ہاتھ پہلے لگ گیا ۔ اس کا ہو گیا اور جو چیز ایسی ہو یعنی مباح غیر مملوک ہو تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوتا جیسے شکار جس نے پہلے پکڑ لیا اس کا ہے اس میں کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہوتی پس اسی طرح معدن کے اندر بھی کوئی چیز نمس وغیرہ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ امام شافعی معدن کے اندرو جوب زکوۃ پر اس روایت سے بھی استدلال کرتے ہیں جو موطا امام مالک میں مذکور ہے روایت کا متن یہ ہے "عَنْ رَبِيعَةَ بْنِ عَبدِ الرَّحْمَانَ عَنْ غَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عُلَمَائِهِمْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَطَعَ لِبِلالِ بْنِ الحَارِثِ المُزَنِي مَعَادِنُ بِالقَبْلِيَةِ وَهِيَ نَاحِيَةُ الْفُرْعِ فَتِلْكَ المَعَادِنُ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهَا إلى اليوم إِلَّا الزكوة، قطع کے معانی با گیر دینا۔ قبیلہ قبل (بفتحة القاف والباء) کی طرف منسوب ہے جو ایک مقام کا نام ہے فرع فاء کے ضمہ اور راء کے سکون کے ساتھ حرمین کے درمیان ایک موضع کا نام ہے۔ اب حدیث کا ترجمہ یہ ہوگا کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بلال بن حارث مزنی کو موضع قبل کے معادن بطور جاگیر عطاء فرمائے پس ان معادن سے سوائے زکوۃ کے آج تک کچھ نہیں لیا جاتا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ معادن میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک معادن نے اگر سونا یا چاندی برآمد ہوا تو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی مگر جوب زکوۃ کے لئے حولان حول شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ حولان حول کی شرط نمو کے واسطے لگائی جاتی ہے اور معادن چونکہ اس کو مفت میں حاصل ہوا ہے اس لئے وہ پورے کا پورانسمو ہے لہذا حولان حول کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے ہماری دلیل باری تعالے کا قول " وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُم مِّنْ شَيْ فَإِنَّ اللهِ حُمَسه یعنی جو کچھ تم کو بطور نیمت حاصل ہوا ہے اس کا پانچواں حصہ اللہ کا ہے اور یہ مال جوز مین سے برآمد ہوا ہے یہ مال غنیمت ہے کیونکہ یہ زمین اور جو کچھ اس کے اندر اللہ نے پیدا کیا ہے وہ سب کفار کے قبضہ میں تھا لیکن جب مسلمان اس پر غالب آگئے تو یہ زمین اور اس کے اندر کے سب خزانے مسلمانوں کے لئے مال غنیمت ہو گئے اور مال غنیمت میں چار شمس غنائم کے اور ایک خمس اللہ کا ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ آیت بالا میں بصراحت مذکور ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ معادن کے اندر ایک شمس اللہ کے لئے واجب ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الرِّكَازِ الْحُمُسُ قِيْلَ مَا الرّكَازُ يَارَسُولَ اللهِ؟ قَالَ الذَّهَبُ وَالْفِضَّةُ الَّذِى خَلْقَهُ اللَّهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ يَوْمَ خُلِقَتِ الْأَرْضُ ( رواه البيهقى) ابو ہریرہ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ رکاز کے اندر خمس واجب ہے کسی نے دریافت کیا کہ رسول خدار کاز کیا چیز ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا کہ وہ سونا اور چاندی جس کو اللہ نے اس دن زمین کے اندر پیدا فرمایا جس روز زمین پیدا کی گئی تھی ۔ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے رکاز کی تعریف کر دینے سے معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث میں رکاز سے مراد معدن ہے کیونکہ یہ تعریف معدن ہی کی کیجاتی ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ معدن کے اندر خمس واجب ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے عقلی دلیل بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ معدن کی تمام زمینیں کفار کے قبضہ میں تھیں مسلمانوں نے ان پر غلبہ پاکران کو غنیمت بنالیا ہے اور غنیمت کے مالوں میں پانچواں حصہ اللہ کا ہوتا ہے اس لئے معادن کے اندر بھی پانچواں حصہ اللہ کے لئے واجب ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف شکار کہ وہ شکار کرنے سے پہلے کسی کے قبضہ میں نہیں تھا لہذا کسی مسلمان کے پکڑنے سے وہ مال غنیمت نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مال غنیمت نہ ہوا تو شکار کے اندر شمس بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
 إِلَّا إِنَّ لِلْغَائِمِينَ .. الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ معدن جس کو اللہ تعالے نے زمین کے اندر پیدا کیا ہے اگر وہ مال غنیمت ہے جیسا کہ کہا گیا ہے تو چار خمس غانمین اور مجاہدین کے ہونے چاہئیں نہ کہ پانے والے کے کیونکہ مال غنیمت کا حکم یہی ہے کہ اس کا ایک شمس اللہ اور رسول کا ہوتا ہے اور چار شمس غانمین کے ہوتے ہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ چارٹس غانمین کے واسطے اس وقت ہوتے ہیں جبکہ شئی مغنوم اور مال غنیمت پر ان کا قبضہ حقیقیہ اور حکما دونوں طرح ثابت ہو ۔ اور جب غانمین کا قبضہ حکما ثابت ہو اور حقیقہ کسی دوسرے کا قبضہ ثابت ہو۔ تو ان کے لئے چار شمس نہیں ہوتے بلکہ جسکا قبضہ حقیقہ ہوگا چارٹس اس کے لئے ہوں گے۔ حاصل یہ کہ معدان جوز مین سے برآمد ہوا ہے اس پر غانمین کا قبضہ فقط حکما ہے اور حقیقی قبضہ پانے والے کا ہے پس ہم نے حکمی قبضہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ایک شمس اللہ کے واسطے واجب کر دیا ہے جس کے حقدار یتامی اور مساکین ہیں اور حقیقی قبضہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے چار خمس پانے والے کو دیدئیے جائیں گے۔ پانے والا مسلمان ہو یا زمی آزاد ہو یا غلام بچہ ہو یا بالغ مرد ہو یا عورت ہو حضرت امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ روایت بلال بن الحارث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث منقطع ہے اور حدیث منقطع قابل استدلال نہیں ہوتی۔
Book of Zakat. Explanation: Minerals are of three types. First: solid that melts and can be cast, like gold, silver, iron, copper, brass. Second: solid that does not melt, like lime, antimony, orpiment, ruby, salt. Third: non-solid, like water, tar. Tar: a black substance used on ships to prevent water entry. Naft: a mineral oil that catches fire quickly and is used for lighting and treatment. Logically, the chapter's issues comprise fifteen categories because gold or silver extracted is either from a mine or a treasure; each of these has two types based on whether found in Dar al-Islam or Dar al-Harb; each of those has three types based on whether found in ownerless land, state land, or a house. That makes twelve. Then treasure specifically has three types based on coinage: Islamic, Jahili, or ambiguous. Out of these fifteen, the ruling for the first type—that which melts and can be cast, like silver, gold, iron, copper, brass—in our view is: whether found in ushr land or kharaj land, a fifth (khums) is wajib. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad said: for minerals other than gold and silver, nothing is wajib; but if gold or silver is found, zakat (one-fortieth) is wajib. Their proof: a mine is mubah (ownerless); whoever takes it first owns it; for ownerless property nothing is due, like game—no payment for hunting. Imam Shafi'i also adduces a narration in Malik's Muwatta from Rabi'a ibn Abd al-Rahman from multiple scholars that the Prophet (peace be upon him) granted Bilal ibn al-Harith al-Muzani mines in al-Qabaliyya (a region of al-Fur'), and from those mines nothing is taken except zakat until today. The author of Hidayah says: For Shafi'i, if gold or silver is found, zakat is wajib but without the condition of hawl (yearly cycle), since hawl is for growth, and minerals are inherently growth. Our proof: Allah's saying 'And know that whatever you take as spoils, verily for Allah is one-fifth thereof'—this wealth from the earth is ghanimah because the land and its contents were in the hands of disbelievers; when Muslims conquered them, the land and treasures became spoils. So one-fifth is for Allah. Second proof: Hadith of Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'In rikaz is khums.' It was asked: 'What is rikaz?' He said: 'Gold and silver that Allah created in the earth on the day the earth was created.' This defines rikaz as ma'din (mine), establishing khums. The author of Hidayah provides a rational proof: all mineral lands were in disbelievers' possession; Muslims conquered them as spoils; thus one-fifth is wajib. In contrast, game is not priorly possessed, so it is not ghanimah and no payment is due. Then a question: If these minerals are ghanimah, then four-fifths should go to the conquering army, not to the finder. The answer: The four-fifths are for the conquerors only when they have both actual and legal possession. Here, they have only legal possession; the actual possessor is the finder. So, considering legal possession, one-fifth is due to Allah (for orphans and needy), and considering actual possession, four-fifths go to the finder (whether Muslim or dhimmi, free or slave, child or adult, man or woman). As for the narration of Bilal ibn al-Harith cited by Shafi'i, it is munqati' (disconnected) and thus not admissible as evidence.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh of Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling on minerals (ma'adin) and the obligation of khums (one-fifth). The author begins by categorizing minerals into three types: meltable solids (metals), non-meltable solids, and liquids. He then explains the logical framework of fifteen categories based on type (mine vs. treasure), location (Dar al-Islam vs. Dar al-Harb), and ownership status (ownerless land, state land, private house). For the first category—meltable metals like gold, silver, iron, copper, brass—the Hanafi position is that khums is wajib regardless of whether the land is 'ushri or kharaji. This is opposed by Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, who restrict zakat to gold and silver only, and even then at the rate of 1/40 (zakat), not khums, with the condition of hawl. The Hanafi proofs are three: First, the Quranic verse on spoils (ghanimah) which commands one-fifth for Allah. Since the land and its minerals were originally in the hands of non-Muslims, when Muslims conquer and take possession, these become ghanimah, hence khums is due. Second, the hadith of Rikaz (treasure) where the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly says 'in rikaz is khums' and defines rikaz as gold and silver created in the earth, which includes mines. Third, a rational argument: all mineral lands were under non-Muslim control; Muslims took them as spoils, so one-fifth applies. The passage also addresses the counterargument that if it is ghanimah, the four-fifths should go to the conquering army. The response distinguishes between legal possession (which the army has) and actual possession (which the finder has), so the finder keeps four-fifths and pays one-fifth to the state treasury for the needy. Finally, the hadith of Bilal ibn al-Harith (cited by Shafi'i) is rejected on grounds of being munqati' (broken chain).

Key Terms
معدن (ma'din): A mineral deposit extracted from the earth; includes both metals and non-metals.
خمس (khums): One-fifth (20%) levy on spoils and certain found wealth like minerals and treasure.
ركاز (rikaz): In this context, defined by the Prophet as gold and silver created in the earth; equivalent to mines.
غنیمت (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from non-Muslims by force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the obligation on finding a meltable mineral (like gold or iron) from any land?
A) Only zakat (1/40) after one year.
B) Khums (one-fifth) is wajib immediately.
C) Nothing is due because it is mubah (ownerless).
D) Only if it is gold or silver, then zakat.

Key Takeaway
Khums (one-fifth) is wajib on all meltable minerals found in any land, based on the Quranic verse on ghanimah and the hadith of Rikaz.

Mine in One's House: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Khums
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for a mine in private property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on khums for a mine found in one's own house, explain Abu Hanifa's qiyas of part and whole, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, khums is due on a mine in one's house (Sahibayn) despite Abu Hanifa's qiyas that the part follows the whole.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that a mine found in one's own house is exempt from khums because it is a natural part of the land, and the land itself incurs no levy. His students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), disagree, relying on the general proofs that obligate khums on all mines. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh qiyas against general textual evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate in the Arabic text the views of Abu Hanifa ("falis fihi shay'") and Sahibayn ("fihi al-humus"). Note that the dispute is specific to a mine found in one's own house.
The general consensus on public lands is not disputed here.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's qiyas
Extract the analogy: the mine is juz' (part) of the land, and the land as a whole (kull) is not subject to khums. Since the part cannot oppose the whole, the mine is free. Note the exception for kanz (treasure), which is not compounded in the earth.
The illa (effective cause) is "compounded in the earth" (murakkab fiha).
3
Examine Sahibayn's dalil
The text says "li-l-itlaq ma rawayna" — due to the generality of what we narrated. This refers to the general hadith of rikaz and the ayah on ghanimah that apply to all mines regardless of location.
The exact hadith is not quoted here, but it is well-known: "In rikaz is khums."
4
Compare the reasoning for kanz
Note that both sides agree that a kanz (buried treasure) found in one's house is subject to khums. The difference from a mine is that kanz is not naturally part of the land; it is placed externally. This exception supports Abu Hanifa's qiyas — only compounded parts follow the whole.
The exception is used by Abu Hanifa to strengthen his case, but Sahibayn still apply the general rule to mines.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although the Hidayah sometimes prefers Abu Hanifa, later fatwa practice adopted Sahibayn's view due to the strength of the general evidence. The mufta bihi is that khums is wajib even in one's own house.
Tarjih authority: later Hanafi scholars like Ibn Abidin follow Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ وَجَدَ فِي دَارِهِ مَعْدِنَا فَلَيْسَ فِيهِ شَيٍّ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا فِيهِ الْحُمُسُ لِلإطْلَاقِ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَهُ أَنَّهُ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ الْأَرْضِ مُرَكَّبٌ فِيهَا وَلَا مُؤْنَةَ فِى سَائِرِ الاجْزَاءِ فَكَذَا فِى هَذَا الْجُزْءِ لَاَنَّ الْجُزء لا يُخَالِفُ الْجُمْلَةَ بِخِلَافِ الكنز لأنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُرَّكَبِ فِيهَا
ترجمہ اور اگر اپنے گھر میں معدن پائی تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس میں بھی خمس واجب ہے اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معدن زمین کے اجزاء سے زمین کے اندر مرکب ہے اور زمین کے اجزاء میں کوئی مونت اور بار نہیں ہے لہذا اس جز کے اندر بھی کوئی بار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جز اپنے کل سے مخالف نہیں ہوتا۔ برخلاف کنز ( دفینہ ) کے کیونکہ وہ زمین میں مرکب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی انسان کو اپنے گھر کے اندر سے کوئی کان دستیاب ہو گئی تو اس کان میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کوئی شمس
And if he finds a mine in his house, there is nothing due in it according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: in it is khums due to the generality of what we have narrated. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that it is from the parts of the earth, compounded in it, and there is no burden (mu'na) in the other parts, so likewise in this part, because the part does not oppose the whole, unlike a treasure (kanz), because it is not compounded in it. Translation: And if one finds a mine in his house, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, nothing is obligatory. The two (Sahibayn) said: khums is also obligatory in it due to the generality of the hadith we narrated. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that a mine is from the parts of the earth, compounded in it, and there is no burden (tax) on the other parts, so on this part also there will be no burden, because the part does not oppose the whole. Unlike a treasure (buried wealth), because it is not compounded in the earth. Explanation: The issue is that if a person finds a mine within his house, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no khums (one-fifth) is due.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a mine (ma'din) found within one's own house. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no khums or any payment is due on such a mine. His reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy): the mine is a part (juz') of the land, compounded within it. The land itself (the 'whole') is not subject to any levy merely by virtue of its parts—i.e., owning land does not incur a tax on its components. Since the part cannot be different from the whole, the mine (as part of the land) should also be free from any extra charge. This contrasts with a buried treasure (kanz), which is not a natural part of the land but externally placed, so khums applies. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They argue that the general evidence (the hadith of Rikaz and the ayah on ghanimah) applies universally to all mines, including those found in one's house. For them, the location does not change the obligation; the mine is still a mineral deposit and thus subject to khums. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn—that khums is wajib even if the mine is in one's own house. However, Abu Hanifa's view is also recorded and studied.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): A part or component; here referring to the mine as a physical part of the land.
كل (kull): The whole; here the land itself.
كنز (kanz): Buried treasure (humanly deposited), as opposed to a natural mineral deposit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a mine is found in one's own house, what is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school?
A) Nothing is wajib, following Imam Abu Hanifa.
B) Khums is wajib, following the Sahibayn.
C) Zakat (1/40) is wajib after one year.
D) Only if it is gold or silver, then khums.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, khums (1/5) is wajib on a mine found in one's own house, following the Sahibayn's view, which outweighs Abu Hanifa's qiyas due to the strength of general textual evidence.

The Ruling and Proof for Khums on Minerals (Ma'din)
Establishes ruling and proof for khums on ma'din

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khums is wajib on minerals from public land, identify the dalil (hadith and qiyas), and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Khums (one-fifth) is wajib on minerals mined from public land because they fall under rikaz and booty.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on khums for minerals extracted from public (dead) land. You will learn the primary hadith proof from the Prophet ﷺ defining rikaz, the rational extension (qiyas) to booty, and the rebuttal of the Shafi'i objection based on a broken-chain hadith. Understanding this ruling clarifies a key difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i fiqh on public finance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the exact act being ruled upon (mining minerals from public land) and the hukm level (wajib khums).
Note: khums here is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is ahad.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Read the hadith from Bayhaqi that defines rikaz as gold and silver created in the earth. Understand how this definition includes ma'din.
The hadith: 'Al-khumusu…' (the one-fifth is due). What is rikaz? Gold and silver created by God in the earth.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Apply the Hanafi usul principle: the imperative 'al-khumus' indicates obligation (wujub). Also, the definition of rikaz as God-created gold/silver matches ma'din (minerals extracted from mines).
Also note the rational proof: ma'din lands were war booty, hence one-fifth is due.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i
Identify the opposing proof (hadith of Bilal ibn al-Harith) and the Hanafi response: the hadith is munqati' (broken chain), hence unreliable.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Shafi'i may not require khums on certain ma'din; Hanafi does.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is stronger because it relies on a sound hadith and qiyas, while the opposing hadith is rejected for chain weakness.
Mufta bihi: khums is wajib on ma'din from public land for any finder (Muslim or dhimmi, free or slave, etc.).

Source Text

كتاب التركوة
الحُمُسُ قِيْلَ مَا الرّكَازُ يَارَسُولَ اللهِ؟ قَالَ الذَّهَبُ وَالْفِضَّةُ الَّذِى خَلْقَهُ اللَّهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ يَوْمَ خُلِقَتِ الْأَرْضُ ( رواه البيهقى) ابو ہریرہ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ رکاز کے اندر خمس واجب ہے کسی نے دریافت کیا کہ رسول اللہ رکاز کیا چیز ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا کہ وہ سونا اور چاندی جس کو اللہ نے اس دن زمین کے اندر پیدا فرمایا جس روز زمین پیدا کی گئی تھی ۔ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے رکاز کی تعریف کر دینے سے معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث میں رکاز سے مراد معدن ہے کیونکہ یہ تعریف معدن ہی کی کیجاتی ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ معدن کے اندر خمس واجب ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے عقلی دلیل بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ معدن کی تمام زمینیں کفار کے قبضہ میں تھیں مسلمانوں نے ان پر غلبہ پاکران کو غنیمت بنالیا ہے اور غنیمت کے مالوں میں پانچواں حصہ اللہ کا ہوتا ہے اس لئے معادن کے اندر بھی پانچواں حصہ اللہ کے لئے واجب ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف شکار کہ وہ شکار کرنے سے پہلے کسی کے قبضہ میں نہیں تھا لہذا کسی مسلمان کے پکڑنے سے وہ مال غنیمت نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مال غنیمت نہ ہوا تو شکار کے اندر خمس بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
إِلَّا إِنَّ لِلْغَائِمِينَ .. الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ معدن جس کو اللہ تعالے نے زمین کے اندر پیدا کیا ہے اگر وہ مال غنیمت ہے جیسا کہ کہا گیا ہے تو چار خمس غانمین اور مجاہدین کے ہونے چاہئیں نہ کہ پانے والے کے کیونکہ مال غنیمت کا حکم یہی ہے کہ اس کا ایک خمس اللہ اور رسول کا ہوتا ہے اور چار خمس غانمین کے ہوتے ہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ چار خمس غانمین کے واسطے اس وقت ہوتے ہیں جبکہ شئی مغنوم اور مال غنیمت پر ان کا قبضہ حقیقیہ اور حکما دونوں طرح ثابت ہو ۔ اور جب غانمین کا قبضہ حکما ثابت ہو اور حقیقہ کسی دوسرے کا قبضہ ثابت ہو۔ تو ان کے لئے چار خمس نہیں ہوتے بلکہ جسکا قبضہ حقیقہ ہوگا چار خمس اس کے لئے ہوں گے۔ حاصل یہ کہ معدن جو زمین سے برآمد ہوا ہے اس پر غانمین کا قبضہ فقط حکما ہے اور حقیقی قبضہ پانے والے کا ہے پس ہم نے حکمی قبضہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ایک خمس اللہ کے واسطے واجب کر دیا ہے جس کے حقدار یتامی اور مساکین ہیں اور حقیقی قبضہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے چار خمس پانے والے کو دیدئیے جائیں گے۔ پانے والا مسلمان ہو یا ذمی آزاد ہو یا غلام بچہ ہو یا بالغ مرد ہو یا عورت ہو حضرت امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ روایت بلال بن الحارث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث منقطع ہے اور حدیث منقطع قابل استدلال نہیں ہوتی۔
Book of Rikaz. Khums (one-fifth) is due. It was said: O Messenger of God, what is rikaz? He said: Gold and silver which God created in the earth on the day the earth was created (narrated by Bayhaqi). Abu Hurairah says that the Messenger of God said that khums is obligatory on rikaz. Someone asked: O Messenger of God, what is rikaz? He said: That gold and silver which God created in the earth on the day the earth was created. From the definition of rikaz by the Messenger of God, it became clear that in the hadith rikaz means ma'din (mine), because this definition applies to ma'din. So it is established that khums is wajib on ma'din. The author of Hidayah presented a rational proof: all lands of ma'din were in the possession of disbelievers; Muslims overcame them and made them booty. In booty, one-fifth belongs to God, so on ma'din also one-fifth is wajib for God. Unlike hunting, which before being hunted was not in anyone's possession, so when a Muslim catches it, it does not become booty, and when not booty, khums is not wajib. The phrase 'except that for the ghanimin...' is the answer to a question. The question is: ma'din which God created in the earth, if it is booty as said, then four-fifths should be for the ghanimin and mujahidin, not for the finder, because the ruling of booty is that one-fifth is for God and the Messenger, and four-fifths for the ghanimin. The answer is: four-fifths are for the ghanimin only when their possession over the captured thing is both real (haqiqiyyah) and legal (hukman). When the possession of the ghanimin is only legal and the real possession is of someone else, then four-fifths are not for them but for the one who has real possession. So, on a mine extracted from the earth, the ghanimin have only legal possession, and the real possession is for the finder. Therefore, considering the legal possession, we made one-fifth wajib for God, whose beneficiaries are orphans and poor, and considering the real possession, four-fifths will be given to the finder, whether the finder is Muslim or dhimmi, free or slave, child or adult, male or female. The response to the hadith of Bilal ibn al-Harith presented by Imam Shafi'i is that this hadith is munqati' (broken chain) and a munqati' hadith is not admissible as proof.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on rikaz. It first presents the hadith from Bayhaqi defining rikaz as gold and silver created in the earth, and then establishes that ma'din (mines) are included in the ruling of khums. The author then provides a rational proof: since mines are in conquered lands, they are like booty (ghanima) and thus one-fifth is due. A distinction is made with hunting. Then a question is answered regarding the distribution of khums between the finder and the public treasury, clarifying that legal possession gives one-fifth to the state, and real possession gives four-fifths to the finder. Finally, the hadith of Bilal ibn al-Harith, used by Shafi'i, is rejected as munqati'.

Key Terms
رِكَاز (rikaz): Treasure trove, specifically gold and silver created by God in the earth.
مَعْدِن (ma'din): Mine, a source of minerals extracted from the earth.
خُمُس (khums): One-fifth tax on rikaz and booty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi response to the hadith of Bilal ibn al-Harith used by Imam al-Shafi'i?
A) It is accepted because it is from a Companion.
B) It is rejected because the chain is broken (munqati').
C) It is reconciled through ta'wil.
D) It is considered abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Khums (one-fifth) on minerals from public land is wajib in the Hanafi school, proven by a sound hadith defining rikaz and rational analogy to booty, with the Shafi'i objection rejected due to the weak chain of their proof.

Mine Found in One's House: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on khums for a mine found in one's house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ on the obligation of khums for a mine found in one's house, and apply their respective proofs to distinguish between a mine (ma'din) and a buried treasure (kanz).

Core Idea
A mine composed in house land is exempt from khums per Abu Hanifa, not for Sahibayn.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person discovers a mine within the boundaries of his own home, does khums become due? Imam Abu Hanifa, relying on the principle that parts follow the whole, argues that since the land itself bears no tax, neither does the mine. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, appeal to the general command of the hadith on rikaz. Understanding this disagreement sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and textual interpretation in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the specific situation? A person finds a mine (ma'din) inside his own house. The dispute is whether khums (one-fifth) is wajib on this mineral wealth.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that no khums is due. His proof: the mine is a part of the earth composed in it; parts of the earth (like the house land) have no mu'nah (tax burden), so this part follows the whole: it is also free of tax. He analogizes the mine to the land itself.
This is a qiyas argument: the part (mine) shares the ruling of the whole (land).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say khums is wajib. Their proof: the hadith 'wa fi al-rikazi al-khumus' is absolute ('amm), covering all mines regardless of location, including those found in houses. No exception for private property.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim in the text but is referenced.
4
Analyze the distinction between ma'din and kanz
Abu Hanifa distinguishes a mine (composed in the earth) from a buried treasure (kanz) which is deposited but not composed. For a treasure found in the house, even Abu Hanifa agrees khums is due. This distinction is key to his reasoning.
The text also addresses a subsidiary question about tayammum with minerals, confirming that gold/silver are not of the same genus as earth despite being parts of it.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: according to Abu Hanifa, the finder keeps the entire mine's value; according to Sahibayn, he must give one-fifth to the state. The text does not specify which view is relied upon (mufta bihi).
This is an unresolved ikhtilaf within the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
