Khums on Turquoise and Mercury: Mineral Ruling and Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Ruling on khums for minerals with Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khums for turquoise and mercury, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Stones from mountains have no khums; mercury has khums in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the khums obligation on minerals extracted from mountains. Two specific substances are treated: turquoise, a gemstone, and mercury, a liquid metal. While the ruling on stones is clear from a hadith, mercury sparked a notable intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to navigate ikhtilaf within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on turquoise
Turquoise is classified as a stone (hajar); thus no khums is due, based on the explicit hadith 'La khumsa fi al-hajar'.
This is uncontested within the Hanafi school.
2
State the Hanafi position on mercury
Mercury (zaybaq) is not a stone; Abu Hanifa's later view and Imam Muhammad hold that khums is wajib. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding no khums.
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa (later) and Muhammad.
3
Identify the evidence for each
For stones, the hadith provides direct textual evidence. For mercury, there is no explicit text; the ruling is based on analogy or ijtihad, leading to ikhtilaf.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa initially held no khums on mercury, then changed to wajib. Abu Yusuf maintained the initial view; Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa's later view.
The dispute is recorded by the author of al-'Inayah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that khums is wajib on mercury, following Abu Hanifa's later opinion and Imam Muhammad.
This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah as per Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِى الْفِيرُوزَجِ الَّذِي يُوجَدُ فِي الْجِبَالِ حُمُشٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا حُمُسَ فِي الْحَجَرِ وَفِي الرِّيْبَقِ الْخُمْسُ فِي قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ اخِرًا وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ

ترجمہ اور اس فیروز میں جو پہاڑوں میں پایا جائے خمس نہیں ہے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا "لا خمس في الحجر" اور زیق میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے آخری قول میں خمس نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی قول امام محمد کا ہے ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ہے

تشریح فیروز ایک قسم کا قیمتی پتھر زیق پارہ الکل مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ فیروز سنگ سرمہ یا قوت وغیرہ جو پہاڑوں سے دستیاب ہوئے ہوں ان میں خمس واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور دلیل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان "لا حُمسَ فِی الحَجَرِ" ہے۔ اور پارہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا آخری قول وجوب خمس کا ہے۔ اور یہی قول امام محمد کا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک پارہ میں خمس وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہے صاحب عنایہ نے ایک دلچسپ حکایت تحریر کی ہے انہوں نے فرمایا کہ امام ابو یوسف سے حکایت ہے کہ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ اولاً فر مایا کرتے تھے کہ پارہ کے اندر شمس وغیرہ کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے اور میں وجوب شمس کا قائل تھا میں برابر غور کرتا رہا تو معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت امام صاحب پارہ کے اندر وجوب شمس کے قائل ہو گئے ہیں اور میں نے دیکھا کہ اس میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اب حاصل یہ ہوا کہ پارہ میں امام صاحب کا آخری قول اور ابو یوسف کا قول اول اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے یہ ہے کہ اس میں خمس واجب ہے اور ابو یوسف کا قول آخر اور امام صاحب کا قول اول یہ ہے کہ اس میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے
And there is no khums on firuzaj (turquoise) that is found in the mountains, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'No khums on stone.' And on zaybaq (mercury), khums is due in the later opinion of Abu Hanifa, and it is the opinion of Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf.

Translation: And on this firuz that is found in mountains, there is no khums, because the Prophet ﷺ said 'la khumsa fi al-hajar'. And on zaybaq, in Abu Hanifa's later opinion, there is khums, but Abu Yusuf disagrees.

Explanation: Firuz is a type of valuable stone; zaybaq is mercury. The ruling: on firuz, surma (antimony), and similar stones found in mountains, khums is not obligatory. The proof is the hadith. On mercury, Abu Hanifa's later opinion is that khums is obligatory, and this is also Muhammad's opinion. Abu Yusuf holds that no khums is due. The author of al-'Inayah narrates: Abu Yusuf said that Abu Hanifa initially said no khums on mercury, but later changed to obligation. Abu Yusuf held the initial view.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning khums on minerals found in mountains. Two items are discussed: (1) Turquoise (firuzaj) and similar stones: the ruling is that no khums is due, based on the hadith 'No khums on stone.' This is agreed upon within the Hanafi school. (2) Mercury (zaybaq): there is a difference of opinion. Abu Hanifa's later view (mufta bihi) and Imam Muhammad's view is that khums is wajib. Abu Yusuf's view is that no khums is due. The commentary explains Abu Yusuf's reasoning: he adhered to Abu Hanifa's earlier opinion and saw no basis for khums. The author of al-'Inayah relates that Abu Hanifa changed his position from no khums to khums. Thus, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that khums is wajib on mercury, following Abu Hanifa's later view and Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
الزِّيْبَق (zaybaq): Mercury, a liquid metal found in mines.
الفَيْرُوزَج (firuzaj): Turquoise, a blue gemstone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later view of Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on khums for mercury (zaybaq) found in mountains?
A) Khums is wajib
B) Khums is not wajib
C) It is makruh
D) Only zakat is due

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, stones like turquoise are exempt from khums, but mercury incurs khums as per the relied-upon view.
